# CLAUDE_TASK — Full Codebase Architectural Review

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline. Apply each task in order._


## `src\agent\action_translation.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Suggestions for Reducing P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference:**

*   **Task 1.1: src\agent\action_translation.py - `normalize_computer_use_function_call`**
    *   **Description**: For a small, fixed number of `name` values, the current `if/elif` chain is efficient. However, as the number of supported `name` values grows, this structure can lead to increased P99 latency due to sequential comparisons. Consider refactoring this into a dictionary lookup mapping `name` strings to handler functions or a pre-computed mapping for faster dispatch.
    *   **Actionable Step**: Profile `normalize_computer_use_function_call` under high load or with a significantly expanded set of action types. If latency is observed, refactor the `if/elif` chain to use a dictionary dispatch table for function name to action-creation logic.
*   **Task 1.2: src\agent\action_translation.py - `translate_computer_use_action`**
    *   **Description**: Similar to `normalize_computer_use_function_call`, this function also uses an `if/elif` chain for `action_type`. While currently efficient, future expansion could benefit from a dictionary dispatch pattern.
    *   **Actionable Step**: Profile `translate_computer_use_action`. If it becomes a P99 bottleneck with many action types, refactor to use a dictionary dispatch table for `action_type` to `AgentAction` construction logic.
*   **Task 1.3: src\agent\action_translation.py - General**
    *   **Description**: The module performs purely transformational operations (dict to dict, dict to object). These are generally CPU-bound and fast. For extreme latency requirements, ensure that the `AgentAction` and `PolicyDecision` Pydantic models (implied from imports) are optimized for creation speed (e.g., avoiding excessive validation overhead in very hot paths, though this is usually minor).
    *   **Actionable Step**: Continuously monitor and profile the entire inference pipeline, including model validation overhead, to ensure that object instantiation and data copying do not introduce unexpected P99 latency as the system scales.

**2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency:**

*   **Task 2.1: src\agent\action_translation.py - Entire Module**
    *   **Description**: All functions in this module (`_scale_grid_coord`, `_scale_grid_magnitude`, `normalize_computer_use_function_call`, `normalize_computer_use_actions`, `translate_computer_use_action`, `build_policy_decision`) are already inherently idempotent. They are pure functions: given the same input, they will always produce the same output and have no observable side effects (e.g., no external state modification, I/O, or time-dependent behavior).
    *   **Actionable Step**: No changes required. Maintain this functional, idempotent design for future additions.

**3. Suggested Agentic Features (Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines):**

*   **Task 3.1: src\agent\action_translation.py - Error Handling & Self-Healing**
    *   **Description**: Currently, missing `args` keys (e.g., `args["url"]` for `navigate`) or unsupported function calls raise Python exceptions (`KeyError`, `BackendCompatibilityError`). A truly agentic system could implement self-healing.
    *   **Actionable Step**:
        *   Modify `normalize_computer_use_function_call` and `translate_computer_use_action` to catch expected errors (e.g., `KeyError` for missing arguments). Instead of simply raising, return a special `AgentAction(action_type=ActionType.REPORT_ERROR)` or similar, containing detailed error context.
        *   Implement a downstream feedback loop to the policy/LLM. If an invalid or incomplete action is generated, the agent should `re-prompt` the policy with the error details (e.g., "The 'navigate' action requires a 'url' argument, which was missing. Please provide a complete action.").
        *   For `BackendCompatibilityError`, explore a higher-level planning component that can decompose unsupported actions into a sequence of supported primitive actions, or provide a "no-op" or "wait_for_user" action with an explanation.
*   **Task 3.2: src\agent\action_translation.py - Adaptive Behavior (Dynamic Scaling)**
    *   **Description**: `_scale_grid_coord` and `_scale_grid_magnitude` rely on static `screen_width` and `screen_height`. A robust agent should adapt to changes in the visual environment (e.g., screen resolution changes, application window resizing, multi-monitor setups).
    *   **Actionable Step**: Instead of passing `screen_width`/`screen_height` directly, consider having a system-level visual perception module that provides *current, dynamic* screen dimensions. This module could update these values on-the-fly, allowing `normalize_computer_use_function_call` to always use the most accurate dimensions for coordinate scaling. This might involve changing the signature to fetch this state implicitly or from a global/context object.
*   **Task 3.3: src\agent\action_translation.py - Post-Action Visual Verification**
    *   **Description**: The output `AgentAction` defines an intended action. A core "visual servo" principle is *closed-loop control*. After an action is dispatched, the agent should visually verify its success.
    *   **Actionable Step**: While not directly implemented in *this* translation module, ensure the `AgentAction` objects generated (e.g., `CLICK`, `TYPE`) are enriched with enough information (e.g., intended visual change, expected state after action) that a downstream execution engine can use for visual servo feedback. For example, a `TYPE` action could also include the *expected resulting text in the field* to verify. This implies adding optional fields to `AgentAction` or creating a richer `PolicyDecision` envelope.
*   **Task 3.4: src\agent\action_translation.py - Batch Action Optimization**
    *   **Description**: `normalize_computer_use_actions` produces a batch. An agentic system could re-order or optimize actions within a batch based on visual state, dependencies, or efficiency.
    *   **Actionable Step**: Implement an optional "optimizer" pass *after* `normalize_computer_use_actions` and *before* `translate_computer_use_action` (or within `translate_computer_use_action` if a batch is processed). This pass could re-sequence actions (e.g., group all "type" actions, or prioritize actions based on their immediate visual impact) or even merge semantically similar actions if the visual state permits.

**4. Flagged Violations of Operon's Invariants:**

*   **Task 4.1: src\agent\action_translation.py - `translate_computer_use_action` (ActionType.TYPE)**
    *   **Violation**: `target_element_id=action_payload.get("target_element_id")` for `ActionType.TYPE` directly violates Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant. Operon is a vision-only, zero-abstraction agent and must not rely on underlying DOM structure or element IDs. All interaction must be coordinate-based, driven by visual perception.
    *   **Actionable Step**:
        *   Remove `target_element_id` from the `AgentAction` constructor for `ActionType.TYPE`.
        *   Ensure that any `TYPE` action *always* provides `x` and `y` coordinates, even if they are optional in the `AgentAction` definition. The agent must visually determine the target location for typing. If `x` and `y` are not provided in the input, `normalize_computer_use_function_call` should raise an error or return a `WAIT_FOR_USER` action, as the `TYPE` action cannot be translated without visual coordinates.

## `src\agent\anthropic_policy.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.

1.  **Task:** Refine prompt generation for conciseness and efficiency.
    *   **Description:** Analyze the `_render_prompt` method (inherited from `GeminiPolicyService` in `src/agent/policy.py`) to identify opportunities to reduce prompt token count without sacrificing critical information. This could involve more aggressive summarization of `AgentState` or `ScreenPerception`, or dynamically pruning less relevant context based on task complexity.
    *   **Action:** Review and optimize `src/agent/policy.py:_render_prompt`'s implementation and associated prompt templates.

2.  **Task:** Implement streaming capabilities for Anthropic API responses.
    *   **Description:** Investigate if `src/clients/anthropic.py:AnthropicHttpClient.generate_policy` can be modified to support streaming partial responses from the Anthropic API. If so, update `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` and `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:_parse_output` to process these streams incrementally, potentially allowing for early parsing and action execution to reduce perceived latency.
    *   **Action:**
        *   Modify `src/clients/anthropic.py:AnthropicHttpClient.generate_policy` to support response streaming.
        *   Update `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` and `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:_parse_output` to consume and incrementally parse streaming outputs.

3.  **Task:** Optimize underlying HTTP client for network efficiency.
    *   **Description:** Ensure that `src/clients/anthropic.py:AnthropicHttpClient` utilizes connection pooling, persistent HTTP connections, and appropriate TCP settings to minimize handshake overhead and improve network throughput for successive requests to the Anthropic API.
    *   **Action:** Review and configure `src/clients/anthropic.py:AnthropicHttpClient`'s underlying HTTP client for optimal connection management.

4.  **Task:** Explore speculative decoding or early exit mechanisms (future).
    *   **Description:** Evaluate the feasibility of using a smaller, faster local model or heuristic to generate and validate a candidate policy prefix from an initial subset of the Anthropic model's output. If a high-confidence simple action is identified early, it could be executed speculatively or without waiting for the full LLM response, reducing tail latency for straightforward tasks.
    *   **Action:** (Research & Design) Propose a technical design for speculative execution integrated into `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` and `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:_parse_output`.

#### 2. Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.

1.  **Task:** Verify idempotency of debug artifact writing.
    *   **Description:** Confirm that the `bg_writer.enqueue` calls in `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` consistently overwrite existing files at the deterministic artifact paths when called multiple times with identical `state` and `perception` inputs. This ensures the artifact storage remains idempotent from a functional perspective.
    *   **Action:** Review the implementation of `src/store/background_writer.py:enqueue` to confirm its file overwrite behavior.

2.  **Task:** Document LLM non-determinism for policy generation.
    *   **Description:** Add a docstring or inline comment to `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` clarifying that while internal state updates and artifact writing are designed to be idempotent, the `PolicyDecision` returned may not be strictly idempotent if the underlying Anthropic LLM exhibits non-deterministic behavior for identical prompts. This sets clear expectations for consumers of the service.
    *   **Action:** Add a clarifying comment or docstring to `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action`.

#### 3. Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.

1.  **Task:** Implement self-correction for `PolicyDecision` parsing failures.
    *   **Description:** Modify `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action` to handle errors from `_parse_output` (which calls `src/agent/policy.py:parse_policy_output`). Instead of immediately raising, implement a retry mechanism that constructs a new prompt. This revised prompt should append the parsing error message and potentially the expected `PolicyDecision` Pydantic schema to the original prompt, instructing Anthropic to correct its output format in the subsequent attempt.
    *   **Action:** Implement a retry loop with dynamic prompt modification around the `_parse_output` call in `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action`.

2.  **Task:** Implement intelligent retry and dynamic fallback for Anthropic client errors.
    *   **Description:** Enhance `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action`'s handling of `AnthropicClientError`. Instead of a simple re-raise, implement:
        *   Configurable exponential backoff retries with a maximum number of attempts.
        *   A fallback mechanism, such as:
            *   Temporarily switching to a different, potentially simpler, LLM service (e.g., the base `GeminiPolicyService` if its client is available and suitable for simpler tasks).
            *   Leveraging a cached previous successful policy for the same or similar `AgentState`.
            *   Invoking a hardcoded heuristic or a local, fast model for critical, simple actions.
    *   **Action:** Implement advanced error handling, retries, and fallback logic for `AnthropicClientError` in `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action`.

3.  **Task:** Introduce adaptive prompting based on observed policy outcomes.
    *   **Description:** Develop a feedback loop where the success or failure of `PolicyDecision` executions is logged and used to inform future prompt generation. The `_render_prompt` method (in `src/agent/policy.py`) could dynamically adjust prompt instructions, add more specific examples, or highlight common failure modes based on past performance for similar tasks or UI patterns.
    *   **Action:** Design and implement a system to collect execution feedback and integrate it into `src/agent/policy.py:_render_prompt`'s logic for dynamic prompt adaptation.

4.  **Task:** Implement a fast, local pre-validation step for generated policies.
    *   **Description:** After `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:_parse_output` returns a `PolicyDecision`, introduce a lightweight, local validation step within `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:choose_action`. This validation would use simple heuristics or a small, fast model to check for obvious illogical or impossible actions (e.g., click coordinates outside screen bounds, attempting to type into a non-input field given `ScreenPerception` details). If the policy fails pre-validation, trigger a refinement loop (similar to handling parsing failures).
    *   **Action:** Implement a new private method `_validate_policy_decision` in `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py` and integrate its call into `choose_action` before returning the decision.

#### 4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.

1.  **Task:** Enforce "no DOM/selectors" at the `PolicyDecision` interface.
    *   **Description:** Ensure that the `src/models/policy.py:PolicyDecision` model (which `src/agent/anthropic_policy.py:_parse_output` produces) strictly prevents the representation of actions based on DOM selectors, abstract UI element IDs, or any other non-visual, non-coordinate-based identifiers. Actions must solely rely on vision-based parameters (e.g., pixel coordinates, bounding boxes, textual content, visual patterns).
    *   **Action:** Review the Pydantic schema and validation logic within `src/models/policy.py:PolicyDecision` and the parsing logic in `src/agent/policy.py:parse_policy_output` to guarantee compliance. Add explicit validation if not already present.

2.  **Task:** Verify `_render_prompt` adheres to "no DOM/selectors" principle.
    *   **Description:** Review the prompt templates and logic used by `src/agent/policy.py:_render_prompt` to ensure it does not generate prompts that instruct the LLM to output or reason about DOM-like structures, abstract UI trees, or anything beyond the visual and directly observed state from `ScreenPerception`. The prompt must exclusively guide the LLM towards vision-only action planning.
    *   **Action:** Thoroughly review the prompt templates and rendering logic in `src/agent/policy.py:_render_prompt` to confirm strict adherence to vision-only instructions.

3.  **Note on Atomic Focus+Type and Visual Servo:**
    *   **Description:** This module, `AnthropicPolicyService`, is responsible for *planning* the next action (`PolicyDecision`), not executing it. The invariants "atomic focus+type" and "visual servo" apply primarily to the *execution engine* that consumes the `PolicyDecision`. The `ScreenPerception` input and `PolicyDecision` output are compatible with these invariants, assuming the `PolicyDecision` model correctly encodes atomic, visual-servo-compatible actions. There are no direct violations within this module.
    *   **Action:** (No action required in this module, but acknowledge the dependency on other components.)

## `src\agent\backend.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task 1.1: Enhance `perceive` with explicit focus hints.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\backend.py`
        *   **Function:** `perceive`
        *   **Action:** Modify the `perceive` signature to accept an optional parameter, e.g., `perception_focus_hints: List[PerceptionFocusHint] | None = None`. This allows the `AgentState` or previous `PolicyDecision` to guide the perception model on what specific areas or features to prioritize, potentially speeding up inference by reducing the scope of visual processing.
        *   **Context:** `PerceptionFocusHint` would be a new model, e.g., `dataclass` defining a region of interest or a semantic object to look for, derived from previous visual context.
    *   **Task 1.2: Introduce early-exit mechanism for `perceive` when no significant change is detected.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\backend.py`
        *   **Function:** `perceive`
        *   **Action:** Consider modifying `ScreenPerception` to include an `is_significant_change: bool` flag or a `similarity_score: float` against the previous frame. If the implementation detects minimal visual change, it could return a pre-computed or greatly simplified `ScreenPerception` quickly, avoiding full re-inference. This requires ensuring `AgentState` can carry enough context for such a comparison.
    *   **Task 1.3: Enable pipelined action prediction.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py` (impacts `choose_action` return type)
        *   **Function:** `PolicyDecision` (return type of `choose_action`)
        *   **Action:** Augment `PolicyDecision` to include an optional `predicted_next_perception_focus: List[PerceptionFocusHint] | None`. This allows the agent to suggest what the *next* perception cycle should focus on *before* the current action is even executed, facilitating speculative perception and reducing latency in a visual servo loop.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task 2.1: Make `add_advisory_hints` idempotent.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\backend.py`
        *   **Function:** `add_advisory_hints`
        *   **Action:** Modify the internal logic (or guide implementation) for `add_advisory_hints` to only add hints that are not already present in the current set of advisory hints, especially when considering `source` and `run_id`. This ensures that calling the method multiple times with the same hints from the same source doesn't result in a growing list of duplicates. For example, hints could be stored in a `set` keyed by `(source, hint_content)`.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **Task 3.1: Enhance `PolicyDecision` for self-healing and adaptation.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py` (impacts `choose_action` return type)
        *   **Function:** `PolicyDecision`
        *   **Action:** Augment `PolicyDecision` to include:
            *   `confidence_score: float`: A numerical value indicating the agent's certainty about the chosen action.
            *   `contingency_actions: List[PolicyDecision] | None`: An ordered list of alternative actions that could be attempted if the primary action fails or its `confidence_score` is low, enabling multi-step self-healing.
            *   `expected_outcome_description: str | None`: A short description of the visual or state changes expected after the action, used by a monitor or subsequent perception cycle to validate success.
    *   **Task 3.2: Introduce a self-reflection mechanism via `AgentState` and advisory hints.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (impacts `AgentState`) and `src\agent\backend.py` (for `add_advisory_hints` usage)
        *   **Function:** `AgentState` and `add_advisory_hints`
        *   **Action:** Design `AgentState` to store a structured history of `(PolicyDecision, actual_outcome, perceived_environment_change)` tuples. The `AgentBackend` implementation should be guided to leverage this history to internally call `self.add_advisory_hints()` with self-generated feedback (e.g., "avoid region X after previous failure," "prioritize element Y for similar tasks"). This enables the agent to learn and adapt its own operational strategy over time, beyond externally provided hints.
    *   **Task 3.3: Implement proactive learning feedback through debug artifacts.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\logs.py` (impacts `latest_debug_artifacts` return type)
        *   **Function:** `ModelDebugArtifacts` (return type of `latest_debug_artifacts`)
        *   **Action:** Ensure `ModelDebugArtifacts` can include structured representations of model uncertainties, misclassifications, or unexpected perception outputs. The agent's orchestrator or a dedicated learning component should then consume these artifacts to automatically refine the perception or policy models, effectively closing a learning loop for continuous improvement and self-optimization.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Task 4.1: Enforce "No DOM/selectors" invariant for `ScreenPerception`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\perception.py`
        *   **Function:** `ScreenPerception`
        *   **Action:** Add explicit documentation and, if possible, structural constraints (e.g., via Pydantic model validation if applicable) to `ScreenPerception` to ensure it *strictly* describes elements and relationships based on visual features (bounding boxes, pixel clusters, OCR text, color patterns, semantic regions derived from visual models) and contains *no* references to DOM elements, accessibility trees, CSS selectors, XPath, or other non-visual, abstract UI identifiers.
    *   **Task 4.2: Enforce "Atomic focus+type" invariant for `PolicyDecision`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function:** `PolicyDecision`
        *   **Action:** Add explicit documentation and structural constraints to `PolicyDecision` to ensure actions are represented as low-level, direct input operations (e.g., `click(x: int, y: int)`, `type_text(text: str)`, `scroll(direction: str, amount: int)`, `wait(duration: float)`) that directly interact with the screen. It *must not* include high-level actions that imply or depend on DOM elements, selectors (e.g., `click_button_by_id('submit')`), or other abstractions not derivable from pure vision.
    *   **Task 4.3: Enforce "Visual Servo" and "No DOM/selectors" invariants for `advisory_hints`.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\backend.py`
        *   **Function:** `add_advisory_hints`
        *   **Action:** Add explicit documentation or validation guidance for the `hints: list[str]` parameter. These strings *must* exclusively describe visual patterns, semantic concepts derived from vision, or high-level goals/strategies (e.g., "look for a green button", "expect a text field to appear", "navigate to login page"). They *must not* contain DOM selectors, element IDs, or any other identifiers that violate the vision-only, zero-abstraction principle.

## `src\agent\benchmark.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

    *   **src\agent\benchmark.py:_build_loop**:
        *   **Task**: Refactor `_build_loop` to allow for reuse of `GeminiHttpClient` and potentially `DesktopExecutor` across multiple benchmark tasks within a suite. Currently, a new instance of `GeminiHttpClient` and `DesktopExecutor` is created for *each task* in `run_benchmark_suite`, leading to unnecessary setup overhead.
        *   **Suggestion**: Implement a `ServiceFactory` or a dependency injection pattern that manages the lifecycle of shared, long-lived resources, allowing `run_benchmark_suite` to pass already initialized clients/executors to the `AgentLoop` builder. This amortizes startup costs.
    *   **src\agent\benchmark.py:run_benchmark_suite**:
        *   **Task**: Consider running `generate_run_metrics`, `write_run_metrics`, `generate_suite_summary`, `write_suite_summary`, and markdown rendering operations asynchronously or in a separate thread/process.
        *   **Suggestion**: These operations are post-run analytics and file I/O. Moving them off the main execution path will prevent them from adding to the critical path latency for subsequent task initialization or, if relevant, real-time feedback (though for benchmarks, this is less critical than for live inference). Use `asyncio.to_thread` or a dedicated `ThreadPoolExecutor`.
    *   **src\agent\loop.py:AgentLoop.run_live_benchmark (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Implement warm-up routines for `GeminiPerceptionService` and `GeminiPolicyService` if the underlying models or connections benefit from initial requests.
        *   **Suggestion**: During `_build_loop`, perform a lightweight, non-blocking "ping" or dummy inference call to the Gemini services to ensure connections are established and models are loaded into memory before the actual benchmark starts.
    *   **src\clients\gemini.py:GeminiHttpClient (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Ensure the `GeminiHttpClient` uses persistent connections and connection pooling efficiently.
        *   **Suggestion**: Verify `aiohttp` or similar underlying HTTP client settings are optimized for long-lived connections, e.g., appropriate `timeout` and `limit` parameters for the `ClientSession`.

2.  **Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

    *   **src\store\run_store.py:FileBackedRunStore & src\store\memory.py:FileBackedMemoryStore (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Implement atomic file writes for `FileBackedRunStore` and `FileBackedMemoryStore`.
        *   **Suggestion**: When writing to files, write to a temporary file first, then atomically rename it to the final destination. This prevents partial or corrupted files if the process crashes during a write operation, ensuring that read operations will always get a consistent (even if slightly older) state.
    *   **src\agent\benchmark.py:write_run_metrics & src\agent\benchmark.py:write_suite_summary**:
        *   **Task**: Enhance file writing functions to provide better versioning or appending options, especially for summary data.
        *   **Suggestion**: Instead of directly overwriting `benchmark_suite_summary.json` and `.md`, consider:
            1.  Including a timestamp or a unique run ID in the filename (e.g., `benchmark_suite_summary_20231027-103000.json`).
            2.  Maintaining an index file that points to the latest summary.
            3.  Appending to an aggregate log for metrics if historical tracking is desired, rather than overwriting.
            This ensures that re-running the benchmark suite is idempotent in the sense that previous results are preserved or explicitly versioned, rather than simply replaced.
    *   **src\agent\benchmark.py:run_benchmark_suite**:
        *   **Task**: For each task, ensure that the `root_dir` for file-backed stores is uniquely identified per run instance, or that cleanup/reset logic for shared stores is robust.
        *   **Suggestion**: The current approach of recreating `FileBackedRunStore` and `FileBackedMemoryStore` per task instance (via `_build_loop`) ensures isolation and thus a form of idempotency for each task's internal state. Ensure that if `root_dir` is ever made shared across runs, explicit partitioning or versioning within that directory is enforced to avoid cross-task data corruption.

3.  **Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **src\agent\recovery.py:RuleBasedRecoveryManager (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Evolve `RuleBasedRecoveryManager` into a learning-based adaptive recovery system.
        *   **Suggestion**: Instead of fixed rules, implement a system that uses Reinforcement Learning or a heuristic search to explore recovery actions when a failure condition is met. This could involve:
            *   Learning which recovery actions (e.g., re-perceive, scroll, zoom out, click "back") are most effective for specific failure types or visual contexts.
            *   Maintaining a "playbook" of successful recovery sequences that can be recalled and adapted.
            *   Integrating a confidence score: if recovery efforts consistently fail, the agent should escalate to a higher-level planning phase or seek human assistance.
    *   **src\agent\verifier.py:DeterministicVerifierService (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Enhance `DeterministicVerifierService` with probabilistic or contextual verification.
        *   **Suggestion**: Instead of relying solely on an `expected_completion_signal`, allow the verifier to use a multimodal model to infer task completion based on the overall visual state and historical context, even if the exact signal is absent. This enables robustness to minor variations in "success" screens or alternative completion paths. The verifier could also trigger recovery if confidence in completion is low but no explicit failure occurred.
    *   **src\agent\policy_coordinator.py:PolicyCoordinator & src\store\memory.py:FileBackedMemoryStore (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Implement a "skill library" or long-term memory for `PolicyCoordinator` using the `memory_store`.
        *   **Suggestion**: Allow the agent to abstract and store successful sequences of actions (skills) for common sub-goals (e.g., "login," "navigate to settings page"). When a new task requires a known sub-goal, the agent can recall and adapt the learned skill, rather than generating a new policy from scratch. This would involve embedding the visual context of the skill's applicability and its corresponding action sequence.
    *   **src\agent\loop.py:AgentLoop (implicit dependency)**:
        *   **Task**: Introduce a real-time self-monitoring and adaptation mechanism.
        *   **Suggestion**: Monitor internal metrics like perception latency, policy generation time, and executor success rate *during* a live run. If significant degradation is detected (e.g., P99 latency spikes), the agent could autonomously adapt its strategy, such as simplifying its perception queries, reducing the planning horizon, or attempting a soft reset of internal components.

4.  **Violations of Operon's Invariants**

    *   **No direct violations in `src\agent\benchmark.py`**:
        *   **Flag**: The `src\agent\benchmark.py` module itself does not directly contain logic for parsing DOM, using selectors, or abstracting away atomic focus/type. It relies on other modules to uphold these invariants.
        *   **Recommendation**: Ensure rigorous code reviews and static analysis are in place for `src\executor\desktop.py`, `src\agent\perception.py`, and `src\agent\policy.py` to confirm they strictly adhere to:
            *   **No DOM/selectors**: All interactions and perceptions must be based solely on raw pixel data, OCR, and visual cues, not HTML structure or accessibility trees.
            *   **Atomic focus+type**: Actions should be direct, low-level desktop interactions (e.g., pixel-precise mouse clicks, keyboard events) derived from visual perception, without relying on high-level browser APIs that abstract these actions.
            *   **Visual servo**: The `AgentLoop` structure already supports this by continuously looping capture-perceive-policy-execute. The implementation of each service must ensure low-latency feedback and processing to make this loop effective.

---

## `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference

*   **TASK**: **Improve `_build_user_content` and `_build_function_response_content` for asynchronous image I/O.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_build_user_content`, `_build_function_response_content`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The `image_path.read_bytes()` call in `_build_user_content` (and indirectly in `_build_function_response_content` if `client.build_function_response_content` reads the screenshot) is a blocking file system operation. For larger screenshots, this can add significant latency.
    *   **ACTION**: Replace `Path.read_bytes()` with an asynchronous file I/O equivalent (e.g., using `aiofiles` if the runtime supports it, or passing an `AsyncPath` object). Alternatively, investigate if `GeminiComputerUseClient` can directly accept an image path/URL or stream instead of a base64-encoded string, offloading the encoding.

*   **TASK**: **Evaluate and optimize `browser_runtime.get_current_url()` latency.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_run_turn`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The `await self.browser_runtime.get_current_url()` call involves inter-process communication or I/O, which can introduce latency.
    *   **ACTION**: Measure the P99 latency of `get_current_url()`. If significant, explore optimizations within the `browser_runtime` (e.g., caching the URL for a short period, pushing updates from the browser side, or making it truly non-blocking).

*   **TASK**: **Explore tiered model inference or early exit strategies in `_run_with_retry`.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_run_with_retry`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The current retry mechanism performs a full, potentially slow, LLM inference, then *another* full inference if the first isn't satisfactory. This serializes two potentially high-latency operations.
    *   **ACTION**: Investigate if `GeminiComputerUseClient` could support a "fast path" or "low-fidelity" inference that returns a preliminary response quickly, allowing an early exit or speculative action, while a "high-fidelity" inference runs in the background. Or, consider if the initial prompt can be designed to elicit "less confident but faster" responses, with the retry only triggered if more certainty is needed.

### 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

*   **TASK**: **Ensure idempotency of `_ConversationState` updates in `_run_turn`.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_run_turn`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: In `_run_turn`, `conversation.contents.append(function_response)` occurs *before* `await self.client.generate_turn()`. If `generate_turn` fails and `_run_turn` is retried *independently* (not by `_run_with_retry` which handles the conversation state carefully for its own retry), the same `function_response` could be appended multiple times for the same pending actions, leading to a corrupted conversation history.
    *   **ACTION**: Modify `_run_turn` to only append the `function_response` to `conversation.contents` *after* a successful `generate_turn` call, ensuring that the state update is atomic with the external inference. If `function_response` must be included in the request, ensure it's not permanently persisted in `conversation.contents` until the LLM response is received and processed successfully.

### 3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines

*   **TASK**: **Implement adaptive model parameter tuning based on observed performance and state.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_render_prompt`, `_run_with_retry`, `_run_turn`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The agent currently uses a fixed retry suffix. More sophisticated adaptation could significantly improve robustness.
    *   **ACTION**: Introduce logic to dynamically adjust `GeminiComputerUseClient` parameters (e.g., temperature, top_p, top_k) or vary the prompt structure in `_render_prompt` based on:
        *   `state.retry_counts`: For high retry counts, increase exploration (higher temperature) or provide more explicit, step-by-step guidance.
        *   `response_payload.confidence` (from `_needs_stronger_retry`): If confidence is persistently low, try a more cautious or descriptive prompt.
        *   `ScreenPerception.page_hint`: Use different strategies for `PageHint.LOGIN_PAGE` vs. `PageHint.PRODUCT_LISTING`.

*   **TASK**: **Develop a self-reflection and root cause analysis mechanism for failures.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_run_with_retry`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: Current error handling primarily results in `BackendCompatibilityError` or re-trying with a suffix. A true agent should try to understand *why* it failed.
    *   **ACTION**: When a `GeminiComputerUseError`, `BackendCompatibilityError`, or repeated `_needs_stronger_retry` occurs, trigger a specialized "diagnostic mode." In this mode, the agent could:
        *   Generate a new internal sub-goal to "diagnose browser state" (e.g., take a more detailed screenshot, check network status via `browser_runtime`).
        *   Formulate a prompt specifically for the LLM to identify the likely cause of the previous failure based on `state.action_history` and `state.observation_history`.
        *   Suggest meta-actions like "refresh page," "go back," or "search for alternative methods."

*   **TASK**: **Introduce proactive information-seeking behaviors.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `perceive`, `_render_prompt`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The agent typically acts only after receiving a perception and decision. Proactive exploration can prevent errors.
    *   **ACTION**: Implement a "scan" phase or heuristic check in `perceive`. If `ScreenPerception.page_hint` is `PageHint.UNKNOWN`, or if the screen visual complexity is high, or if prior actions failed repeatedly on similar pages, `_render_prompt` could include explicit guidance to the LLM to first perform low-risk exploratory actions like `hover_at`, `scroll_at`, or `examine_elements` to gather more context before attempting a direct interaction. This could populate `_advisory_hints` with pre-computed observations.

*   **TASK**: **Integrate a persistent, long-term memory system via `_advisory_hints`.**
    *   **FILE**: `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `add_advisory_hints`, `_render_prompt`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: `_advisory_hints` is a temporary mechanism. A richer memory allows the agent to learn and adapt across sessions or tasks.
    *   **ACTION**: Develop an external long-term memory component that can feed into `add_advisory_hints`. This memory could store:
        *   Successful navigation paths for specific websites.
        *   Known problematic UI elements or interaction patterns.
        *   Common error resolutions for certain domains.
        *   Learned patterns from multiple Operon agents operating in similar environments. The `source` parameter in `add_advisory_hints` could be used to differentiate between real-time, short-term hints and long-term, memory-derived guidance.

### 4. Violations of Operon's Invariants

*   **NO VIOLATIONS IDENTIFIED**: The module `src\agent\browser_computer_use.py` appears to adhere to Operon's core invariants.
    *   There is no direct use of DOM/selectors. The module processes visual `ScreenPerception` outputs from the model.
    *   Actions (`PolicyDecision`) are built from high-level function calls, implying atomic actions as per the invariant.
    *   The entire process is driven by `screenshot: CaptureFrame` in `perceive`, indicating a visual servo loop.

## `src\agent\browser_json.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task 1.1: Implement a Perception Result Cache.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py` (parent of `BrowserJsonBackend`)
        *   **Function:** `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.perceive(self, visual_input: Any, context: Any) -> Dict`
        *   **Action:** Introduce an in-memory or Redis-backed cache to store recent perception outputs (e.g., identified UI elements, their locations, states) based on the visual input hash and context. Before invoking `GeminiClient` for perception, check the cache. Implement a time-to-live (TTL) appropriate for dynamic UI.
    *   **Task 1.2: Implement Policy Decision Speculation.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py` (parent of `BrowserJsonBackend`)
        *   **Function:** `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.decide_policy(self, perception_output: Dict, goal: Any) -> Any`
        *   **Action:** Based on frequently observed perception-action pairs or common workflows, pre-compute or speculatively generate the most probable next action(s). If the actual perception matches a speculated input, use the pre-computed policy, bypassing a `GeminiClient` call.
    *   **Task 1.3: Optimize Prompt Size and Structure.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py` (and potentially `src\clients\gemini.py`)
        *   **Function:** `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService._construct_prompt(self, ...)` (or similar prompt generation logic)
        *   **Action:** Implement advanced prompt compression techniques (e.g., summarization, intelligent filtering of visual data, removing redundant context) to minimize token count for `GeminiClient` requests without losing critical information. Analyze prompt effectiveness for faster inference.
    *   **Task 1.4: Investigate Concurrent Perception and Policy Evaluation.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py`
        *   **Function:** `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.execute_step(self, ...)` (or similar high-level method)
        *   **Action:** Analyze if subsequent perception steps can be initiated while the current policy decision is being formulated, or if multiple policy options can be evaluated in parallel if `GeminiClient` supports concurrent calls, allowing faster selection of the optimal action.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task 2.1: Implement Visual Confirmation for Actions.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\browser_json.py`
        *   **Function:** Add a new method `BrowserJsonBackend.execute_action_and_confirm(self, action: Dict, expected_visual_state: Dict) -> bool`
        *   **Action:** Modify all action execution paths within `BrowserJsonBackend` to include a post-action visual perception step. The agent must visually confirm that the UI transitioned to the `expected_visual_state` after performing an action (e.g., a click resulted in a button appearing pressed, or a new page loaded). If confirmation fails, the action should be retried or flagged for re-planning.
    *   **Task 2.2: Ensure All Actions are State-Conditional.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py` (and executed in `src\agent\browser_json.py`)
        *   **Function:** `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.decide_policy(...)`, `BrowserJsonBackend.execute_action(...)`
        *   **Action:** The policy generated by `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService` and executed by `BrowserJsonBackend` must explicitly include preconditions based on the *current observed visual state*. For example, "click button X" should become "click button X *if button X is visually present and enabled*." This prevents erroneous actions on an unexpected UI state.
    *   **Task 2.3: Introduce Action Request Identifiers.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\browser_json.py` (and communication layer to browser)
        *   **Function:** `BrowserJsonBackend.send_action_to_browser(self, action_id: str, action_payload: Dict)`
        *   **Action:** Assign a unique, idempotent ID to each action request sent to the underlying browser execution layer. This allows the backend to safely retry communication failures or detect duplicate requests without unintended side effects on the browser state.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **Task 3.1: Implement Dynamic Goal-Driven Re-planning.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py`
        *   **Function:** Add a new method `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.replan(self, current_visual_state: Any, original_goal: Any, failure_reason: Any) -> List[Dict]`
        *   **Action:** When an action fails or the visual state deviates unexpectedly, the agent should invoke a re-planning mechanism. Instead of simple retries, `GeminiClient` should be prompted with the current visual state, the original high-level goal, and the failure context to generate a *new, alternative sequence of actions* to achieve the goal. This moves beyond fixed paths to adaptive problem-solving.
    *   **Task 3.2: Develop a Contextual Memory and Learning System.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py`
        *   **Function:** Modify `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService.__init__` to include a memory store, and add `_update_memory(self, ...)` and `_retrieve_memory(self, ...)` methods.
        *   **Action:** Implement a system to store and retrieve past successful and failed interaction sequences, associated visual contexts, and `GeminiClient` responses. This memory should inform future perception and policy decisions (e.g., "I encountered this error pattern before, here's how I resolved it"). This allows the agent to learn and improve its performance over time.
    *   **Task 3.3: Implement Adaptive Prompt Generation based on Performance.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\combined.py`
        *   **Function:** Modify `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService._construct_prompt(self, ...)`
        *   **Action:** Instead of loading static prompts from `prompt_path`, dynamically adjust prompt parameters, examples, or instructions for `GeminiClient` based on historical success rates or observed ambiguity in `GeminiClient` responses. This allows the agent to "tune" its LLM interaction for better accuracy and efficiency in different contexts.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Flag 4.1: Potential DOM/Selectors Access (Violation Risk).**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\browser_json.py`
        *   **Observation:** The class name `BrowserJsonBackend` suggests interaction with a browser. There's an inherent risk that the underlying browser interaction layer might directly or indirectly use DOM (Document Object Model) elements or CSS selectors for identifying/manipulating UI elements.
        *   **Action:** **URGENT:** Verify that all browser interaction primitives used by `BrowserJsonBackend` strictly operate on pixel coordinates, visual regions, or accessibility metadata that *does not expose or rely on DOM structure*. Any `WebElement` object, `selector` string, or similar API usage is a critical violation. Define a strict interface for `BrowserJsonBackend` that only accepts visual-derived targets (e.g., `(x, y)` coordinates, bounding boxes, perceived semantic labels from vision) and returns only visual-derived feedback.
    *   **Flag 4.2: Atomic Focus+Type Enforcement.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\browser_json.py`
        *   **Function:** Add a new method `BrowserJsonBackend.atomic_focus_and_type(self, target_coords: Tuple[int, int], text: str)`
        *   **Action:** Ensure that the policy generated by `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService` and executed by `BrowserJsonBackend` treats the act of bringing an input element into focus and then typing into it as a single, indivisible operation. The `BrowserJsonBackend` must implement this as a robust, single-step execution, guarding against interruptions or partial inputs. If a visual confirmation of the typed text doesn't match, the entire operation must be considered failed.
    *   **Flag 4.3: Visual Servo Integration Requirement.**
        *   **File:** `src\agent\browser_json.py`
        *   **Function:** Modify `BrowserJsonBackend.move_mouse(self, target_visual_feature: Any)` and `BrowserJsonBackend.scroll_to_visual_region(self, target_region: Any)`
        *   **Action:** Any action involving continuous movement (mouse cursor, scrolling, drag-and-drop) must be implemented using a closed-loop visual servo system. The `CombinedPerceptionPolicyService` should output a desired *visual target* (e.g., "center of the button 'Submit'", "the bottom edge of the scrollbar") rather than static coordinates. `BrowserJsonBackend` must then continuously adjust its movement based on real-time visual feedback to home in on and maintain alignment with that target, adapting to slight UI shifts or animations.

## `src\agent\capture.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Replace the fixed `asyncio.sleep(0.5)` with a dynamic, visually-driven wait mechanism after `focus_window`. Instead of sleeping for a predetermined duration, implement a loop that polls `self.executor.capture()` until `frame.visual_velocity` consistently falls below `_VELOCITY_WARN_THRESHOLD` for a specified number of consecutive frames (e.g., 2-3 frames), or until a maximum timeout is reached. This ensures the agent proceeds only when the screen is visually stable, eliminating unnecessary waits and reducing P99 latency caused by waiting for a fixed, often over-estimated, duration.
    **Action**: Modify the initial focus block.

2.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Decouple the file persistence (`shutil.move`) from the critical path of returning the `CaptureFrame`. After obtaining the `frame` from `self.executor.capture()`, immediately return a copy of the `CaptureFrame` with a placeholder or original temporary `artifact_path`. Spawn a separate, non-blocking asynchronous task (e.g., using `asyncio.create_task` or a dedicated background worker) to perform the `shutil.move` operation. This allows downstream perception and inference to begin without waiting for disk I/O, significantly reducing P99 latency for the core loop.
    **Action**: Refactor file movement to be a background task.

3.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Investigate and implement a mechanism for `self.executor.capture()` to write the screenshot directly to the `planned_path` or a temporary file within the target `planned_path.parent` directory. This would eliminate the need for a separate `shutil.move` operation post-capture, reducing redundant I/O and further lowering latency.
    **Action**: Coordinate with `Executor` implementation to adjust its capture output path.

### Structural Idempotency

4.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Enhance the file persistence logic to be robust against retries and interruptions. Instead of `shutil.move`, which is not inherently idempotent across crashes if the source path might be reused or disappear, consider an "atomic write and replace" pattern. If the executor writes to a temporary location, `ScreenCaptureService` should then perform an atomic `os.replace` (on POSIX) or similar operation from the temporary file to the `planned_path`. This ensures that `planned_path` either contains the complete, correct frame or nothing, regardless of how many times the operation is attempted or if it's interrupted. The existing `if Path(frame.artifact_path) != planned_path:` check is a good start, but the final write needs to be atomic.
    **Action**: Refactor file movement using `os.replace` for atomic updates.

5.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Re-evaluate the condition for `focus_window` (`if state.step_count == 0`). While `focus_window` should be atomic, its invocation condition should be more robust. If a system restart occurs or an unhandled error prevents subsequent `focus_window` calls, the agent might never regain focus. Consider making `focus_window` callable idempotently (i.e., multiple calls have no side effects beyond the first successful one) and potentially invoking it if visual feedback (e.g., `visual_velocity`, or a higher-level state check) indicates the window is not in the desired state, even if `state.step_count > 0`.
    **Action**: Modify the `focus_window` invocation logic to be more resilient and potentially repeatable.

### Agentic Features

6.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Implement the adaptive "wait for visual stability" mechanism detailed in Task 1.1 as a core agentic feature. This moves beyond a simple warning threshold to active visual feedback looping. If stability isn't achieved after a configurable maximum timeout, raise an `InstabilityError` or trigger a specific recovery workflow.
    **Action**: Implement the polling loop for `visual_velocity` as described in Task 1.1.

7.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Description**: Explicitly leverage the "3-frame burst" capability mentioned in the docstring (`The executor returns a 3-frame burst`). Modify `executor.capture()` to return a list of `CaptureFrame` objects (or a new `CaptureBurst` model). `ScreenCaptureService` should then analyze this burst (e.g., compare visual velocities, identify the most stable frame, or perform motion analysis) to select the optimal frame for downstream inference. This enhances the perception stage with temporal consistency, making it more robust against transient visual noise or ongoing animations.
    **Action**: Refactor `capture()` to handle and process a burst of frames from the executor.

8.  **Task**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService`
    **Description**: Introduce a self-healing mechanism for persistent visual instability. If the adaptive waiting mechanism (Task 6) consistently fails to achieve stability after multiple attempts or within a cumulative timeout, trigger a higher-level recovery action. This could include, for example, sending a signal to restart the `Executor` (e.g., browser process), logging a critical incident for human intervention, or attempting to re-focus the window multiple times with increasing backoff delays.
    **Action**: Define and implement an `InstabilityError` and corresponding retry/recovery logic within or around `ScreenCaptureService`.

### Violations of Operon's Invariants

9.  **Flag**: `src\agent\capture.py - ScreenCaptureService.capture`
    **Violation**: The `asyncio.sleep(0.5)` call within the `if state.step_count == 0` block directly violates the "visual servo" invariant. Operon is a vision-only agent that operates based on real-time visual feedback. Introducing an arbitrary, fixed delay contradicts the principle of reacting dynamically to the visual state, potentially causing the agent to wait longer than necessary or act before the screen is truly stable.
    **Action**: Remove `asyncio.sleep(0.5)` and replace it with the adaptive, visually-driven stability check outlined in Task 1.1 and Task 6.

10. **Flag**: `src\executor\browser.py` (Implicit violation, requiring external module audit)
    **Violation**: While not present in `capture.py`, the reliance on `self.executor` implies interaction with a browser. If `src\executor\browser.Executor` uses DOM manipulation, CSS selectors, or accessibility trees internally to perform `capture()` or `focus_window()`, it would be a critical violation of Operon's "zero-abstraction" and "no DOM/selectors" invariants. Operon mandates purely vision-based perception and low-level, direct input injection.
    **Action**: Create a separate audit task for `src\executor\browser.Executor` to confirm strict adherence to vision-only and low-level input principles, ensuring no underlying DOM/selector usage.

## `src\agent\combined.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

1. Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.

    *   **Action:** Evaluate if `state.observation_history[-1].summary` can be further truncated or summarized to reduce token count for the LLM. Consider a configurable maximum length for `previous_summary` or a keyword extraction approach to keep the prompt concise, especially for P99 cases where longer prompts contribute to higher latency.

    *   **Action:** Replace `json.loads` with a faster alternative like `orjson` or `ujson` for parsing the `raw_output`. Profile the impact of this change on parsing time, especially for large responses, to improve P99 performance. This would require adding a new dependency.

    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`

If a recurring pattern of quality issues is detected (e.g., consistently missing labels on a specific screen type), the `_render_prompt` function could proactively incorporate more explicit instructions or examples into the *initial* prompt, reducing the likelihood of needing a costly retry.
*   **TASK 1.4: Implement early exit for critical parsing failures.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `_parse_combined_output`
    *   **Action:** Prioritize parsing critical information (e.g., action type) first. If immediate and fatal parsing errors occur (e.g., `PerceptionError("Combined output was not valid JSON.")`), fail faster with a specific error type that could trigger a dedicated, simpler fallback mechanism in an outer orchestration layer, rather than proceeding with full parsing that is guaranteed to fail.

### 2. Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.

*   **TASK 2.1: Ensure advisory hints persist across retries within a single `perceive` call.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `_render_prompt`
    *   **Action:** Currently, `self._advisory_hints.pop(...)` removes hints after the first prompt render within a `perceive` execution. If `_MAX_COMBINED_RETRIES > 0`, subsequent attempts in the same `perceive` call will not receive these hints. Change this to `self._advisory_hints.get(...)` for reading the hints, and `clear_advisory_hints(state.run_id)` should be called only upon *successful completion* of the `perceive` method (or explicitly after the retry loop, if hints are desired only for the first attempt).
*   **TASK 2.2: Make `add_advisory_hints` idempotent to prevent duplicate hints.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `add_advisory_hints`
    *   **Action:** Modify the method to check if an incoming `(hint, source)` tuple already exists in the `bucket` list before appending it. This ensures that adding the same hint multiple times has the same effect as adding it once, preventing prompt bloat with redundant information.
