### 3. Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.

*   **TASK 3.1: Implement adaptive prompt generation based on historical performance.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `_render_prompt`
    *   **Action:** Introduce a mechanism (potentially through an extension of `AgentState` or an external feedback loop) to track the types of actions that frequently succeed or fail in specific contexts. `_render_prompt` could then dynamically adjust prompt emphasis or provide specific examples based on this learned history (e.g., if "CLICK" actions on buttons of a certain visual style often fail, the prompt could request more explicit coordinates or alternative methods).
*   **TASK 3.2: Introduce dynamic model/strategy switching based on failure modes.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `perceive` (and external orchestration)
    *   **Action:** If `PerceptionError` or `PolicyError` reaches the retry limit, instead of just re-raising, this module could return a more nuanced status code or exception type. An outer orchestration layer could then interpret this and trigger a switch to a completely different strategy (e.g., a "diagnostic mode" prompt that focuses purely on describing the screen, or delegating to a simpler, faster, but less capable local model for a specific type of task). This requires extending error handling and integrating with a higher-level agent loop.
*   **TASK 3.3: Implement internal hint generation/long-term memory integration.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `add_advisory_hints` (and external components)
    *   **Action:** While `add_advisory_hints` currently receives hints externally, an agentic feature would be for Operon itself to *generate* these hints. This would involve an upstream component that processes `state.observation_history`, `state.action_history`, and potentially a long-term memory store (e.g., a vector database of past successful/unsuccessful interactions). This component would proactively call `add_advisory_hints` to inject relevant context for the next `perceive` call, enabling self-correction and learned behavior over time.

---

### 4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.

*   **TASK 4.1: Verify strict adherence to "no DOM/selectors" in perception processing.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py` (Indirect check via imported functions)
    *   **Function:** `_normalize_visible_elements`, `parse_perception_output` (from `src/agent/perception.py`)
    *   **Action:** Confirm that the internal logic of `_normalize_visible_elements` and `parse_perception_output` strictly operates on visual data (e.g., bounding boxes, extracted text, visual roles derived from appearance) and does not internally generate or rely on any HTML DOM, CSS selectors, or accessibility trees for identifying interactive elements or their properties. The `combined.py` module itself passes a screenshot path and relies on these functions; the invariant integrity rests on their implementation.
*   **TASK 4.2: Confirm `PolicyDecision` supports atomic `focus+type` representation.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/combined.py`
    *   **Function:** `_parse_combined_output`
    *   **Action:** Verify that the `PolicyDecision` object, specifically the `Action` it contains, can represent a single `TYPE` action that inherently includes both the target element's identification (e.g., coordinates) for focus and the text to be typed, as a single, atomic unit. This module produces the decision; the execution (elsewhere) must then honor this atomic execution. No violations are explicitly found in this module, but it's a critical interface point.

## `src\agent\fallback_backend.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference: Implement Speculative Execution for `perceive`**

*   **Task:** Modify the `perceive` method to execute `self.primary.perceive` and `self.secondary.perceive` concurrently. Prioritize the primary backend's result. If the primary backend fails with a `BackendCompatibilityError`, use the secondary backend's result if it succeeded. Otherwise, propagate the relevant error.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Import `asyncio`.
    2.  In `FallbackBackend.perceive`, replace the current `try-except` block with `asyncio.gather` calls for both primary and secondary backends, capturing their results and potential exceptions.
    3.  Implement logic to check `primary_result`. If it's a successful `ScreenPerception`, return it.
    4.  If `primary_result` is an exception and specifically `BackendCompatibilityError`, then check `secondary_result`. If `secondary_result` is a successful `ScreenPerception`, return it.
    5.  Otherwise (e.g., primary failed with a non-compatibility error, or both failed, or secondary failed after primary's compatibility error), re-raise the appropriate exception (preferably the primary's non-compatibility error, or a combined error if both failed).
    6.  Ensure `_active_backends` and `_latest_backend` are updated based on which backend's result was ultimately used.
    7.  Retain the `_clear_inactive_hints` call, ensuring it operates on the *final active* backend.

**2. Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference: Implement Speculative Execution for `choose_action`**

*   **Task:** Apply the same speculative execution pattern from Task 1 to the `choose_action` method to reduce P99 latency.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  In `FallbackBackend.choose_action`, parallelize calls to `self.primary.choose_action` and `self.secondary.choose_action` using `asyncio.gather`.
    2.  Implement the same result prioritization logic: primary success, then secondary success if primary had a `BackendCompatibilityError`, otherwise propagate errors.
    3.  Ensure `_active_backends` and `_latest_backend` are updated correctly.
    4.  Retain the `_clear_inactive_hints` call.

**3. Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency: Deduplicate Hints in `add_advisory_hints`**

*   **Task:** Modify `add_advisory_hints` to ensure that hints are deduplicated before being passed to the primary and secondary backends, preventing redundant hint appending if the same hint is added multiple times.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  In `FallbackBackend.add_advisory_hints`, convert the input `hints` list to a `set` to remove duplicates.
    2.  Convert the deduplicated set back to a `list` before passing it to `self.primary.add_advisory_hints` and `self.secondary.add_advisory_hints`.
    3.  Consider if the `AgentBackend` interface should internally handle hint deduplication to ensure idempotent behavior at the backend level, and add a docstring note if so. For now, `FallbackBackend` will ensure idempotent input.

**4. Suggest Agentic Features: Implement Dynamic Backend Switching Based on Performance**

*   **Task:** Introduce a mechanism for `FallbackBackend` to dynamically switch its default or preferred backend for new `run_id`s based on observed performance metrics (e.g., average latency, recent error rates) of `self.primary` and `self.secondary`.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Add internal state to `FallbackBackend` to track performance metrics for `primary` and `secondary` (e.g., `_performance_history: dict[AgentBackend, list[float]]` for latencies, `_error_counts: dict[AgentBackend, int]`). Update these metrics after each `perceive` and `choose_action` call.
    2.  Create a new asynchronous private method `_evaluate_backend_priority(run_id: str) -> AgentBackend` that analyzes these metrics and returns the currently preferred backend (either `primary` or `secondary`) for a given `run_id`, potentially based on an internal heuristic.
    3.  Modify `FallbackBackend._backend_for_run` to consult `_evaluate_backend_priority` when a `run_id` is encountered for the first time (`run_id` not in `_active_backends`). The result of this evaluation will then be stored in `_active_backends` for that `run_id`.

**5. Suggest Agentic Features: Proactive Backend Health Checks**

*   **Task:** Implement a background task within `FallbackBackend` to periodically and proactively check the health and readiness of both `primary` and `secondary` backends, independent of live inference requests.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Define a new abstract method `check_health(self) -> bool` in the `AgentBackend` base class, which concrete backends must implement (e.g., a lightweight ping or self-test).
    2.  In `FallbackBackend.__init__`, create an `asyncio.create_task` that periodically (e.g., every 60 seconds) calls `primary.check_health()` and `secondary.check_health()`.
    3.  Store the health status (e.g., `_backend_health: dict[AgentBackend, bool]`) and integrate this status into the `_evaluate_backend_priority` logic from Task 4, allowing an unhealthy backend to be deprioritized.
    4.  Add a `close()` or `shutdown()` method to `FallbackBackend` to gracefully cancel this background task.

**6. Suggest Agentic Features: Contextual Backend Preference Learning (Conceptual)**

*   **Task:** Introduce the foundation for the agent to learn and apply contextual preferences for backends based on the type or history of interaction associated with a `run_id`.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Augment `AgentState` or add a new parameter to `perceive`/`choose_action` (if applicable in `AgentBackend` interface) to include a `context_id` or `task_type`.
    2.  In `FallbackBackend`, add a persistent (e.g., `_context_preferences: dict[str, AgentBackend]`) mapping.
    3.  When a backend successfully completes a `perceive` or `choose_action` for a given `context_id`/`task_type`, update this `_context_preferences` to favor that backend for future similar contexts, especially if it outperformed the other. This preference would inform `_evaluate_backend_priority` (Task 4).
    4.  Log detailed success/failure events, including latency and the `context_id`/`task_type`, to enable future development of sophisticated learning algorithms for these preferences.

**7. Suggest Agentic Features: "Cognitive Backtracking" Mechanism**

*   **Task:** Provide a conceptual hook or method within `FallbackBackend` that would enable the main agent loop to trigger a "cognitive backtracking" or re-evaluation if a chosen action fails validation or execution, potentially forcing a re-perception or re-decision with modified parameters.
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Add a new asynchronous method `FallbackBackend.re_evaluate_action(self, state: AgentState, failure_reason: str, specific_hints: list[str] = None, force_backend: AgentBackend = None) -> PolicyDecision | None`.
    2.  This method would encapsulate logic to:
        *   Potentially modify `state` or `add_advisory_hints` based on `failure_reason` and `specific_hints`.
        *   If `force_backend` is provided, temporarily override `_backend_for_run` for this re-evaluation attempt.
        *   Re-invoke `self.perceive` and `self.choose_action` with the updated context.
        *   Return a new `PolicyDecision` or `None` if no viable action can be found after retry.
    3.  This method acts as an entry point for more sophisticated retry strategies from the main agent loop, allowing the agent to dynamically adapt its perception and policy generation after an initial action failure.

**8. Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants: Clarify `BackendCompatibilityError`**

*   **Task:** Add a clear documentation comment or design note regarding `BackendCompatibilityError` to ensure its use cases align with Operon's invariants (no DOM/selectors, zero-abstraction).
*   **Actionable Steps:**
    1.  Add a docstring to the `BackendCompatibilityError` class or a comment within `FallbackBackend`'s definition.
    2.  The docstring/comment should explicitly state that `BackendCompatibilityError` must be raised for generic contract failures (e.g., unsupported input format, resolution, missing general context) and *not* for issues related to missing or malformed UI-specific selectors, DOM elements, or other low-level structural abstractions. This reinforces that compatibility is about the *abstract perceptual/policy contract*, not the underlying implementation's specific handling of UI components.

## `src\agent\geometry.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

    *   **Task 1.1: Precompute and Cache Derived Bounding Box Properties**
        *   **Context:** Functions like `bbox_center`, `vertical_overlap`, and `horizontal_overlap` repeatedly calculate derived properties (center coordinates, `right`, `bottom`). Recomputing these on every call, especially when iterating over many `UIElement`s, introduces unnecessary overhead and can impact P99 latency.
        *   **Action:** Modify the `src/models/perception.py` (assuming `UIElement` is defined there) to store precomputed `center_x`, `center_y`, `right`, and `bottom` properties directly on the `UIElement` object upon initialization or during the perception pipeline. If `UIElement` is immutable, these should be computed once and stored.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/perception.py` (UIElement class), `src\agent\geometry.py` (update functions to use new properties).
        *   **Example Change (conceptual for UIElement):**
            ```python
            # In src/models/perception.py
            class UIElement:
                def __init__(self, x, y, width, height, ...):
                    self.x = x
                    self.y = y
                    self.width = width
                    self.height = height
                    # Precomputed properties
                    self.center_x = x + (width / 2.0)
                    self.center_y = y + (height / 2.0)
                    self.right = x + width
                    self.bottom = y + height
                    # ... other properties
            ```
            ```python
            # In src\agent\geometry.py, update bbox_center for consistency
            def bbox_center(element: UIElement) -> tuple[float, float]:
                return (element.center_x, element.center_y) # Use precomputed
            ```
            (And similar updates for `vertical_overlap`, `horizontal_overlap`, `same_row`, `same_column`, `is_above`, `is_left_of` to use `element.right`, `element.bottom` where applicable).

    *   **Task 1.2: Implement Batch Processing with NumPy for Core Geometric Comparisons**
        *   **Context:** When comparing a large list of `UIElement`s against another list (e.g., finding all labels for all input fields), iterating with Python loops and individual function calls can be slow. NumPy allows for highly optimized, vectorized operations.
        *   **Action:** Introduce a utility function or class that can convert lists of `UIElement`s into NumPy arrays (e.g., `N x 4` array for `[x, y, width, height]`) and perform batched versions of functions like `bbox_distance`, `vertical_overlap`, `horizontal_overlap`, `same_row`, and `same_column`. This should be opt-in for scenarios where large batch processing is expected.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (add new functions like `batch_bbox_distances`, `batch_vertical_overlaps`).
        *   **Example Change (conceptual):**
            ```python
            # In src\agent\geometry.py
            import numpy as np
            from typing import List

            def _elements_to_numpy(elements: List[UIElement]) -> np.ndarray:
                # Convert list of UIElement to a NumPy array of bounding boxes
                # Each row: [x, y, width, height, center_x, center_y, right, bottom]
                return np.array([
                    [e.x, e.y, e.width, e.height, e.center_x, e.center_y, e.right, e.bottom]
                    for e in elements
                ])

            def batch_bbox_distances(elements_a: List[UIElement], elements_b: List[UIElement]) -> np.ndarray:
                bboxes_a = _elements_to_numpy(elements_a)
                bboxes_b = _elements_to_numpy(elements_b)
                # Assuming center_x, center_y are at index 4, 5
                centers_a = bboxes_a[:, 4:6]
                centers_b = bboxes_b[:, 4:6]

                # Efficiently compute all-to-all distances if needed, or pairwise
                # For all-to-all: (Mx2) - (Nx2) results in a broadcasted (MxNx2) diff
                diff = centers_a[:, np.newaxis, :] - centers_b[np.newaxis, :, :]
                distances = np.sqrt(np.sum(diff**2, axis=2))
                return distances
            ```

    *   **Task 1.3: Introduce Spatial Data Structures for Proximity Queries**
        *   **Context:** When dealing with potentially thousands of `UIElement`s on a complex screen, finding nearby elements (e.g., for label grounding) using brute-force comparison (O(N^2)) is prohibitive for real-time performance.
        *   **Action:** Implement a spatial partitioning data structure (e.g., a k-d tree or R-tree) to efficiently query for `UIElement`s within a certain radius or region. This can significantly reduce the complexity of `bbox_distance` and similar proximity-based searches.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (add a `SpatialIndex` class/functions), or a new utility module for spatial indexing.
        *   **Example Change (conceptual):**
            ```python
            # In src\agent\geometry.py or new src/agent/spatial_index.py
            from scipy.spatial import KDTree

            class UIElementsSpatialIndex:
                def __init__(self, elements: List[UIElement]):
                    self.elements = elements
                    self.centers = np.array([bbox_center(e) for e in elements])
                    self.kdtree = KDTree(self.centers)

                def query_nearby(self, element: UIElement, max_distance: float) -> List[UIElement]:
                    center = bbox_center(element)
                    indices = self.kdtree.query_ball_point(center, max_distance)
                    return [self.elements[i] for i in indices]

            # In label grounding logic (not in geometry.py, but where it would be used)
            # spatial_index = UIElementsSpatialIndex(all_elements_on_screen)
            # nearby_labels = spatial_index.query_nearby(target_input_field, NEARBY_LABEL_MAX_DISTANCE_PX)
            ```

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

    *   **Task 2.1: Confirm and Document Functional Idempotency**
        *   **Context:** All functions in `src\agent\geometry.py` are pure functions; they take `UIElement` inputs and deterministic parameters, perform calculations, and return a result without any side effects or external state modification. This makes them inherently idempotent.
        *   **Action:** Explicitly document this property within the module or in the function docstrings. While not a structural change, it formalizes understanding of the module's behavior.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (module docstring, function docstrings).
        *   **Example Change:** Add a note to the module docstring: "All functions within this module are pure and stateless, ensuring functional idempotency."

    *   **Task 2.2: Ensure Idempotent Perception Pipeline for UIElement Generation**
        *   **Context:** For the geometric calculations to be structurally idempotent in a broader sense, the `UIElement` objects themselves must be generated idempotently. That is, given the same visual input (e.g., a screenshot), the perception pipeline (which is upstream of this module) must consistently produce the exact same list of `UIElement`s with identical bounding boxes and properties.
        *   **Action:** This is an upstream concern, but critical. Flag a requirement for the perception pipeline (`src/models/perception.py` and related vision modules) to guarantee deterministic and consistent `UIElement` outputs for identical visual inputs. Any stochasticity in `UIElement` generation would undermine the idempotency of downstream geometric reasoning.
        *   **File/Function:** (Flag for upstream: `src/models/perception.py` and visual processing modules).

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., Self-Healing Workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **Task 3.1: Implement Adaptive Geometric Tolerances with Contextual Learning**
        *   **Context:** The current tolerances (`ROW_TOLERANCE_PX`, `COLUMN_TOLERANCE_PX`, etc.) are fixed constants. An agentic system can adapt its understanding of "nearness" or "alignment" based on task performance and learned patterns.
        *   **Action:** Design a mechanism where these tolerances can be adjusted dynamically based on:
            *   **Application Context:** Different applications might have different UI design languages (e.g., a compact mobile app vs. a spacious desktop app).
            *   **Task Success/Failure:** If a task involving `same_row` fails repeatedly but a slightly larger tolerance would have succeeded (and made sense visually), the agent could learn to adjust.
            *   **User Feedback:** (If applicable) Explicit or implicit feedback could fine-tune tolerances.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (modify constants to be configurable/dynamic, potentially through a `ConfigManager` or `LearnedParameters` class). Implement a `ToleranceLearner` in `src/agent/learning.py` (new module).
        *   **Example Change:**
            ```python
            # In src\agent\geometry.py
            # ROW_TOLERANCE_PX = 22 # Becomes a default
            # Instead, these would be retrieved from a config/learning module
            # from src.agent.config import get_tolerance
            # from src.agent.learning import AdaptiveLearner

            def same_row(a: UIElement, b: UIElement, tolerance: float = None) -> bool:
                if tolerance is None:
                    # Dynamically retrieve based on context or learned values
                    # Assume context_id could be part of UIElement or inferred globally
                    # tolerance = AdaptiveLearner.get_row_tolerance(a.app_id)
                    tolerance = ROW_TOLERANCE_PX # Fallback, or load from config
                return abs(bbox_center(a)[1] - bbox_center(b)[1]) <= tolerance or vertical_overlap(a, b) >= 0.5
            ```

    *   **Task 3.2: Introduce Proactive Visual Servoing Optimization for Element Alignment**
        *   **Context:** Operon uses "visual servo" to guide actions. Currently, this likely reacts to the current state. An agentic feature would be to proactively adjust the view or target to *optimize* for interaction, even if the element is currently visible.
        *   **Action:** Develop functions that use geometric analysis to:
            *   **Predict optimal scroll/zoom:** Determine if scrolling or zooming (via `visual_servo`) would bring a target element into a more central or unobstructed view before interaction, improving reliability of subsequent atomic focus+type.
            *   **Suggest UI rearrangement (internal simulation):** For multi-step tasks, if two related elements are geometrically far apart or obscured, the agent could internally simulate a "better" arrangement (e.g., if it had control over the application layout) to anticipate potential interaction challenges and report them.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (add `calculate_optimal_view_offset`), `src/agent/visual_servo_planner.py` (new module for planning visual servo actions).

    *   **Task 3.3: Implement Anomaly Detection based on Geometric Relationships**
        *   **Context:** Standard workflow engines don't typically "understand" visual layout. Operon, as an agent, can. If the geometric relationship between key elements deviates significantly from learned or expected patterns, it could indicate an anomaly (e.g., a UI bug, an unexpected A/B test, or an application crash leading to a distorted view).
        *   **Action:** Create a system that profiles typical geometric relationships (e.g., "login button is usually below username field within X distance"). If observed relationships (`is_above`, `is_left_of`, `bbox_distance`) fall outside learned bounds, flag an anomaly that can trigger self-healing (e.g., re-scan, try alternative interaction strategy, alert user/developer).
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (extend functions to optionally return "confidence" or "deviation scores"), `src/agent/anomaly_detector.py` (new module).

4.  **Flag any Violations of Operon's Invariants**

    *   **Assessment:**
        *   **No DOM/selectors:** `src\agent\geometry.py` strictly operates on `UIElement` objects which are defined purely by visual bounding box coordinates (`x`, `y`, `width`, `height`). There is no mention or reliance on DOM elements, IDs, classes, XPaths, or CSS selectors. This module *perfectly adheres* to this invariant.
        *   **Atomic focus+type:** While `geometry.py` itself doesn't perform actions, it provides the fundamental spatial reasoning required to precisely locate target `UIElement`s for atomic focus and typing operations. By providing accurate `bbox_center` and proximity calculations, it directly supports this invariant.
        *   **Visual servo:** Similar to "atomic focus+type," `geometry.py` is foundational for visual servoing. The functions here enable the agent to understand the spatial relationships between elements, identify targets, and determine how to visually navigate to them. It *adheres* to this invariant by providing the necessary spatial intelligence.

    *   **Task 4.1: Confirm Adherence to Invariants**
        *   **Action:** Document that `src\agent\geometry.py` fully adheres to Operon's invariants by solely relying on visual properties (bounding boxes) for spatial reasoning, directly supporting `atomic focus+type` and `visual servo` operations without any reliance on DOM structures.
        *   **File/Function:** `src\agent\geometry.py` (module docstring).
        *   **Example Change:** Add to the module docstring: "This module strictly adheres to Operon's invariants by operating solely on vision-derived bounding box properties, enabling precise spatial reasoning crucial for atomic focus+type interactions and visual servo guidance, without any reliance on DOM or selectors."

## `src\agent\hitl.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task:** Implement an explicit, configurable timeout for the `gemini_client.generate_policy` call within `async def generate_hitl_message`. If the LLM call exceeds this timeout, the function should immediately fall back to returning the `fallback` message.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_hitl_message`
        *   **Details:** The `gemini_client` likely has its own timeout, but an explicit timeout here can ensure graceful degradation without blocking indefinitely.
    *   **Task:** Introduce an in-memory Least Recently Used (LRU) cache for the results of `generate_hitl_message`. Cache keys should be derived from the input parameters (`intent`, `page_hint`, `url`, `visible_element_names`) to reuse previously generated messages for recurring stuck states.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_hitl_message`
        *   **Details:** Consider `functools.lru_cache` if applicable, or a custom async cache.
    *   **Task:** Explore implementing speculative execution for `generate_hitl_message`. If other operations are performed *before* the HITL message is strictly needed (e.g., logging, initial UI refresh), kick off the LLM call concurrently. If it completes before the message is displayed, use it; otherwise, use the fallback.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_hitl_message` (and potentially its callers)
        *   **Details:** This might require changes in the calling logic to initiate the LLM call earlier.

2.  **Structural Idempotency Opportunities**
    *   **Task:** Implement a short-term, per-`run_id` debounce or rate-limiting mechanism within `notify_desktop` (or its callers) to prevent sending multiple identical desktop notifications if `notify_desktop` is invoked rapidly for the same HITL event.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `notify_desktop` (and potentially `start_escalation_timer`'s `notify_fn` caller)
        *   **Details:** A global dictionary `_active_notifications = {run_id: last_timestamp}` could track recent notifications and block/debounce subsequent identical calls within a short window.
    *   **Task:** Ensure `async def start_escalation_timer` is idempotent per `run_id`. If `start_escalation_timer` is called multiple times for the same `run_id` while an existing escalation task is active, it should either ignore subsequent calls or cancel the existing task and start a new one, preventing duplicate escalation sequences and notifications.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `start_escalation_timer`
        *   **Details:** Maintain a dictionary of active `asyncio.Task` objects keyed by `run_id` to manage this.
    *   **Task:** Augment the payload of `async def post_hitl_webhook` with a unique `notification_id` (e.g., a UUID or a combination of `run_id` and timestamp/sequence number). This will enable downstream webhook consumers to implement idempotency, ensuring that even if the same webhook is sent multiple times, it's processed only once by the receiver.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `post_hitl_webhook`
        *   **Details:** The `run_id` identifies the overall agent run; a `notification_id` would uniquely identify *this specific notification event*.

3.  **Agentic Features Beyond Standard Workflows**
    *   **Task:** Introduce a "self-healing policy" mechanism that allows the agent to attempt predefined, vision-based corrective actions for known `HITL_PAGE_HINT_KEYWORDS` *before* escalating to human intervention. For example, if "cookie_consent" is detected, try visually identifying and clicking an "Accept" button.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py` (and potentially a new module for policy execution)
        *   **Details:** This would extend `HITL_PAGE_HINT_KEYWORDS` to map keywords to specific vision-servo action sequences.
    *   **Task:** Implement a feedback loop to learn from human interventions. When a human unblocks the agent (e.g., clicks "Resume" after an intervention), capture the visual context, the human's actions (if possible), and the resolution. This data can then be used to train or refine future self-healing policies or to improve prompt generation.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py` (and system-level components capturing human input)
        *   **Details:** Requires storing interaction logs and potentially a separate learning component.
    *   **Task:** Enhance HITL triggering by incorporating broader vision-based pattern recognition. Beyond simple substring matches in `page_hint`, use screen classification or object detection (e.g., to identify "captcha-like forms" or "login page layouts") to proactively detect intervention needs, even if explicit keywords are absent.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py` (and upstream visual processing components)
        *   **Details:** This leverages Operon's vision-only nature to identify common problematic UI patterns.
    *   **Task:** Implement automated diagnostic data collection. When HITL is triggered, automatically package relevant diagnostic information (e.g., full screenshot, agent's internal thought process/state, recent action history, relevant logs) to present to the human or a higher-level diagnostic agent.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py` (and its calling context)
        *   **Details:** This data would be invaluable for faster human debugging and future agent improvements.

4.  **Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Task:** Explicitly document the origin and derivation method for the `page_hint` parameter in the docstring of `async def generate_hitl_message` (and any other functions consuming it).
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_hitl_message`
        *   **Details:** Confirm that `page_hint` is derived *exclusively* from visual processing (e.g., OCR of prominent page text, visual classification of page type) and *not* from any DOM inspection or selector-based extraction.
    *   **Task:** Explicitly document the origin and derivation method for the `visible_element_names` parameter in the docstring of `async def generate_hitl_message`.
        *   **File:** `src\agent\hitl.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_hitl_message`
        *   **Details:** Confirm that `visible_element_names` are derived *exclusively* from visual recognition (e.g., OCR of text within visible elements, visual semantic labeling) and *not* from DOM element attributes (like `id`, `name`, `aria-label`).
    *   **Justification for Invariant Flags:** The `hitl.py` module itself does not perform actions that directly violate "no DOM/selectors," "atomic focus+type," or "visual servo." However, its inputs (`page_hint`, `visible_element_names`) are critical. The current code *assumes* these inputs conform to Operon's invariants but does not enforce or explicitly state their vision-only origin. This ambiguity needs to be resolved through documentation to ensure strict adherence to Operon's architectural principles throughout the system.

## `src\agent\loop.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference

-   **TASK 1.1: Optimize `_page_signature` computation (Memoization/Caching)**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_page_signature` (and its callers like `_sync_progress_state_with_perception`, `_block_redundant_action`, `_update_progress_state`)
    -   **Description:** `_page_signature` generates a string by iterating through `visible_elements` and string concatenation. This is called multiple times per step, and for UI-heavy pages, this string processing can introduce minor overhead.
    -   **Action:** Modify `_page_signature` to memoize its result for a given `ScreenPerception` object within a single `step_run` execution. Alternatively, consider integrating a `_page_signature` field directly into the `ScreenPerception` model, computed once upon perception creation.
    -   **Rationale:** Avoid redundant computation of the same page signature within a single step or across steps if the underlying perception hasn't changed meaningfully, reducing CPU cycles on the critical path.

-   **TASK 1.2: Optimize `_resolve_action_target` for large `visible_elements` lists**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_resolve_action_target`
    -   **Description:** This function performs linear searches through `perception.visible_elements` (once by `element_id`, once by coordinates). For UIs with many elements, this O(N) lookup can become a P99 bottleneck.
    -   **Action:** Modify the `ScreenPerception` model (defined externally, but affects usage here) to include an efficient lookup map (e.g., `dict[str, UIElement]`) for `element_id` to `UIElement` mapping. For coordinate-based lookups, consider spatial indexing structures like an R-tree or quadtree if `visible_elements` frequently exceeds a few hundred.
    -   **Rationale:** Improve element lookup speed, especially for complex or dense UIs, converting linear searches into near-constant-time operations.

-   **TASK 1.3: Asynchronous `_prepare_step_artifacts` file operations**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_prepare_step_artifacts`
    -   **Description:** `Path(...).mkdir` and `Path(...).touch` are synchronous file system operations. While minor, these can cause brief blocking in an `asyncio` event loop.
    -   **Action:** Convert these synchronous file operations to use `asyncio.to_thread` or an equivalent non-blocking approach to prevent event loop blocking.
    -   **Example Hint:**
        ```python
        await asyncio.to_thread(Path(before_artifact_path).parent.mkdir, parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        await asyncio.to_thread(Path(after_artifact_path).parent.mkdir, parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        await asyncio.to_thread(Path(self._run_log_path(run_id)).parent.mkdir, parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        await asyncio.to_thread(Path(self._run_log_path(run_id)).touch, exist_ok=True)
        ```
    -   **Rationale:** Ensure all I/O is non-blocking to maintain responsiveness of the event loop, crucial for low P99 latency.

-   **TASK 1.4: Asynchronous Logging for `_trace` function**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_trace`
    -   **Description:** The `print` statement inside `_trace` is synchronous. When `_TRACE` is enabled, frequent `print` calls can block the event loop, especially if stdout is buffered or redirected to a slow target.
    -   **Action:** Modify `_trace` to use `asyncio.to_thread` for the `print` call, or integrate with an asynchronous logging library.
    -   **Rationale:** Prevent synchronous logging from introducing unpredictable delays and impacting P99 latency when detailed tracing is active.

-   **TASK 1.5: Evaluate and Optimize `_wait_for_page_load` for faster page state detection**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_wait_for_page_load`
    -   **Description:** This function relies on fixed exponential backoff (`asyncio.sleep` for up to 14s total) and re-captures to detect page load completion. This can significantly increase P99 latency for pages with variable loading times.
    -   **Action:** Investigate if the underlying `executor` (e.g., browser or desktop executor) can provide more proactive, non-blocking signals for visual stability or page readiness (e.g., a "visually stable" event) *without* violating Operon's visual-only invariant. This might involve the executor intelligently monitoring rendering changes at a higher frequency internally.
    -   **Rationale:** Expedite recovery from `PENDING` states by reducing reliance on fixed-delay polling, thereby improving P99 latency.

### 2. Opportunities for structural idempotency

-   **TASK 2.1: Formalize idempotency for `start_run` and `run_store.create_run`**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `start_run`, `self.run_store.create_run`
    -   **Description:** Currently, `run_store.create_run` generates a new `run_id` for every `RunTaskRequest`. If an external system retries or re-invokes `start_run` with the same logical intent, it could create duplicate runs.
    -   **Action:** Enhance `run_store.create_run` to check for an existing "active" run (e.g., `RUNNING`, `WAITING_FOR_USER`) that matches the `intent` and `start_url` before creating a new one. If found, return the existing run's `run_id` and status. Define clear criteria for what constitutes a "matching" run.
    -   **Rationale:** Prevent logical duplicate runs, ensure consistent state management across retries, and reduce unnecessary resource allocation.

-   **TASK 2.2: Ensure `target_failure_counts` is robust to internal retries**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_update_target_failure_signal`
    -   **Description:** The `_update_target_failure_signal` function increments failure counters. The `step_run` method's internal `while True` loop for `EXECUTE`/`VERIFY` can result in multiple *attempts* within a single logical step. If this function is called on each attempt, `target_failure_counts` could over-count failures for a single "step decision," potentially triggering `_coordinate_thrash_detected` prematurely.
    -   **Action:** Re-evaluate when `_update_target_failure_signal` is called. It should ideally reflect distinct failures across *logical agent steps* rather than *internal execution attempts* within a single step. Consider linking failure counts to `(action_signature, step_index)` or reset counts per `step_index` if the intent is to track failures across different policy decisions. The current approach with `attempt_index` in `_record_unified_step` could inform a more precise key for `target_failure_counts`.
    -   **Rationale:** Maintain accurate failure metrics to prevent false positives in internal loop detection mechanisms (`_coordinate_thrash_detected`).

-   **TASK 2.3: Verify `Executor.aclose_run` idempotency**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_cleanup_completed_run` (calls `self.executor.aclose_run`)
    -   **Description:** The `_cleanup_completed_run` is invoked after a run completes. If this method is called multiple times (e.g., due to retry mechanisms or race conditions), `Executor.aclose_run` must handle subsequent calls gracefully.
    -   **Action:** Verify the implementation of `Executor.aclose_run` (and its adapters like `UnifiedBrowserExecutor.aclose_run`) to ensure it's idempotent. It should gracefully do nothing or return success if the underlying run/resources are already closed.
    -   **Rationale:** Ensure reliable resource cleanup and avoid errors during idempotent retry scenarios.

### 3. Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines

-   **TASK 3.1: Proactive Strategy Re-planning and Goal Decomposition on Stagnation/Loops**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_inject_stagnation_hint`, `_block_redundant_action`, `_detect_loop_failure`
    -   **Description:** The current system uses hints and blocks redundant actions when stagnation or loops are detected, eventually leading to a failure. A more agentic approach would involve a deeper, generative re-planning.
    -   **Action:** Instead of simply blocking or resetting a subgoal to a generic "Stalled" message, when a persistent loop or stagnation is detected (e.g., by `_detect_loop_failure` or `_block_redundant_action`):
        1.  Trigger a dedicated "Re-planning" sub-agent or LLM call.
        2.  This sub-agent, with access to `state.intent`, `state.observation_history`, `state.progress_state`, and failure traces, would generate a *fundamentally new* approach or decomposed subgoals to overcome the obstacle. This could involve exploring different parts of the UI, searching for alternative interaction patterns, or even recommending a different application.
        3.  The output of this re-planning would update `state.current_subgoal` and potentially inject a new action into the policy service's memory.
    -   **Rationale:** Move beyond reactive, rule-based recovery to proactive, intelligent re-strategizing, enabling the agent to resolve complex impasses without external human intervention.

-   **TASK 3.2: Active Learning from Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) Interventions**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_pause_for_user`, `self.reflector`
    -   **Description:** The agent can pause for human intervention. The `PostRunReflector` analyzes completed runs. This is a solid foundation for learning.
    -   **Action:**
        1.  When `_pause_for_user` is invoked, capture the comprehensive state (`state`, `perception`, `decision`) immediately *before* human intervention.
        2.  Upon `resume_run`, if the human manually interacts with the environment, ensure these manual actions are logged precisely.
        3.  Extend `PostRunReflector` to specifically analyze these "before/after" HITL events. This analysis would generate structured learning data (e.g., "Given this state, the human performed this action leading to success") which can be used to:
            *   Generate new rules for `PolicyService` or `RecoveryManager`.
            *   Provide training examples or fine-tuning data for the LLM powering `PolicyService` or `PerceptionService` (e.g., correcting misinterpretations).
    -   **Rationale:** Transform human intervention from merely a recovery mechanism into a continuous feedback loop for agent improvement, allowing Operon to learn from its failures and adapt its policies over time.

-   **TASK 3.3: Predictive Failure Anticipation with Internal Simulation**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Description:** The current loop is primarily reactive, detecting failures *after* an action is executed and verified.
    -   **Action:** Introduce an optional "Pre-execution Simulation" phase after `POLICY` but before `EXECUTE`.
        1.  Develop a lightweight internal "world model" within the agent (e.g., a simplified representation of UI state transitions and action effects).
        2.  After the `PolicyService` proposes an `AgentAction`, the agent could (via this internal model or a fast, small LLM call) simulate the likely outcome of that action.
        3.  If the simulation predicts a high probability of failure, a loop, or an undesirable state, the agent would proactively *reject* its own policy decision and trigger an immediate internal re-policy or adaptation step *before* actually performing the action.
    -   **Rationale:** Move from reactive self-healing to proactive self-adaptation, minimizing wasted steps, reducing costly real-world interactions, and improving overall efficiency and P99 reliability by avoiding predictable failures.

---

### 4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.

-   **TASK 4.1: Eliminate DOM/selector fields from `UIElement` model**
    -   **File:** `src\models\perception.py` (model definition, external to `AgentLoop`) and implications for `src\agent\selector.py`, `src\models\selector.py`
    -   **Violation:** **NO DOM/SELECTORS INVARIANT.** The `UIElement` model, which is the output of the `PerceptionService` and consumed by `AgentLoop`, includes fields like `dom_id`, `css_selector`, and `xpath`. These are direct browser DOM abstractions and fundamentally violate Operon's "vision-only, zero-abstraction" principle. The `AgentAction` also supports `selector`.
    -   **Action:**
        1.  **HIGH PRIORITY:** Remove `dom_id`, `css_selector`, and `xpath` fields from the `UIElement` model in `src\models\perception.py`.
        2.  Ensure that `PerceptionService` (`src\agent\perception.py`) is strictly visual-based and *never* populates or relies on these DOM-specific attributes.
        3.  Audit `DeterministicTargetSelector` (`src\agent\selector.py`) and `TargetIntent` (`src\models\selector.py`) to confirm they rely *only* on visually-derived properties (e.g., `primary_name`, `role`, `element_type`, bounding box coordinates, `is_interactable`).
        4.  Remove the `selector` field from `AgentAction` and `TargetIntent`. If `action.selector` in `_target_signature` is intended for non-DOM visual identifiers, it must be renamed to reflect this.
    -   **Severity:** High. This is a core architectural violation, compromising the "zero-abstraction" promise.

-   **TASK 4.2: Consolidate "focus" behavior within the `TYPE` action for atomic interaction**
    -   **File:** `src\agent\loop.py`
    -   **Function:** `_apply_coord_anchor`, `_update_coord_anchor`
    -   **Violation:** **ATOMIC FOCUS+TYPE INVARIANT.** The `_apply_coord_anchor` logic attempts to correct `TYPE` action coordinates based on the coordinates of a *previously successful `CLICK` action* on the same element. This implies that the `TYPE` action itself (via the executor) does not reliably handle the "focus" aspect (clicking/activating the input field) before typing, or that its visual servo is not robust enough for this, thus requiring a non-visual, cached coordinate correction from a prior `CLICK`. This breaks the atomicity of "focus+type."
    -   **Action:**
        1.  Refactor the `Executor` (and its unified adapters, `UnifiedBrowserExecutor`, `UnifiedDesktopExecutor`) so that any `TYPE` action, when given `(x, y)` coordinates, *atomically* performs a robust visual servo "focus" operation (e.g., a precise click or activation) at those coordinates *before* typing. This `TYPE` action should be self-contained and visually servo-driven from start to finish.
        2.  Upon successful implementation in the executor, remove the `_update_coord_anchor` and `_apply_coord_anchor` logic from `AgentLoop`. The visual servo for `TYPE` should be sufficient without cached coordinates.
    -   **Severity:** Medium. Introduces a workaround that bypasses core invariant principles and adds an unnecessary layer of statefulness.

-   **TASK 4.3: Validate Executor Implementations for Strict Visual Servo Adherence**
    -   **File:** `src\executor\browser.py` and `executors\browser_executor.py`, `executors\desktop_executor.py` (external to `AgentLoop`, but its behavior is critical)
    -   **Violation:** **VISUAL SERVO INVARIANT (Potential, requires external validation).** The `AgentLoop` passes `AgentAction` objects (with coordinates) to the `executor`. For Operon to truly be visual-servo driven, the `executor` *must* interact with the system by visually targeting pixels and confirming actions visually. This is a critical dependency, and `AgentLoop` cannot enforce it directly.
    -   **Action:** Conduct a thorough audit and validation of the `src.executor.browser.Executor`, `executors.browser_executor.UnifiedBrowserExecutor`, and `executors.desktop_executor.UnifiedDesktopExecutor` implementations to ensure they:
        1.  Do not fall back to hidden DOM/accessibility tree interactions for actions like `CLICK`, `TYPE`, `DRAG`, `HOVER`, etc.
        2.  Perform pre-action visual checks (e.g., target element is visible and unobstructed at `(x,y)`).
        3.  Actively monitor for visual changes *during* and *after* action execution to confirm success and provide feedback (e.g., `ExecutedAction.success`).
    -   **Severity:** High (if violated in executor). This is a foundational invariant that the `AgentLoop` implicitly trusts its executor to uphold.

## `src\agent\perception.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

    *   **Task 1.1: Asynchronous Image Dimension Retrieval**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_check_coord_bounds`
        *   **Description**: The `Image.open(screenshot_path)` call is a synchronous I/O operation that can block the event loop, contributing to P99 latency. `CaptureFrame` likely already holds the native dimensions (`width`, `height`).
        *   **Action**: Modify `_check_coord_bounds` to accept `native_w` and `native_h` directly from the `CaptureFrame` object (e.g., `screenshot.width`, `screenshot.height`). Remove the `Image.open` call from this function.
        *   **Impact**: Eliminates blocking disk I/O during perception processing, significantly reducing latency spikes.

    *   **Task 1.2: Offload CPU-bound JSON Parsing and Pydantic Validation**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `parse_perception_output`
        *   **Description**: `json.loads(cleaned)` and `RawScreenPerception.model_validate(parsed)` are synchronous, CPU-bound operations that can introduce significant latency, especially with large or complex LLM outputs.
        *   **Action**: Wrap these CPU-intensive calls in `run_in_executor` to move them to a `ThreadPoolExecutor`, preventing them from blocking the asyncio event loop.
        *   **Impact**: Prevents blocking the event loop during heavy CPU computations, improving responsiveness and P99 latency.

    *   **Task 1.3: Optimize `_fix_spaced_json` for Performance**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_fix_spaced_json`
        *   **Description**: The current iterative `re.sub` loop can be inefficient if the input string is very long or contains many spaced characters, impacting P99 latency when this fallback is triggered.
        *   **Action**: Re-evaluate the regex and looping mechanism. Consider if a single, more complex regex `re.sub(r'(?<=\S)\s+(?=\S)', '', text)` (or a variation) can achieve the desired result in one pass, or if a more explicit token-based parsing approach would be faster for character collapsing.
        *   **Impact**: Reduces latency for malformed LLM outputs that require character collapsing.

    *   **Task 1.4: Pre-compute `_label_text_candidates`**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Functions**: `perceive` (caller), `_apply_weak_canonicalization`, `_salvage_perception`
        *   **Description**: The `_label_text_candidates` helper function is called multiple times (`_apply_weak_canonicalization`, `_salvage_perception`) with the same list of elements within a single `perceive` invocation.
        *   **Action**: In the `perceive` method, compute `text_candidates = _label_text_candidates(perception.visible_elements)` once after initial parsing and pass this pre-computed list to `_apply_weak_canonicalization` and `_salvage_perception`.
        *   **Impact**: Reduces redundant list filtering and iteration, providing a minor improvement to average latency.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

    *   **Task 2.1: Ensure Functional Purity of `_normalize_visible_elements`**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_normalize_visible_elements`
        *   **Description**: The function `_normalize_visible_elements` modifies the `parsed` dictionary in place. While its behavior is deterministic, explicitly returning a new, modified copy enhances functional purity and predictability, reinforcing idempotency if the raw output needs to be re-processed.
        *   **Action**: Modify `_normalize_visible_elements` to accept a dictionary, perform the necessary modifications on a *copy* of that dictionary (or a deep copy of its 'visible_elements' list), and return the modified copy.
        *   **Impact**: Improves the predictability and strict idempotency of the parsing pipeline by avoiding in-place modifications of input data.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **Task 3.1: Adaptive Prompt Refinement based on Specific Failure Modes**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_render_prompt`
        *   **Description**: The current semantic retry appends a generic instruction. An agentic system could leverage the specific `low_quality_reason` to provide more targeted, intelligent instructions to the LLM for the retry.
        *   **Action**: Enhance `_render_prompt` to accept `low_quality_reason` as an optional parameter. Dynamically construct the retry instructions based on the specific reason provided (e.g., if "unlabeled_ratio" is high, ask the LLM to prioritize labeling; if "no interactive elements", ask it to explicitly identify clickable/typable areas).
        *   **Impact**: Improves the agent's ability to self-correct more efficiently by guiding the LLM with highly specific feedback based on prior output quality issues.

    *   **Task 3.2: Dynamic Model or Strategy Switching for Persistent Failures**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `perceive`
        *   **Description**: If `PerceptionLowQualityError` persists after all configured retries and salvaging, the agent currently fails. A more agentic approach would be to dynamically switch to a more robust (potentially slower or more expensive) perception strategy.
        *   **Action**: Implement logic in `perceive` to, upon unrecoverable `PerceptionLowQualityError`, attempt a fallback strategy. This could involve using a different `GeminiClient` instance (e.g., a higher-capacity or fine-tuned model), invoking a different perception pipeline (if available), or capturing the screenshot with different parameters (e.g., higher resolution).
        *   **Impact**: Enhances the agent's resilience by allowing it to adapt its tools and methods to overcome complex or challenging perception scenarios.

    *   **Task 3.3: Proactive Ambiguity Resolution for Unlabeled Elements**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_salvage_perception`, `_infer_nearby_label`
        *   **Description**: When `_infer_nearby_label` fails to find a label for an interactable element, the agent currently just proceeds, potentially leading to a lower quality perception. An agentic system would actively seek clarification.
        *   **Action**: If an interactable element remains unlabeled (and `is_unlabeled` is `True`) after `_salvage_perception`, introduce an optional step to generate a *follow-up, targeted LLM query*. This query would present a focused sub-screenshot around the unlabeled element and ask the LLM specifically for its purpose or a suitable label. The result would then update the `UIElement`.
        *   **Impact**: Reduces reliance on heuristics and improves the semantic grounding of critical interactive elements, leading to more accurate and reliable agent actions.

    *   **Task 3.4: Integrate Diagnostic Feedback into Active Learning Loop**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\perception.py`
        *   **Function**: `_write_diagnostics_artifact`
        *   **Description**: The detailed diagnostic artifacts are valuable but are currently primarily for debugging. An agentic system would use this data for continuous self-improvement.
        *   **Action**: Design and implement an asynchronous mechanism to ingest and analyze the `diagnostics_artifact.json` data. This analysis should identify patterns in `quality_gate_reason` and `salvage_reason` across multiple perception steps. This system could then autonomously trigger updates to prompt templates, adjust quality thresholds, or inform fine-tuning efforts for the perception LLM over time.
        *   **Impact**: Enables the agent to learn from its perception successes and failures, leading to autonomous improvement in its overall performance and robustness.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo**

    *   **Finding**: No violations of Operon's invariants were identified in the `src/agent/perception.py` module.
    *   **Justification**:
        *   **No DOM/selectors**: The module explicitly works with visually derived `UIElement` properties (bounding boxes, labels, types) from a `CaptureFrame`, entirely bypassing reliance on a Document Object Model or selector-based targeting.
        *   **Atomic focus+type**: This module provides the `ScreenPerception` data, including `focused_element_id` and precise coordinates, which are essential inputs for downstream components that perform atomic focus and type actions. It ensures the data is suitable for such operations without performing the actions itself.
        *   **Visual servo**: The module handles coordinate upscaling (`_upscale_element_coords`) to native screen resolution and includes a coordinate bounds check (`_check_coord_bounds`). These functionalities are critical for ensuring the output `ScreenPerception` is accurate and reliable for pixel-accurate visual servoing by other components.

## `src\agent\policy.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to reduce P99 latency for real-time inference**

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize `_render_prompt` for common scenarios.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService._render_prompt`
    *   **Action:**
        *   Analyze if the `advisory_hints` processing, particularly the string concatenation `"\n".join(f"- {h}" for h, _ in hints)`, could become a bottleneck if the `hints` list grows very large (e.g., hundreds or thousands of hints). Consider if a fixed maximum number of hints should be included in the prompt, or if a more efficient data structure (e.g., a pre-formatted string stored with the hints) could reduce rendering time for the tail latency cases.
        *   Consider pre-rendering static parts of the prompt or using a more efficient templating engine if Python's `str.format` becomes a measurable bottleneck for very complex state/perception objects (unlikely but worth considering for extreme P99 targets).

*   **Task 1.2: Implement client-side caching for `choose_action` (optional but impactful).**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService.choose_action`
    *   **Action:** Introduce a limited-size, in-memory cache (e.g., LRU cache) for `PolicyDecision` objects based on a hash of the `state` and `perception` inputs. This could significantly reduce P99 latency if similar states or perceptions are encountered frequently. Ensure the cache key generation is efficient and robust, considering the potentially large size of `perception.model_dump_json()`.

*   **Task 1.3: Implement a fast-path/fallback mechanism for LLM errors.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService.choose_action`
    *   **Action:** Modify the `except GeminiClientError` block to include a retry mechanism with exponential backoff for transient errors, or a configurable timeout after which a simplified, heuristic-driven `PolicyDecision` is returned (e.g., "WAIT_FOR_USER", "REFRESH_PAGE") as a fallback, rather than immediately raising an exception. This improves overall availability and reduces the P99 for receiving *any* decision.

*   **Task 1.4: Optimize JSON serialization and parsing.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `_normalize_policy_payload` and `parse_policy_output`
    *   **Action:** While `json.loads` and Pydantic validation are generally fast, for extremely high-throughput or low-latency environments with very large policy outputs, investigate alternative, faster JSON parsers (e.g., `orjson`) or pre-compiling Pydantic models. Profile these functions to determine if they contribute significantly to P99 latency before implementing.

---

**2. Opportunities for structural idempotency**

*   **Task 2.1: Ensure idempotency of `add_advisory_hints`.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService.add_advisory_hints`
    *   **Action:** Currently, `add_advisory_hints` appends hints, allowing duplicates. If the intention is for `_advisory_hints` to contain unique entries per `(hint, source)` tuple for a given `run_id`, modify the logic to check for existing hints before appending. For example, convert the `bucket` list to a `set` for de-duplication, or iterate and check `if incoming_hint not in bucket`. This prevents prompt bloat from repeated hints if the agent or external systems call this function multiple times with the same advice.

*   **Task 2.2: Verify background writer idempotency.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `bg_writer.enqueue` calls within `GeminiPolicyService.choose_action` and `_latest_usage`
    *   **Action:** Review the `src.store.background_writer` implementation (outside this module, but relevant) to explicitly confirm that enqueuing the same content to the same file path multiple times results in the same final file state without errors or resource contention. Specifically, ensure that concurrent or sequential enqueues of identical content for the same path are handled gracefully (e.g., overwriting, or ignoring if content is identical) without introducing race conditions or excess disk I/O.

**3. Agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement adaptive prompt modification based on `verification_history`.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService._render_prompt`
    *   **Action:** Enhance the `_render_prompt` logic. Instead of merely including `last_verification` as a string, dynamically inject specific instructions or rephrase the prompt if `state.verification_history` indicates a failed verification (`last_vr.status == "failed"`). For example, if `last_vr.recovery_hint` is available, transform it into an explicit instruction for the LLM like: "PREVIOUS ACTION FAILED. REASON: '{last_vr.reason}'. RECOVERY HINT: '{last_vr.recovery_hint}'. ADAPT YOUR NEXT ACTION ACCORDINGLY." This enables the agent to self-correct by explicitly guiding the LLM based on past failures.

*   **Task 3.2: Introduce self-reflection and re-prompting for `PolicyError`.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService.choose_action`
    *   **Action:** Modify the `except PolicyError` block. If `parse_policy_output` fails due to `PolicyError` (e.g., invalid JSON or schema mismatch), instead of immediately raising, the agent should:
        1.  Log the error with higher severity.
        2.  Increment a retry counter for this specific `state.run_id` or `state.step_count`.
        3.  If under a retry threshold, generate a *new* meta-prompt that explicitly instructs the LLM to correct its output format, referencing the parsing error. For example: "YOUR PREVIOUS RESPONSE FAILED TO PARSE. ENSURE YOUR OUTPUT IS STRICTLY VALID JSON AND CONFORMS TO THE SCHEMA. DO NOT INCLUDE ANY ADDITIONAL TEXT." Then, re-call `gemini_client.generate_policy` with this modified prompt. This allows the agent to self-heal its interaction with the LLM.

*   **Task 3.3: Dynamic advisory hint generation from observed patterns.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `GeminiPolicyService.add_advisory_hints` and `_render_prompt` (and potentially a new internal method)
    *   **Action:** Develop an internal mechanism (e.g., a lightweight pattern detector or a simple short-term memory) that observes sequences of successful actions or common error recovery patterns. Automatically generate and add `advisory_hints` (scoped to `run_id` or globally) based on these observations. For instance, if the agent repeatedly navigates to a specific URL and then clicks a certain `(x, y)` coordinate successfully, it could generate a hint like: "When on page X, click button at (Y, Z) to proceed." This moves beyond manually injected hints to learned, dynamic guidance.

---

**4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**

*   **Task 4.1: Eliminate `selector` field from policy output processing.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py`
    *   **Function:** `_normalize_policy_payload`
    *   **Violation:** The presence of `"selector"` within the `_PAYLOAD_FIELDS` set implies that the policy output *could* contain a selector, which directly violates Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant. Even if currently normalized out for some action types, its mere presence in the processing logic indicates a potential path for abstraction.
    *   **Action:** Remove `"selector"` from the `_PAYLOAD_FIELDS` set. Ensure that the `PolicyDecision` model (defined in `src.models.policy`, which is an import dependency) does not include a `selector` field for any action type. All interactive actions must solely rely on visual coordinates (`x`, `y`) or direct key/text input.

*   **Task 4.2: Confirm `PolicyDecision` model adheres to atomic focus+type.**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\policy.py` (implicitly impacts `src.models.policy`)
    *   **Function:** `_normalize_policy_payload` (specifically `ActionType.TYPE` logic)
    *   **Invariant Check:** The current `_normalize_policy_payload` correctly handles `text`, `key`, and `press_enter` for `TYPE` actions, aligning with an atomic "type this then optionally press enter" operation. This is consistent with atomic focus+type *provided* the system guarantees visual focus on an input element before this action is executed.
    *   **Action:** No direct change needed in this module, but this serves as a flag to ensure the `PolicyDecision` model itself for `TYPE` actions only allows `text` and `press_enter` and *does not* include any fields that would imply intermediate steps for focus manipulation or element identification (e.g., `focus_element_id`, `find_input_by_label`). The responsibility of achieving focus must be an explicit preceding visual-servo driven action, not part of the `TYPE` action decision payload itself.

## `src\agent\policy_coordinator.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Violation of Operon Invariant: No DOM/selectors**
    *   **Reasoning**: The module explicitly imports, processes, and logs `SelectorTrace` objects. Operon's core invariant is "vision-only, zero-abstraction," meaning it should not interact with or have knowledge of DOM or abstract selectors. Even if for debugging, their presence in the data flow implies an abstraction that violates this principle. The agent should operate purely on visual perception.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Action**: Remove all references and handling of `SelectorTrace` objects.
            *   Remove `from src.models.selector import SelectorTrace`.
            *   In `PolicyCoordinator.choose_action`:
                *   Remove `selector_traces = self.rule_engine.latest_selector_traces()`.
                *   Remove `self._last_debug_artifacts = self._attach_selector_trace(...)`.
                *   Update `self._write_rule_debug_artifacts` call to remove the `selector_traces` argument.
            *   In `PolicyCoordinator._write_rule_debug_artifacts`:
                *   Remove the `selector_traces: list[SelectorTrace]` parameter.
                *   Remove the call to `self._write_selector_trace`.
                *   Update the `ModelDebugArtifacts` creation, setting `selector_trace_artifact_path` to `None`.
            *   Remove the entire `PolicyCoordinator._write_selector_trace` static method.
            *   Remove the entire `PolicyCoordinator._attach_selector_trace` method.
            *   **Note to `PolicyRuleEngine` owner**: The `PolicyRuleEngine` (upstream source of `SelectorTrace`) must be refactored to *not* produce or rely on selector information, adhering to the "vision-only" principle.

2.  **P99 Latency Reduction: Optimize MemoryStore I/O**
    *   **Reasoning**: `self.memory_store.get_hints` (in `_get_hints`) and `self.memory_store.get_episode` (in `_try_episode_hint`) are synchronous calls that may involve blocking disk I/O (e.g., JSONL reads). This is a P99 latency hotspot, especially if these calls block the main inference thread.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Function**: `PolicyCoordinator._get_hints`, `PolicyCoordinator._try_episode_hint`
        *   **Action**:
            *   Modify these methods to use asynchronous I/O (`await self.memory_store.get_hints(...)`, `await self.memory_store.get_episode(...)`) if the `MemoryStore` interface can be made asynchronous.
            *   Enhance the in-memory caching beyond the single-step cache. Implement a more persistent, multi-step or benchmark-scoped cache for frequently accessed hints/episodes within the `MemoryStore` itself, potentially pre-loading on `reset_run_context`.

3.  **P99 Latency Reduction: Reduce Sequential LLM Calls in Validation**
    *   **Reasoning**: The `_confirm_success`, `_reject_premature_stop`, and `_reject_hallucinated_target` methods can each trigger *additional, sequential* LLM calls (`self.delegate.choose_action`). This significantly increases P99 latency for inference paths that require these validation/re-planning steps.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Functions**: `PolicyCoordinator.choose_action`, `PolicyCoordinator._confirm_success`, `PolicyCoordinator._reject_premature_stop`, `PolicyCoordinator._reject_hallucinated_target`
        *   **Action**:
            *   **For `_confirm_success`**: Introduce a confidence threshold for rule-based `STOP` decisions. If the `PolicyRuleEngine` provides high confidence, skip the LLM confirmation. Alternatively, explore using a much faster, smaller local model for confirmation, or run the confirmation prompt in parallel with the main LLM call and merge results based on confidence/criteria.
            *   **For `_reject_premature_stop` and `_reject_hallucinated_target`**:
                *   **Proactive Hinting**: Instead of reactive re-planning, identify potential failure modes (e.g., initial STOP, hallucinated IDs) *before* the initial `delegate.choose_action`. Inject preemptive "correction" hints into the initial LLM prompt to guide it toward a correct first decision, thereby reducing the need for a second LLM call. For hallucinated targets, proactively provide the list of `known_ids` in the LLM prompt.
                *   **Fast-path re-planning**: If a re-plan is unavoidable, consider using a faster, smaller LLM or a more constrained prompt for the re-planning step to reduce latency compared to a full `delegate.choose_action`.

4.  **Structural Idempotency: Debug Artifact Writing**
    *   **Reasoning**: While `bg_writer.enqueue` offloads the I/O, if `PolicyCoordinator.choose_action` is retried due to a transient failure (e.g., LLM error), `_write_rule_debug_artifacts` could be called multiple times for the "same logical step." The current `step_dir / "..."` approach might overwrite previous debug artifacts from a failed attempt of the same step, losing valuable debugging information.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Function**: `PolicyCoordinator._write_rule_debug_artifacts`
        *   **Action**: Modify the artifact path generation to include a unique identifier for each *attempt* or *retry* within a logical step (e.g., `policy_prompt_attempt_1.txt`, `policy_prompt_attempt_2.txt`). This ensures that retrying `choose_action` preserves debug artifacts from all attempts for a given logical step.

5.  **Agentic Feature: Dynamic Recalibration for Episode Replay**
    *   **Reasoning**: The current `_try_episode_hint` simply deactivates episode replay after `max_deviations`. A more robust agentic feature would attempt to recover or re-synchronize, increasing resilience and adaptability.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Function**: `PolicyCoordinator._try_episode_hint`
        *   **Action**: Instead of deactivating replay on deviation, implement a "fuzzy matching" or re-synchronization logic. Attempt to find the current `perception` within a window of subsequent episode steps. If a match is found, reset `current_step_index` to the re-synchronized point. If a re-sync isn't immediately possible, consider prompting the LLM (or a faster local model) for a "bridging action" to get back on track with the intended episode trajectory.

6.  **Agentic Feature: Adaptive Re-planning based on Failure History**
    *   **Reasoning**: The `_reject_premature_stop` and `_reject_hallucinated_target` provide generic correction hints. A more agentic approach would learn from past rejections and adapt its re-planning strategy or initial policy generation.
    *   **Actionable Task**:
        *   **File**: `src/agent/policy_coordinator.py`
        *   **Functions**: `PolicyCoordinator._reject_premature_stop`, `PolicyCoordinator._reject_hallucinated_target`
        *   **Action**:
            *   Integrate a mechanism to track the frequency and types of rejections (e.g., "premature STOP on login page," "hallucinated ID for button X").
            *   Use this accumulated knowledge to dynamically adjust the hints provided (e.g., if "premature STOP" is common for an intent, add a stronger, more specific warning upfront).
            *   For persistent issues (e.g., repeatedly hallucinating a specific element type), trigger an automatic "meta-learning" process (e.g., generate synthetic training data for LLM fine-tuning or suggest new explicit rules for `PolicyRuleEngine`) to prevent recurrence.

## `src\agent\policy_rules.py`

            *   Define `_SITE_QUALIFIER_REGEX = re.compile(r"\s+on\s+\w[\w.]*$", flags=re.IGNORECASE)` at the module level.

        *   **Action**: Optimize `_submit_button` to avoid repeated `DeterministicTargetSelector` instantiation.

            *   Update `_search_query_rule` to read from and write to this structured state, ensuring clearer, more robust idempotency across state transitions.

        *   **Action**: Implement adaptive `_NO_PROGRESS_REPEAT_THRESHOLD`.
