This could involve tracking `state.run_id`-specific thresholds.
        *   **Action**: Enhance "stuck" detection for `_dismiss_blocking_overlay_rule`.
            *   Extend the "stuck signal" in `_dismiss_blocking_overlay_rule` to include perception similarity. Specifically, if `state.action_history` shows a sequence of *different* actions (or repeated actions whose targets change slightly) but `perception.summary` or a higher-level visual hash of the screen remains effectively identical for N steps, consider this a "stuck" state. This requires an external perception similarity metric to be available.
        *   **Action**: Implement proactive search input activation.
            *   Within `_search_query_rule` or a new primitive, if `state.intent` clearly indicates a search task and no direct search input or trigger is visible, introduce a rule to attempt common keyboard shortcuts (e.g., pressing `/` key) to reveal a hidden search bar. This demonstrates a more proactive, explorative agent behavior.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Invariant Check**: **No DOM/selectors**
        *   **Status**: Compliant within this module, *assuming* `src.models.perception.UIElement` and `src.agent.selector.DeterministicTargetSelector` are implemented purely using vision-derived data and do not internally access or rely on the DOM or traditional HTML selectors. The use of `element_id` is acceptable as a unique visual identifier.
        *   **Action**: No action required in this module based on this assumption.
    *   **Invariant Check**: **Atomic focus+type**
        *   **Status**: **VIOLATION.** The current implementation explicitly separates focus (`ActionType.CLICK`) from typing (`ActionType.TYPE`). Operon's invariant implies that a `TYPE` action on a `target_element_id` should inherently include the necessary focus operation as a single, atomic step.
        *   **Action**: **CRITICAL REFACTORING.**
            *   **File**: `src\agent\policy_rules.py`, `_avoid_identical_type_retry`
                *   Remove the explicit `_click_decision` call for re-establishing focus. The `TYPE` action issued by the agent's executor should guarantee focus acquisition on the `target_element_id` before typing.
            *   **File**: `src\agent\policy_rules.py`, `_search_query_rule`
                *   Remove the explicit `_click_decision` call to focus the search input. The `TYPE` action for the search input should implicitly handle acquiring focus as part of its execution.
            *   **File**: `src\agent\policy_rules.py`, `_click_decision`
                *   Review and deprecate or restrict the use of `_click_decision` for the sole purpose of focusing an input field. Ensure its usage is limited to actual click interactions.
            *   **External Impact (Note for AI assistant)**: This refactoring implies that the `AgentAction` execution layer (outside this module) must be updated to ensure `ActionType.TYPE` reliably focuses its `target_element_id` before typing.
    *   **Invariant Check**: **Visual servo**
        *   **Status**: Compliant. The use of `x`, `y`, `width`, `height` to calculate a click centroid (`x + max(1, width // 2), y + max(1, height // 2)`) is consistent with visual servoing principles.
        *   **Action**: No action required.

## `src\agent\recovery.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Reduce P99 latency for real-time inference**

*   **Task 1.1: Refactor `_retry_key` string construction for performance.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._retry_key`
    *   **Description:** The current string concatenation, while generally efficient, could be optimized for very long `target_text` values by using a more performant string builder or by directly hashing components if `target_text` is frequently extremely long. For Operon's low-level nature, even minor string overheads can aggregate. Consider if a tuple of components could serve as a dictionary key directly instead of a combined string.
    *   **Action:** Profile `_retry_key` with typical and worst-case `target_text` lengths. If performance is a concern, consider replacing f-string concatenation with `"".join()` or using a tuple of key components as the dictionary key to avoid repeated string re-allocations for long strings.
*   **Task 1.2: Evaluate `retry_after_ms` delays against P99 latency goals.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._ladder_decision`
    *   **Description:** The fixed `retry_after_ms` values (500, 1000, 1500) directly contribute to task P99 latency. While strategic, these delays could be dynamic. For critical paths or known fast-recovery scenarios, these delays might be too long.
    *   **Action:** Introduce a mechanism (e.g., configuration, learned policy) to dynamically adjust `retry_after_ms` based on the specific `FailureCategory`, `LoopStage`, or even historical performance data. This might involve a faster "hot path" for transient errors that don't warrant significant delays.

**2. Identify opportunities for structural idempotency**

*   **Task 2.1: Clarify and enforce `recover` call semantics.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover`
    *   **Description:** The `state.retry_counts` mechanism relies on `recover` being called *exactly once* per action-verification cycle for a given `retry_key`. Multiple calls without an intervening action would incorrectly increment retry counts, leading to premature escalation.
    *   **Action:** Add a clear docstring to `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover` explicitly stating this expectation. Consider if the `retry_counts` should be managed internally by `RecoveryManager` rather than being part of the broader `AgentState` if `AgentState` can be snapshot-ed or re-evaluated multiple times without action execution.
*   **Task 2.2: Ensure `_retry_key` stability and granularity.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._retry_key`
    *   **Description:** The `_retry_key` determines if a failure is "the same" for retry purposes. Ensure its components (`active_subgoal`, `target`, `suffix`) are sufficiently granular to differentiate distinct failure contexts, yet stable enough to group genuine repeated failures. The current design seems robust, but it's a critical point for idempotency of retry counting.
    *   **Action:** Review scenarios where two logically distinct failures might generate the same key, or logically similar failures generate different keys. No immediate code change, but keep this in mind for future failure modes.

**3. Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Adaptive Recovery Parameters.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover`, `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._ladder_decision`
    *   **Description:** The `MAX_RECOVERY_ATTEMPTS` and `retry_after_ms` values are static. An agent could learn optimal values based on task history, current environment stability, or specific `FailureCategory`.
    *   **Action:** Introduce a mechanism (e.g., a learned model, a lookup table) to make `MAX_RECOVERY_ATTEMPTS` and `retry_after_ms` dynamic. For instance, a `FailureCategory.NETWORK_ERROR` might get a longer `retry_after_ms` but fewer `MAX_RECOVERY_ATTEMPTS` before a `SESSION_RESET`.
*   **Task 3.2: Integrate Proactive Diagnostics into Recovery.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover`
    *   **Description:** Before simply escalating strategies, the agent could perform lightweight diagnostics based on the `VerificationResult` to better understand the root cause. For example, if `VerificationFailureType.ACTION_FAILED` with `EXECUTION_TARGET_NOT_FOUND`, it could trigger a visual re-scan for similar targets.
    *   **Action:** Introduce a diagnostic step or module that `recover` can invoke conditionally. This diagnostic would run specific, low-latency checks (e.g., screenshot analysis for specific UI elements, network connectivity check) and provide additional context or suggest an optimal recovery strategy beyond the fixed ladder.
*   **Task 3.3: Develop Learned/Adaptive Escalation Policies.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._ladder_decision`
    *   **Description:** The current ladder (RETRY_SAME, RETRY_DIFFERENT_TACTIC, CONTEXT_RESET, SESSION_RESET) is fixed. A truly agentic system could use an ML model or a sophisticated policy to determine the *most effective* next recovery strategy based on current `AgentState`, `PolicyDecision`, `ExecutedAction`, `VerificationResult`, and historical success rates for similar failures.
    *   **Action:** Replace the fixed `if/elif` ladder logic in `_ladder_decision` with an extensible policy mechanism (e.g., a strategy pattern, a small decision tree, or a reinforcement learning agent) that selects the `RecoveryStrategy` and `retry_after_ms` more intelligently.
*   **Task 3.4: Implement Meta-Recovery and Dynamic Task Re-planning.**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover` (specifically when `MAX_RECOVERY_ATTEMPTS` is reached)
    *   **Description:** When `MAX_RECOVERY_ATTEMPTS` is reached, the agent simply stops. A more agentic approach would involve attempting to dynamically re-plan the remaining task or escalate to a higher-level task manager for re-evaluation. This is true self-healing beyond a single step.
    *   **Action:** When a terminal `RecoveryDecision` is made due to `RETRY_LIMIT_REACHED`, instead of just stopping, trigger a higher-level `TaskReplan` or `EscalateToHuman` event. This would involve a new `RecoveryStrategy` type and corresponding handling in the main agent loop.

**4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo**

*   **Task 4.1: Eliminate `action.selector` usage (Violation: No DOM/selectors).**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._retry_key`
    *   **Description:** The line `f"selector:{action.selector}" if action.selector is not None` directly violates Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant. The agent must not interact with DOM selectors.
    *   **Action:** Remove any logic that uses `action.selector`. If a target needs to be identified for a retry key, it must be based purely on visual information (e.g., visual hash, region coordinates, OCR'd text).
*   **Task 4.2: Clarify/Refactor `action.target_element_id` origin (Potential Violation: No DOM/selectors).**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/recovery.py`
    *   **Function:** `RuleBasedRecoveryManager._retry_key`, `RuleBasedRecoveryManager.recover`
    *   **Description:** The use of `action.target_element_id` (`f"id:{action.target_element_id}"`) is highly suspicious given the "no DOM/selectors" invariant. While `id` *could* theoretically be derived visually (e.g., OCR of an element's attribute in a screenshot), it is typically a DOM-level abstraction. If this `id` originates from any DOM inspection, it's a violation. Similarly, the line `target = decision.action.target_element_id or "input"` in `recover` relies on this ID.
    *   **Action:** Investigate the source of `action.target_element_id`. If it is derived from DOM inspection, it must be replaced with a purely visual identifier (e.g., a visual hash of the element's appearance, its centroid coordinates, or an OCR'd label). If it is already a visual abstraction, document this explicitly within the `Action` model or relevant data flow to ensure compliance.

## `src\agent\reflector.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to reduce P99 latency for real-time inference

*   **Task 1.1: src\agent\reflector.py - `PostRunReflector.reflect` - Integrate Real-time Anomaly Detection**
    *   **Description**: The current reflection process is purely post-run. To significantly reduce P99 latency in real-time inference, crucial pattern detections (e.g., `_detect_repeated_key_press`, `_detect_stuck_subgoal`, `_detect_no_screen_change_actions`) should be migrated or mirrored into a real-time anomaly detection component. This component would operate on the live stream of `EpisodeStep`s, allowing for immediate policy adjustments or interventions *during* a run, preventing prolonged unproductive sequences that contribute to high P99.
    *   **Action**: Create a new module (e.g., `src/agent/realtime_detector.py`) that implements the logic of the identified pattern detection methods. This new module should maintain state across live steps and emit immediate warnings or trigger policy fallbacks when patterns are detected, rather than waiting for a run to complete. The `PostRunReflector` can then focus on higher-level, more computationally intensive analysis not suitable for real-time.
*   **Task 1.2: src\agent\reflector.py - `PostRunReflector.reflect` - Asynchronous Memory Writes**
    *   **Description**: Memory records and episodes are written synchronously at the end of `reflect`. While `reflect` itself is post-run, contention or latency in `MemoryStore` operations could impact the readiness of learning artifacts for subsequent runs, or if other components concurrently access the memory store.
    *   **Action**: Modify the calls to `self.memory_store._append_record(record)` and `self.memory_store.save_episode(episode)` to be asynchronous operations (e.g., using a background thread pool, an event queue, or `asyncio` if the `MemoryStore` supports it). This ensures the `reflect` method itself completes quickly, and memory persistence doesn't block other potential system operations.
*   **Task 1.3: src\agent\reflector.py - `_extract_episode` - Optimize Episode Structure for Real-time Retrieval**
    *   **Description**: Episodes are saved to the `MemoryStore`. If real-time inference relies on quickly retrieving relevant episodes for few-shot learning or policy guidance, the current `Episode` structure (especially a potentially large `steps` list) and its storage might not be optimal for fast lookups.
    *   **Action**: Evaluate the `Episode` model and how `MemoryStore` retrieves and indexes episodes. Consider creating an `EpisodeSummary` model or pre-indexing key fields (e.g., `normalized_intent`, `benchmark`, `action_type`, `page_hint`, `target_description`) for quicker retrieval of high-level information or for semantic search without needing to load the entire episode's step details.

### 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

*   **Task 2.1: src\agent\reflector.py - `PostRunReflector.reflect` - Ensure Idempotent Memory Record Storage**
    *   **Description**: The `self.memory_store._append_record(record)` call appends memory records. If `reflect` is called multiple times for the same `run_id` (e.g., due to retry logic or reprocessing), it will create duplicate `MemoryRecord` entries for the same detected patterns from the same run.
    *   **Action**: Modify the `MemoryStore._append_record` method (or introduce an `upsert_record` method) to ensure that `MemoryRecord`s are uniquely identified and updated rather than simply appended. A reasonable unique key for a pattern detected in a specific run could be a combination of `pattern.pattern_key` and `pattern.source_run_id`, or a hash of relevant `MemoryRecord` fields if content-based uniqueness is desired.
*   **Task 2.2: src\agent\reflector.py - `_extract_episode` - Clarify Episode Saving Idempotency**
    *   **Description**: The `self.memory_store.save_episode(episode)` call relies on the `MemoryStore` to handle idempotency. `Episode.episode_id` is set to `run_id`. This strongly implies that if `save_episode` is called again for the same `run_id`, the existing episode should be updated/overwritten. This behavior should be explicitly confirmed and documented within `MemoryStore.save_episode`.
    *   **Action**: Add a comment or assertion within `PostRunReflector.reflect` or `MemoryStore.save_episode` to explicitly state that `save_episode` is idempotent for a given `episode_id`. If `MemoryStore` currently appends or creates new entries without overwriting for the same `episode_id`, modify `MemoryStore.save_episode` to upsert based on `episode_id`.

### 3. Agentic features not present in standard workflow engines

*   **Task 3.1: src\agent\reflector.py - `ReflectionPattern` - Elevate `suggested_action` to Structured Policy Hint**
    *   **Description**: The `suggested_action` in `ReflectionPattern` is currently a free-form string. To enable true agentic self-healing and adaptive policy, this suggestion needs to be actionable directly by the policy engine, not just a human reader.
    *   **Action**: Replace `suggested_action: str` with a structured `suggested_policy: PolicyHint` object (e.g., defined in `src/models/policy_hint.py`). This `PolicyHint` could contain specific, machine-interpretable directives like `preferred_action_type`, `avoid_context_regex`, `retry_strategy`, `subgoal_transition_rule`, or a callable mini-program/guardrail that the real-time policy can interpret and integrate into its decision-making.
*   **Task 3.2: src\agent\reflector.py - `PostRunReflector.reflect` - Implement Dynamic Policy Update/Correction**
    *   **Description**: `MemoryRecord`s are currently stored but not actively used to *modify* the agent's real-time behavior. A truly agentic feature would be to automatically integrate these learnings into the policy engine or its prompt construction for future runs.
    *   **Action**: After generating `MemoryRecord`s, develop a mechanism to push these structured `PolicyHint`s (from Task 3.1) to an active policy engine (e.g., a "PolicyUpdater" module). This updater could dynamically adjust policy parameters, inject new rules, or modify prompt templates used for the next inference cycle, effectively "patching" the agent's behavior to avoid previously identified failure patterns.
*   **Task 3.3: src\agent\reflector.py - `ReflectionPattern` - Introduce Adaptive Confidence Calibration**
    *   **Description**: The `confidence` field in `ReflectionPattern` is currently a fixed calculation based on streak length. An agentic system would continuously evaluate the effectiveness of its reflections and dynamically adjust confidence scores.
    *   **Action**: Implement a feedback loop that tracks whether subsequent runs, after policy adjustments based on a `ReflectionPattern` or `MemoryRecord`, successfully avoid the detected pattern or improve performance. Update the `confidence` score of the `MemoryRecord` (and thus the underlying `ReflectionPattern` type) based on this measured impact, allowing the agent to learn *which types of reflections and suggestions are most valuable*.
*   **Task 3.4: src\agent\reflector.py - `PostRunReflector.reflect` - Proactive Success Reinforcement**
    *   **Description**: The current reflection primarily focuses on identifying failure patterns (`MemoryOutcome.FAILURE`). An advanced agent should also identify and reinforce successful, efficient behaviors to optimize policy.
    *   **Action**: Introduce new pattern detection methods (e.g., `_detect_efficient_subgoal_transitions`, `_detect_effective_tool_use`, `_detect_optimal_action_sequences`) that analyze successful one-shot steps and highly efficient trajectories. Generate `MemoryRecord`s with `outcome=MemoryOutcome.SUCCESS` to explicitly reinforce good patterns, providing a balanced learning signal for policy optimization and "best practice" encoding.

### 4. Violations of Operon's invariants

*   **Task 4.1: src\agent\reflector.py - `_detect_taskbar_clicking` - Refine Vision-Only Taskbar Detection**
    *   **Description**: The use of a hardcoded `_TASKBAR_Y_THRESHOLD = 1000` for taskbar detection, while leveraging a visual `y` coordinate, represents a fixed abstraction that might not be robust across varying screen resolutions, scaling, or future UI designs. Operon aims for "zero-abstraction" guided by vision.
    *   **Action**: Enhance the taskbar detection to rely purely on dynamic visual pattern recognition rather than fixed pixel thresholds. This could involve leveraging a dedicated visual model or UI element recognition system to identify the taskbar region dynamically (e.g., based on its visual characteristics like icon density, background color, or common UI patterns) to inform action analysis more robustly, aligning more strictly with a "vision-only, zero-abstraction" principle.
*   **Task 4.2: src\agent\reflector.py - General - Confirm `visible_elements` and `page_hint` are DOM-Free**
    *   **Description**: This module consumes `visible_elements` (with `element_id`, `primary_name`) and `PageHint` from the `perception` object. Operon's invariant states "no DOM/selectors." While this module itself doesn't introduce DOM abstractions, it relies on upstream components to provide this data without violating the invariant.
    *   **Action**: Review the upstream `Perception` generation process to explicitly confirm that `visible_elements` and `page_hint` are derived *exclusively* from visual analysis (e.g., advanced OCR, object detection, UI element segmentation, layout understanding) and do not involve any underlying DOM tree parsing, accessibility tree inspection, or selector generation at any stage. If this cannot be definitively confirmed, it indicates a critical invariant violation in the upstream `Perception` component that would indirectly affect `Reflector`'s adherence to Operon's principles.

## `src\agent\screen_diff.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to reduce P99 latency for real-time inference:**

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize pixel comparison in `compute_screen_change_ratio`**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_screen_change_ratio`
    *   **Action:** Replace the Python generator expression for pixel comparison (`sum(1 for a, b in zip(before_data, after_data) if abs(a - b) > _PIXEL_DIFF_THRESHOLD)`) with a NumPy-based vectorized operation. Convert `before_data` and `after_data` to `np.uint8` NumPy arrays after `tobytes()` and before comparison to leverage faster native array operations.
    *   **Rationale:** Python loops for pixel-level comparisons are significantly slower than vectorized NumPy operations, especially for larger resolutions.
*   **Task 1.2: Evaluate and potentially optimize image resizing interpolation in `compute_screen_change_ratio`**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_screen_change_ratio`
    *   **Action:** Change `Image.LANCZOS` to a faster interpolation method such as `Image.BILINEAR` or `Image.NEAREST` within the `resize` calls. Perform a qualitative assessment to ensure the change detection effectiveness at the low resolution (`_COMPARE_WIDTH`, `_COMPARE_HEIGHT`) is not unacceptably degraded.
    *   **Rationale:** `LANCZOS` is a high-quality but computationally intensive interpolation filter. For mere change detection at low resolution, a faster method might be sufficient and reduce CPU cycles.
*   **Task 1.3: Enable in-memory image input for `compute_screen_change_ratio`**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_screen_change_ratio`
    *   **Action:** Overload or create an alternative function (e.g., `compute_screen_change_ratio_from_pil`) that accepts `PIL.Image.Image` objects directly instead of file paths. This would eliminate disk I/O latency when screenshots are already available in memory (e.g., from a frame buffer capture).
    *   **Rationale:** Disk I/O is a significant source of latency. Avoiding it by processing in-memory data directly is crucial for real-time inference.
*   **Task 1.4: Pre-process BGR frames for `compute_temporal_saliency`**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_temporal_saliency`
    *   **Action:** Add a comment or docstring clarification that input `frames` should ideally be provided at an optimized resolution (e.g., similar to `_COMPARE_WIDTH`, `_COMPARE_HEIGHT` used elsewhere) to minimize computation within the function. If higher-resolution frames are commonly passed, consider adding an optional downsampling step at the beginning of the function (e.g., using `cv2.resize` if OpenCV is an allowed dependency, or `PIL.Image.fromarray().resize()`) to reduce the size of arrays processed by NumPy.
    *   **Rationale:** Processing unnecessarily large frames in NumPy, even with vectorized operations, consumes more CPU and memory bandwidth.

**2. Opportunities for structural idempotency:**

*   **Task 2.1: Document inherent idempotency and upstream requirements**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Functions:** `compute_screen_change_ratio`, `compute_temporal_saliency`
    *   **Action:** Add a docstring note to both functions explicitly stating that they are referentially transparent (pure functions) and thus inherently idempotent. Recommend that any upstream processes generating the input `before_path`, `after_path` files, or `frames` ensure these inputs represent stable, immutable states for consistent results across retries or re-evaluations.
    *   **Rationale:** While the functions themselves are pure, their utility in a larger system relies on the consistency of their inputs for full idempotency of the overall workflow.

**3. Suggest agentic features not present in standard workflow engines:**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement adaptive thresholding for screen change detection**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_screen_change_ratio`
    *   **Action:** Modify `compute_screen_change_ratio` to accept optional `thresholds` (e.g., `screen_change_threshold`, `cursor_only_threshold`, `pixel_diff_threshold`) as parameters. If not provided, default to the existing constants.
    *   **Rationale:** This allows a higher-level agent to dynamically adjust sensitivity based on the current task (e.g., detect subtle text changes vs. wait for a major UI overhaul), historical context, or learned parameters, enabling more nuanced and robust visual perception.
*   **Task 3.2: Implement adaptive thresholding for temporal saliency classification**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Function:** `compute_temporal_saliency`
    *   **Action:** Modify `compute_temporal_saliency` to accept optional `velocity_thresholds` (e.g., `velocity_hung`, `velocity_spinner`, `cv_spinner_threshold`) as parameters. If not provided, default to the existing constants.
    *   **Rationale:** Similar to screen change, dynamic adjustment of these thresholds allows the agent to contextually classify motion (e.g., differentiate a "spinner" from a "progressing" state more accurately for different types of UI animations or during specific waiting periods).
*   **Task 3.3: Enhance `TemporalSaliencyResult` with predictive metrics**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Class:** `TemporalSaliencyResult`
    *   **Action:** Add fields to `TemporalSaliencyResult` such as `velocity_trend` (e.g., "increasing", "decreasing", "stable"), and potentially `stability_confidence`.
    *   **Rationale:** This provides more sophisticated signals to a self-healing agent. A "progressing" state with a "decreasing" velocity trend might signal an impending stall or completion, allowing the agent to anticipate and prepare for the next action or trigger a recovery if progress stops unexpectedly. `stability_confidence` can help the agent decide how long to wait before declaring a screen stable or stuck.

**4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants:**

*   **Task 4.1: Confirm compliance with Operon's invariants**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\screen_diff.py`
    *   **Action:** No changes are required.
    *   **Rationale:** The module strictly adheres to Operon's invariants: it operates purely on pixel data (`PIL.Image`, `numpy` arrays) without relying on DOM, selectors, or abstract UI elements. Its outputs (pixel change ratios, motion classifications) directly support a visual servo paradigm and do not imply or require non-atomic focus/type operations. **No violations found.**

## `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task 1.1: Decouple encoding from `stop()` return.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.stop`
        *   **Action**: Modify `stop()` to initiate the `_encode` process as an independent background task (e.g., using `asyncio.create_task` for a fire-and-forget approach or adding it to a dedicated low-priority task queue). This allows `stop()` to return almost immediately, freeing the main agent loop to continue without waiting for video encoding completion.
        *   **Justification**: The current `await asyncio.to_thread(self._encode)` blocks the calling async context, contributing to P99 latency if the agent needs immediate response after signaling the end of a recording. Encoding can be a long-running operation.
    *   **Task 1.2: Implement on-the-fly streaming encoding.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder._capture_loop`, `ScreenRecorder._encode` (refactor into a streaming pipeline)
        *   **Action**: Refactor the recording mechanism to encode frames directly as they are captured, rather than buffering all frames in memory and then encoding in a batch. This typically involves a producer-consumer pattern (e.g., a queue between `_capture_loop` and an encoding worker thread/process).
        *   **Justification**: Reduces memory footprint (`_frames` buffer) and amortizes the encoding cost across the capture duration, making the `stop()` operation nearly instantaneous as frames are already mostly processed. This is critical for systems where recording duration or resolution might increase.
    *   **Task 1.3: Explore hardware acceleration for video encoding.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder._encode`
        *   **Action**: Investigate and implement hardware-accelerated video encoding options within OpenCV's `VideoWriter` (e.g., `CAP_FFMPEG` backend with appropriate codecs like `h264_nvenc` for NVIDIA GPUs or `h264_qsv` for Intel Quick Sync) if the underlying system supports them. This may require specific OpenCV builds or environment configurations.
        *   **Justification**: Significantly reduces CPU utilization and encoding time for `_encode`, further lowering P99 latency for the encoding process itself.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task 2.1: Ensure `start()` is idempotent against multiple calls.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.start`
        *   **Action**: Add a check at the beginning of `start()` to verify if a capture thread is already active (`if self._thread is not None and self._thread.is_alive():`). If so, log a warning and return immediately without starting a new thread.
        *   **Justification**: Calling `start()` multiple times without an intervening `stop()` currently orphans previous threads and overwrites `self._thread`, leading to unexpected behavior and resource leaks.
    *   **Task 2.2: Enhance `stop()` robustness and idempotency.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.stop`
        *   **Action**: Refine the `stop()` method to gracefully handle scenarios where `self._thread` might already be `None` or the thread has already terminated. Ensure `join` is only called if `self._thread` is not `None` and `self._thread.is_alive()`. The `_frames = []` call in `finally` is already idempotent and should remain.
        *   **Justification**: Allows `stop()` to be called safely multiple times without error, improving the reliability of agent workflows that might redundantly signal stop.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features**
    *   **Task 3.1: Implement a circular buffer for retrospective recording.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.__init__`, `ScreenRecorder._capture_loop`, new `save_last_n_seconds` method.
        *   **Action**: Replace `self._frames: list[np.ndarray]` with a fixed-size `collections.deque` (or similar circular buffer implementation). Frames are added to the buffer, and older frames are automatically discarded. Add a new `save_last_n_seconds(output_path: Path)` method that copies the frames from the circular buffer and encodes them.
        *   **Justification**: Enables the Operon agent to continuously "observe" without constantly writing to disk. When an interesting event, error, or decision point occurs, the agent can retrospectively save a clip of the preceding moments, crucial for self-healing, post-mortem analysis, or training data generation, without the overhead of continuous disk writes.
    *   **Task 3.2: Allow dynamic adjustment of capture parameters.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.__init__`, `ScreenRecorder._capture_loop`, new `set_capture_params` method.
        *   **Action**: Modify `_CAPTURE_SCALE` and `fps` to be instance attributes that can be updated dynamically via a new `set_capture_params(scale: float | None = None, fps: int | None = None)` method. The `_capture_loop` should read these parameters dynamically rather than relying solely on `__init__` values. Handle potential thread safety for parameter updates.
        *   **Justification**: An Operon agent, based on its current task, environmental complexity, or system load (inferred visually or via internal metrics), can adapt the quality and frequency of its visual input. For example, higher FPS/resolution for critical, fast-moving UI elements, lower for static background tasks.
    *   **Task 3.3: Implement Region-of-Interest (ROI) capture.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.__init__`, `ScreenRecorder._capture_loop`
        *   **Action**: Extend `ScreenRecorder` to accept a `monitor` or `bounding_box` parameter during initialization or dynamically. Modify `_capture_loop` to use `sct.grab(bounding_box)` instead of `sct.monitors[0]`.
        *   **Justification**: Reduces the amount of raw pixel data captured and processed, focusing the agent's "vision" on relevant areas. This directly reduces memory, CPU load, and I/O, improving efficiency and potentially inference speed by providing more relevant input.
    *   **Task 3.4: Enhance error reporting for self-healing workflows.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Function**: `ScreenRecorder.stop`, `ScreenRecorder._capture_loop`
        *   **Action**: Instead of merely logging and returning `None` on failure in `stop()` and silently stopping in `_capture_loop` (e.g., if `mss` itself fails), consider propagating specific exceptions (e.g., `RecordingError`, `EncodingError`) or emitting structured events. The main agent loop can then implement specific recovery strategies (e.g., retry, switch capture method, notify user).
        *   **Justification**: Enables the Operon agent to intelligently detect and respond to failures within its visual capture pipeline, moving beyond passive logging to active self-healing or adaptive behavior.

4.  **Flag any Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Task 4.1: Confirm adherence to Operon invariants.**
        *   **File**: `src\agent\screen_recorder.py`
        *   **Action**: Review the module against Operon's invariants:
            *   `no DOM/selectors`: **No violation.** The module exclusively uses `mss` for raw pixel data capture and `cv2` for image processing/encoding, without any interaction with DOM, accessibility trees, or UI selectors.
            *   `atomic focus+type`: **No violation.** This module is purely for screen capture and does not involve input events (focus, type).
            *   `visual servo`: **No violation.** This module *provides* the visual data necessary for visual servoing. While the current batch encoding can introduce latency for *retrospective* analysis, the `_capture_loop` delivers frames at the specified FPS, which can be accessed for real-time visual servoing if a live frame access mechanism were added (see Task 1.4). The module itself does not perform the servoing.
        *   **Justification**: The module's design aligns well with Operon's core principles by providing raw, visual-only input.

## `src\agent\selector.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. P99 Latency Reduction for Real-time Inference**

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize `_label_like_text_candidates` and `_visual_groups` calls in `reresolve` method.**
    *   **Description:** The `reresolve` method currently recomputes `text_candidates` and `visual_groups` in each of its `_run_attempt` calls. These are relatively expensive operations involving iterating and sorting `perception.visible_elements`.
    *   **Action:** Modify `DeterministicTargetSelector.reresolve` to precompute `text_candidates` and `visual_groups` once at the beginning of the method. Pass these precomputed values to both the initial and recovery `_run_attempt` calls using the `text_candidates` and `visual_groups` arguments.
    *   **Justification:** Eliminates redundant computations across multiple selection attempts within the same `reresolve` flow, reducing overall latency.

*   **Task 1.2: Implement caching for normalized text and tokenized sets in UIElement and TargetIntent models.**
    *   **Description:** Methods like `_normalize_text`, `_tokenize`, and `_token_overlap` are frequently called within scoring logic. These operations often re-process the same string attributes of `UIElement` objects (e.g., `primary_name`, `label`, `text`, `element_id`) and `TargetIntent` objects (e.g., `target_text`, `target_role`).
    *   **Action:**
        1.  In `src/models/perception.py::UIElement`, add properties (e.g., using `functools.cached_property`) for cached normalized strings and tokenized sets for attributes like `primary_name`, `label`, `text`, `placeholder`, `name`, `element_id`, and `role`.
        2.  Similarly, in `src/models/selector.py::TargetIntent`, add cached properties for normalized and tokenized versions of `target_text`, `target_role`, and `expected_section`.
        3.  Update all call sites within `src\agent\selector.py` to use these cached properties instead of re-calling `_normalize_text` and `_tokenize` directly on the raw strings.
    *   **Justification:** Significantly reduces redundant string processing and set creation, especially when scoring multiple candidates, by performing these operations only once per attribute per object. This is a major factor in P99 latency for text-heavy comparisons.

*   **Task 1.3: Optimize spatial queries using a spatial indexing data structure.**
    *   **Description:** Spatial relationship checks (e.g., `bbox_distance`, `is_above`, `is_left_of`) are performed frequently within `_best_spatial_match` (iterating `text_candidates` for each `element`) and `_unlabeled_fallback_allowed` (iterating `visible_elements` for each candidate). These nested loops can lead to `O(N*M)` complexity, which becomes a bottleneck in dense UIs.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  At the beginning of `DeterministicTargetSelector._run_attempt` (after `text_candidates` and `visual_groups` are determined), construct a spatial index (e.g., an R-tree or Quadtree) from `perception.visible_elements` and/or `text_candidates`.
        2.  Pass this spatial index into `_score_candidate`.
        3.  Refactor `_best_spatial_match` and `_unlabeled_fallback_allowed` to query this spatial index for nearby elements (e.g., `bbox_distance` neighbors, elements within a certain region) instead of performing linear scans.
    *   **Justification:** A spatial index reduces the complexity of proximity queries from linear scans to logarithmic or sub-linear average time, drastically improving performance for selecting targets in visually complex environments.

*   **Task 1.4: Refactor `_duplicate_name_penalty` and `_unlabeled_fallback_allowed` to leverage precomputed data.**
    *   **Description:** `_duplicate_name_penalty` and `_unlabeled_fallback_allowed` both iterate over `perception.visible_elements` for *each* candidate being scored within `_score_candidate`. This results in `O(N*N)` behavior where N is the number of visible elements/candidates.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  At the beginning of `DeterministicTargetSelector._run_attempt`, precompute a map or set of duplicate `primary_name` occurrences among interactable elements.
        2.  Similarly, pre-evaluate the unlabeled fallback allowance conditions (e.g., identifying singleton compatible elements, potential text label groundings) for all elements or pre-index textual labels for fast lookup.
        3.  Pass these precomputed data structures to `_score_candidate`, allowing `_duplicate_name_penalty` and `_unlabeled_fallback_allowed` to perform lookups rather than full scans.
    *   **Justification:** Eliminates redundant nested iterations, reducing the overall complexity of candidate scoring and contributing to lower P99 latency.

**2. Structural Idempotency**

*   **Task 2.1: Formalize immutability assumption for `UIElement` and `ScreenPerception` models.**
    *   **Description:** For `DeterministicTargetSelector` to be strictly idempotent (producing the same `SelectorResult` for identical `ScreenPerception` and `TargetIntent` inputs), the underlying input models (`ScreenPerception`, `UIElement`, `TargetIntent`) must be immutable. While `dataclass(slots=True)` is used, explicit immutability guarantees are beneficial.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Add `frozen=True` to the `@dataclass` decorator for `src/models/perception.py::UIElement` and `src/models/perception.py::ScreenPerception` (and potentially `src/models/selector.py::TargetIntent` if not already).
        2.  Add docstrings to these model classes explicitly stating that instances are immutable after creation.
    *   **Justification:** Explicitly guarantees that the inputs to the selector (and thereby the selector's internal state for a given call) do not change during or between calls, ensuring that `select` and `reresolve` are structurally idempotent for identical inputs. This aids in predictability, debugging, and potential caching of selector results.

**3. Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement dynamic adjustment of selector parameters based on feedback loops.**
    *   **Description:** The current recovery mechanism uses fixed thresholds (`_RECOVERY_ACCEPTANCE_THRESHOLD`, `_RECOVERY_AMBIGUITY_MARGIN`). An agentic system could learn and adapt these parameters over time.
    *   **Action:** Introduce an external feedback loop mechanism (e.g., a "Selector Policy Learner" module). This mechanism would consume `SelectorTrace` data (including selected element, score margin, failure reasons) along with downstream action outcomes (success/failure). Over time, it would dynamically adjust the `_ACCEPTANCE_THRESHOLD`, `_AMBIGUITY_MARGIN`, `_SPATIAL_CAP`, and possibly other signal weights based on observed performance, pushing these updated parameters to the `_SelectorConfig` for different contexts or `TargetIntent` types.
    *   **Justification:** Enables true self-healing beyond predefined rules. The selector becomes adaptive, learning from its operational experience to improve its performance and robustness in real-world, dynamic UI environments without manual tuning.

*   **Task 3.2: Introduce proactive ambiguity resolution / disambiguation requests.**
    *   **Description:** When `FailureCategory.AMBIGUOUS_TARGET_CANDIDATES` occurs, the selector currently fails. An agentic system could proactively seek clarification or use other strategies to resolve ambiguity.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Modify `DeterministicTargetSelector._run_attempt` to return an extended `_AttemptResult` (or `SelectorResult`) when ambiguity is detected. This extended result should include more details about the top ambiguous candidates (e.g., their evidence, bounding boxes).
        2.  Introduce a `SuggestedDisambiguationAction` enum or similar structure within the `SelectorResult` when `AMBIGUOUS_TARGET_CANDIDATES` is the failure reason. This could suggest actions like "request_user_highlight," "try_nlp_context_search," or "evaluate_goal_state_proximity."
        3.  An upstream agentic planner would then interpret this suggestion and execute a strategy to resolve the ambiguity (e.g., render a prompt to the user, activate a different sub-agent).
    *   **Justification:** Moves beyond passive failure to active problem-solving. Instead of just stopping, the agent initiates a process to gain more information or try alternative paths, making the overall system more resilient and capable of handling complex, ambiguous situations.

*   **Task 3.3: Incorporate a "learned attention" mechanism for spatial grounding.**
    *   **Description:** `_SPATIAL_WEIGHTS` are fixed constants. However, the importance of spatial relationships (e.g., label above vs. label left) can vary significantly based on UI element type, context, and overall UI layout.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Introduce a small, context-aware model (e.g., a simple classifier or regression model, potentially trained on human demonstrations or successful past selections) that refines or adjusts spatial weights.
        2.  This model would take `element` and `label` features (types, sizes, positions) as input, along with `intent` context, and output dynamic weighting factors for the `_SPATIAL_WEIGHTS` categories in `_best_spatial_match` or directly estimate the likelihood of a correct spatial match.
        3.  Integrate the output of this model into the scoring logic within `_best_spatial_match` and `_score_candidate`.
    *   **Justification:** Enables a more nuanced and adaptive spatial reasoning. The selector would learn to focus its "visual attention" on the most relevant spatial cues for a given task and UI context, improving accuracy and reducing errors caused by rigid spatial assumptions.

**4. Violations of Operon's Invariants**

*   **Task 4.1: (No Action Required) Confirm adherence to "no DOM/selectors."**
    *   **Description:** Operon strictly prohibits direct DOM interaction or reliance on CSS/XPath selectors.
    *   **Status:** The module adheres to this invariant. It operates solely on `ScreenPerception` and `UIElement` objects, which represent visually observed elements with their bounding boxes and extracted semantic properties (names, labels, text). There is no code that parses or queries a DOM tree, nor any use of CSS or XPath selectors.
    *   **Action:** None.

*   **Task 4.2: (No Action Required) Confirm adherence to "atomic focus+type."**
    *   **Description:** Operon emphasizes atomic, high-fidelity interactions like "focus+type."
    *   **Status:** The module adheres to this invariant. The `DeterministicTargetSelector`'s responsibility is to *identify* the optimal `UIElement` for an action. The actual *execution* of the "focus+type" action, which involves precisely targeting and interacting with the identified element, occurs in a separate, downstream module. This selector provides the necessary input (`UIElement`) for such an atomic action.
    *   **Action:** None.

*   **Task 4.3: (No Action Required) Confirm adherence to "visual servo."**
    *   **Description:** Operon relies on visual feedback for precise control (visual servoing).
    *   **Status:** The module adheres to this invariant. The selector extensively uses geometric functions (`bbox_distance`, `is_above`, `is_left_of`, `same_column`, `same_row`, `horizontal_overlap`) derived from `src.agent.geometry`. These calculations are fundamental for understanding spatial relationships between visually perceived elements, which is critical for a visual servo system to accurately move the cursor or interact.
    *   **Action:** None.

---

## `src\agent\verifier.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **P99 Latency Reduction for Real-time Inference**

    *   **TASK 1.1: Implement cascading verification models.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService._model_verify`
        *   **Action:** Modify `_model_verify` to first attempt verification using a faster, potentially simpler heuristic model or a smaller, fine-tuned LLM (e.g., a "fast critic"). Only if this initial model returns an `UNCERTAIN` status, or explicitly requests more detail/power, should the full `self.gemini_client.generate_verification` (assumed to be a larger, more powerful model) be invoked. This requires modifying the `GeminiClient` interface or implementing a new client abstraction for cascading models.
    *   **TASK 1.2: Implement client-side timeouts for LLM calls.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService._model_verify` (and likely in `src\clients\gemini.py`)
        *   **Action:** Ensure that the `gemini_client.generate_verification` (or `generate_policy`) method is invoked with a configurable, strict timeout. If the timeout is exceeded (e.g., via `asyncio.TimeoutError` or client-specific exception), catch it and return a `VerificationResult` with `status=VerificationStatus.UNCERTAIN`, `failure_type=VerificationFailureType.UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`, and `critic_fallback_reason="critic_timeout"`. This prevents unbounded waits.
    *   **TASK 1.3: Optimize critic prompt for faster LLM inference.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService._render_prompt` and `prompts/critic_prompt.txt`
        *   **Action:** Review and refactor `critic_prompt.txt` (and its rendering logic in `_render_prompt`) to reduce unnecessary verbosity, clarify instructions for the LLM, and potentially add explicit instructions for conciseness or specific output formats (e.g., strict JSON schema adherence). This can lead to faster model responses.

2.  **Structural Idempotency Opportunities**

    *   **TASK 2.1: Formalize idempotency for LLM interaction.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService._model_verify` and `src\clients\gemini.py`
        *   **Action:** Ensure that the `gemini_client`'s underlying API calls are configured for idempotency where possible (e.g., using request IDs if the API supports it). If `_model_verify` were to be retried due to a transient error, ideally the *same* successful LLM response should be returned if the inputs haven't changed. Consider adding a short-term, in-memory memoization layer to `_model_verify` for identical `(state, decision, executed_action)` inputs to avoid redundant LLM calls if the verifier is rapidly re-invoked for the same logical step.
    *   **TASK 2.2: Confirm `_last_debug_artifacts` does not violate idempotency.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService._last_debug_artifacts`
        *   **Action:** Verify that the use of `_last_debug_artifacts` as an instance variable, which holds mutable state, does not lead to race conditions or incorrect debugging data if `verify` were to be called concurrently (e.g., in a multi-threaded context, although unlikely for a single agent loop). For the current single-agent execution model, this is likely acceptable for reporting the *latest* debug artifacts, but be aware if the execution model changes.

3.  **Agentic Features (Self-healing Workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **TASK 3.1: Enhance `VerificationResult` with suggested next actions or remedies.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\models\verification.py` (add field), `src\agent\verifier.py` (`_model_verify`, `_normalize_verification_result`, `_render_prompt`)
        *   **Action:** Add an optional field, e.g., `suggested_remedy: str | None` or `suggested_action_type: ActionType | None`, to the `VerificationResult` model. Modify `critic_prompt.txt` to explicitly instruct the LLM to suggest a corrective action or a next best step when it identifies a failure or uncertainty. Update `_parse_verification_output` and `_normalize_verification_result` to correctly extract and populate this new field from the LLM's response.
    *   **TASK 3.2: Implement proactive stuck-loop detection and remediation suggestions.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService.verify` (or potentially a higher-level loop controller that uses `VerifierService`)
        *   **Action:** Introduce internal state (e.g., `self._consecutive_uncertain_count`, `self._last_perception_hash`) to detect when the agent is consistently receiving `PENDING` or `UNCERTAIN` verification results without significant screen changes. If a threshold of consecutive "stuck" states is reached, the `verify` method should return a `VerificationResult` that includes a recommended recovery action (e.g., `ActionType.REFRESH`, a longer `ActionType.WAIT`, or `ActionType.NAVIGATE` to a known starting point), rather than just the default `UNCERTAIN`.
    *   **TASK 3.3: Introduce dynamic adaptation of verification logic based on failure patterns.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py`, `DeterministicVerifierService.verify`
        *   **Action:** Implement logic to adapt the verification strategy based on recurring failure patterns. For instance, if `VerificationFailureType.PAGE_LOADING` is returned repeatedly, the verifier could dynamically relax the `_is_page_loading` criteria slightly, or conversely, if `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE` is common, it could request more detailed visual analysis from the LLM or prompt a different model. This requires accumulating and analyzing verification history.

4.  **Violations of Operon's Invariants**

    *   **TASK 4.1: Confirm strict adherence to vision-only invariant.**
        *   **Scope:** `src\agent\verifier.py` (entire module)
        *   **Action:** No violations were identified. The module consistently relies on vision-derived information (`PageHint`, `visible_elements`, `summary`, `primary_name`) and internal agent state, without any use of DOM structures, selectors, or other non-visual abstractions. Maintain this strict adherence in all future modifications and extensions.

```

## `src\agent\video_verifier.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. P99 Latency Reduction

*   **Task 1.1: Parallelize Saliency and Gemini Operations**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Function:** `VideoVerifier.verify_action`
    *   **Action:** Refactor `verify_action` to initiate the Gemini client call (`self.gemini_client.generate_video_verification`) concurrently with the video frame extraction and temporal saliency computation. The prompt rendering (`self._render_prompt`) can occur before either starts. Use `asyncio.gather` to await both the saliency result and the Gemini response in parallel. This will significantly reduce the total wall-clock time by overlapping CPU-bound video processing with network-I/O-bound LLM inference.
*   **Task 1.2: Optimize Video Source Handling for Memory Buffers**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Function:** `VideoVerifier._extract_frames`
    *   **Action:** Modify `_extract_frames` to accept either a `Path` object or a file-like object (e.g., `io.BytesIO`) representing the video data. This would allow `VideoVerifier` to process in-memory video streams or buffers directly from the screen recording component, eliminating the intermediate disk I/O required to write the video file to disk and then read it back. This change would reduce latency by avoiding file system operations.
*   **Task 1.3: Introduce Early Exit for High-Confidence "Progressing" Saliency**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Function:** `VideoVerifier.verify_action`
    *   **Action:** Add logic to `verify_action` such that if `saliency.motion_class == "progressing"` and `saliency.confidence` (e.g., > `_CONFIDENCE_SUCCESS`) indicates a strong positive signal, the verification process can short-circuit and return a `VideoVerificationResult` indicating success immediately, *without* calling the Gemini client. This would be a configurable optimization for scenarios where visual progress is sufficient evidence, saving significant LLM latency.

### 2. Structural Idempotency

*   **Task 2.1: Implement In-Memory Caching for `verify_action` Results**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Class:** `VideoVerifier`
    *   **Action:** Introduce an in-memory cache (e.g., a dictionary or `functools.lru_cache`) within the `VideoVerifier` instance. Before performing any computations or API calls in `verify_action`, check if a result for the given unique combination of `(video_path, action, intent)` already exists in the cache and is still valid (e.g., within a short TTL). If a cached result is found, return it directly. Store the result of new verifications in this cache. This will prevent redundant computations and external API calls for identical verification requests, which can occur during retry loops or re-evaluation steps.

### 3. Agentic Features

*   **Task 3.1: Externalize and Adapt Confidence Thresholds**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Functions:** `VideoVerifier.__init__`, `VideoVerifier._compute_confidence`
    *   **Action:** Convert the hardcoded confidence thresholds (`_CONFIDENCE_SUCCESS`, `_CONFIDENCE_UNCERTAIN`, and the implicit `0.35`, `0.9`, `0.2` in `_compute_confidence`) into configurable parameters. These parameters should be settable during `VideoVerifier` initialization, allowing a higher-level agentic policy to dynamically adjust the verification strictness based on task criticality, historical success rates, or observed environment stability.
*   **Task 3.2: Enhance `suggested_next_action` Granularity for Self-Healing**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Functions:** `VideoVerifier._render_prompt`, `VideoVerifier._parse_response`
    *   **Action:** Collaborate on prompt engineering for `prompts/video_verification_prompt.txt` to encourage Gemini to provide more specific and actionable `suggested_next_action` values. Instead of generic "retry_same_step", suggestions could include `wait_and_re_evaluate`, `re_perceive_and_retry`, `try_alternative_click_position`, or `escalate_to_diagnostic_workflow`. Update `_parse_response` to handle and expose these richer suggestions, enabling more intelligent and adaptive self-healing capabilities in the overarching agent.
*   **Task 3.3: Integrate Verification Results with Learning and Policy Improvement**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Function:** `VideoVerifier.verify_action`
    *   **Action:** Introduce an event emission or a callback mechanism within `verify_action` to log the complete `VideoVerificationResult` (including `confidence_score`, `motion_class`), along with the `AgentAction`, `intent`, and `video_path`, to a persistent data store. This rich dataset can be used offline to:
        *   Train specialized, faster local models for specific verification patterns.
        *   Improve the overall agent's action generation policy by learning from verified successes and failures.
        *   Refine prompt engineering for Gemini for better accuracy and more actionable responses.
*   **Task 3.4: Implement Proactive Waiting for "Spinner" Motion Class**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Function:** `VideoVerifier.verify_action`
    *   **Action:** For cases where `saliency.motion_class == "spinner"`, instead of immediately calling Gemini, introduce a configurable "wait-and-recheck" loop. The agent can `asyncio.sleep` for a short duration and then re-evaluate the screen (e.g., by re-running saliency or taking a new screenshot) to see if the loading state has resolved. Only if the spinner persists beyond a certain duration or maximum rechecks should the Gemini call be initiated or a "loading timeout" status be propagated. This prevents unnecessary and costly Gemini calls during expected application loading times.

### 4. Operon Invariants Violations

*   **Task 4.1: Confirm Adherence to Operon Invariants**
    *   **File:** `src\agent\video_verifier.py`
    *   **Action:** No violations of Operon's core invariants have been identified within this module.
        *   **No DOM/selectors**: The module relies solely on raw video frames and multimodal analysis, providing context from `AgentAction` inputs but not using any DOM-based or selector-based mechanisms for its verification process.
        *   **Atomic focus+type**: This module performs verification, not action execution. It provides critical feedback for an action execution system that *would* adhere to atomic focus+type, but does not itself violate this.
        *   **Visual servo**: The `VideoVerifier` provides the "sense" and "feedback" loop component essential for enabling a visual servo system, rather than being the servo itself. Its output directly informs the closed-loop control needed for visual servoing, thus aligning with the invariant.
