## `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns for Reducing P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

1.  **TASK**: Refactor `_get_browser_lock` and `run_suite_background` to support parallel execution of tasks.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_get_browser_lock`, `run_suite_background`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The global `_BROWSER_TASK_LOCK` serializes all browser interactions, leading to high P99 latency for concurrent inference requests. This is the single largest bottleneck for real-time inference throughput.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Investigate if `NativeBrowserExecutor` can be configured to manage multiple, isolated browser contexts or instances concurrently.
        *   If so, modify `_get_browser_lock` to return a `threading.Semaphore` or `asyncio.Semaphore` with a configurable concurrency limit (e.g., `N` concurrent browsers) instead of a binary lock.
        *   Alternatively, adapt `get_loop_fn` to return a *new* executor instance for each task, configured to manage its own isolated browser session, removing the need for a global lock across tasks if executors are truly independent.
        *   Explore an executor pooling mechanism (e.g., `asyncio.Queue` of pre-initialized executors/browser contexts) within `run_suite_background` to reduce the overhead of `loop.start_run` when `get_loop_fn` creates new, heavy-weight resources.

2.  **TASK**: Implement asynchronous loading for task datasets to avoid blocking on I/O.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `_load_all_tasks`, `_load_tasks_filtered`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: Current task loading is synchronous (`path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")`). While not directly "inference" time, it can contribute to the P99 of suite creation if datasets are large or stored on slow I/O, impacting the responsiveness of the API.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Refactor `_load_all_tasks` to use `aiofiles` or `asyncio`'s `loop.run_in_executor` for file I/O to make dataset loading non-blocking.
        *   Ensure `_load_tasks_filtered` and subsequently `create_suite` can correctly await these asynchronous loading operations.
        *   Consider caching the loaded tasks in memory or a fast persistent store if `create_suite` is called frequently with the same parameters, to reduce redundant I/O.

**2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

1.  **TASK**: Introduce idempotent suite creation or retrieval.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `create_suite`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: Calling `create_suite` with the same `difficulty` and `source` will always generate a new `suite_id` and a new `SuiteState`. If the intent is "get an existing suite if params match, otherwise create," this is not idempotent.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Add an optional `suite_id` parameter to `create_suite`. If provided, attempt to retrieve that suite; if it exists and matches parameters, return it.
        *   Alternatively, introduce a separate `get_or_create_suite` function that hashes input parameters (`difficulty`, `source`) to check for an existing suite before creating a new one. This would require storing suites more persistently than just `_SUITES`.

2.  **TASK**: Ensure `run_suite_background` handles re-invocation robustly.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `run_suite_background`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The `run_suite_background` function modifies `SuiteState` in-place. If called on a suite that is already running or completed, it might lead to inconsistent states, re-runs, or errors.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Add a check at the beginning of `run_suite_background` to return early or raise an error if `suite.status` is already "running" or "completed". This makes explicit that re-running a suite requires explicit reset or new creation.
        *   Consider adding a `reset_suite` function that clears task statuses, step counts, and errors, allowing a suite to be explicitly re-run idempotently from a clean state.

3.  **TASK**: Implement persistent storage for `_SUITES` to ensure state idempotency across process restarts.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **GLOBAL_VAR**: `_SUITES`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The `_SUITES` dictionary is an in-memory global variable, meaning all suite state is lost if the process restarts. This violates idempotency for long-running or critical benchmark suites.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Integrate a lightweight persistent store (e.g., SQLite, a JSON file in a known location, or a simple key-value store like Redis) to persist `SuiteState` objects.
        *   Modify `create_suite`, `get_suite`, `get_all_tasks`, `run_suite_background`, and `stop_suite` to load/save/update suite state from/to this persistent store.
        *   Implement a mechanism to recover the state of interrupted suites upon startup (e.g., mark "running" suites as "failed" or "pending_retry").

**3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

1.  **TASK**: Introduce adaptive retry mechanisms based on `infra_tag` and `stop_reason`.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `run_suite_background`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: The current workflow marks a task as "failed" and moves on. An agentic system could learn from specific failure types and adapt.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Modify `run_suite_background` to include a retry loop for tasks that fail with specific `infra_tag` values (e.g., `coordinate_drift`, `perception_blindness`).
        *   Implement a back-off strategy (e.g., exponential back-off) for retries.
        *   Introduce a limited number of "adaptive retries" where the agent might modify its next `StepRequest` based on the failure reason (e.g., if `coordinate_drift`, slightly adjust the target coordinates, or re-run the perception step before the action). This would require modifying the `StepRequest` generation logic within the `loop.step_run` caller, or making `loop.step_run` itself smarter.

2.  **TASK**: Implement dynamic task prioritization and scheduling within a suite.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `run_suite_background`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: Tasks are currently run sequentially in the order they appear. An agentic system could optimize throughput or success rate by re-ordering.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Introduce a mechanism to reorder `suite.tasks` dynamically. For example, prioritize tasks that have historically succeeded, or group tasks by `site` to minimize browser re-initialization overhead.
        *   Consider a "pilot run" mode for new tasks to gather initial `infra_tag` data, which then informs future scheduling or strategy.

3.  **TASK**: Enable self-healing through executor re-initialization or alternative executor selection.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `run_suite_background`
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: Persistent issues like `viewport_clipping` or `perception_blindness` might indicate a corrupted browser state or a failing executor instance. The current system simply flags the failure.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   If a task fails repeatedly with certain `infra_tag`s (e.g., `viewport_clipping`), implement logic to perform a more drastic reset: call `loop.executor.cleanup_run` and then re-acquire a *fresh* executor instance (or fully restart the browser process) for the problematic task or subsequent tasks.
        *   If multiple executors are available (e.g., different model versions, different hardware configurations), implement an intelligent selection mechanism. If an executor consistently fails on certain task types, switch to an alternative executor for those tasks.

**4. Violations of Operon's Invariants**

1.  **TASK**: Add assertion or type-hinting to enforce Operon's invariants at the executor interface.
    *   **FILE**: `src\api\benchmark_suite.py`
    *   **FUNCTION**: `run_suite_background` (specifically, the `get_loop_fn()` and `loop` interface)
    *   **DESCRIPTION**: This module *orchestrates* the agent's actions, but doesn't implement them directly. The invariants (no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo) pertain to the *implementation* of the `NativeBrowserExecutor` provided by `get_loop_fn()`. Currently, there are no *direct* violations in this file. However, the module does not *enforce* these invariants at its interface with the executor.
    *   **ACTIONABLE STEPS**:
        *   Define a clear Python `Protocol` or Abstract Base Class (ABC) for the `NativeBrowserExecutor` interface that explicitly prohibits methods or parameters that could accept DOM selectors or non-visual inputs.
        *   Update the `get_loop_fn` return type hint and the `loop` variable type hint in `run_suite_background` to adhere to this `Protocol`/ABC. This acts as a compile-time (or static analysis time) check that the provided executor respects Operon's core principles.
        *   The existing `_INFRA_FAILURE_MAP` with categories like `coordinate_drift` and `perception_blindness` already *supports* the vision-only, visual servoing model, as these are typical failure modes for such agents. No changes are needed here, but it's a good consistency check.

## `src\api\observer.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **P99 Latency Reduction:**

    *   **TASK:** Implement `functools.lru_cache` for `src\api\observer.py::_image_dimensions` to cache image dimensions based on `path_value`. This function involves disk I/O and PIL operations, which can be slow and are often called repeatedly for the same artifact paths within a run snapshot.
    *   **TASK:** Implement `functools.lru_cache` for `src\api\observer.py::_load_json` and `src\api\observer.py::_read_text` to cache the contents of frequently accessed JSON/text artifacts. These functions perform synchronous disk I/O and JSON parsing/text reading, which can be bottlenecks, especially when the same files are accessed multiple times within a `load_run_snapshot` call or across different requests.
    *   **TASK:** Refactor `src\api\observer.py::list_runs` and `src\api\observer.py::usage_dashboard` to use `ThreadPoolExecutor` for concurrent processing of run directories and their associated `state.json` files and `summarize_run_usage` calls. This will parallelize the I/O-bound operations for multiple runs.
    *   **TASK:** Introduce a dedicated caching layer for `src\api\observer.py::summarize_run_usage`. This could be an in-memory cache, or even a lightweight disk cache (e.g., a `.usage_summary.json` file per run directory) that is updated only when new usage logs are detected. This prevents recalculating usage aggregates for every call in `list_runs` and `usage_dashboard`.
    *   **TASK:** Explore replacing synchronous file I/O operations within `src\api\observer.py::load_run_snapshot` (e.g., calls to `_load_json`, `_read_text`, `_image_dimensions` for various artifact paths) with `aiofiles` and `asyncio.gather` to enable concurrent fetching of multiple artifacts. This would require making `load_run_snapshot` and its helper functions (`_step_payload`, `_pre_step_payload`, etc.) `async`.

2.  **Structural Idempotency:**

    *   **TASK:** Modify `src\api\observer.py::reconcile_orphaned_browser_run` to only write the `state.json` file if the `state.status` or `state.stop_reason` *actually changes*. This reduces unnecessary disk writes.
        *   **Current logic:** `state.status = RunStatus.FAILED`, `state_path.write_text(...)` always executes if `state.status is RunStatus.RUNNING` and criteria met.
        *   **Proposed change:** Add a conditional check: `if state.status is RunStatus.RUNNING and not has_live_session and _looks_like_browser_run(state): # check if status or stop_reason will change if state.status != RunStatus.FAILED or (state.stop_reason is None and some_new_stop_reason_would_be_set): # then apply changes and write state.status = RunStatus.FAILED if state.stop_reason is None: state.stop_reason = StopReason.EXECUTION_NO_PROGRESS state_path.write_text(state.model_dump_json(indent=2), encoding="utf-8")`
    *   **TASK:** (Self-healing/robustness) While not strictly idempotency, ensure the underlying `_load_state_from_path` function (from `src.store.summary`) and its corresponding save function, used by `src\api\observer.py::reconcile_orphaned_browser_run`, implement atomic file writes (e.g., write to a temporary file, then rename). This prevents corrupted `state.json` files if the process crashes during a write operation, ensuring that the state file is always valid (either old or new, fully written).

3.  **Agentic Features (Self-healing Workflows, etc.):**

    *   **TASK:** Enhance `src\api\observer.py::load_run_snapshot` by introducing a new field, perhaps `"agent_insights"`, which provides summary agentic feedback. Implement a new internal function, e.g., `_analyze_run_for_anomalies`, that scans `completed_steps` and `pre_step_failures` within `load_run_snapshot` to detect potential "stuck" states, loops (e.g., repeated `page_hint`, `focused_element_id` over N steps), excessive retries, or high-cost steps. This function should return a summary (e.g., `{"status": "stuck_loop", "reason": "repeated_perception_retries"}`).
    *   **TASK:** Augment `src\api\observer.py::list_runs` and `src\api\observer.py::usage_dashboard` to include a "Run Health Score" or "Alert Status" for each run. This would leverage the `_analyze_run_for_anomalies` (or similar) insights generated for each run to provide a quick overview of which runs might require attention, moving beyond simple `succeeded`/`failed` status.
    *   **TASK:** Modify `src\api\observer.py::reconcile_orphaned_browser_run` to not only mark a run as `FAILED` but also potentially trigger an external "recovery" or "re-launch" signal if an agentic supervisor were present. This moves from passive observation to active intervention based on observed state. For instance, instead of just setting `StopReason.EXECUTION_NO_PROGRESS`, it could set `StopReason.ENVIRONMENT_CRASHED` and signal a specialized recovery mechanism.
    *   **TASK:** (Conceptual, design-level) Propose an extension to the observer API that allows for *dynamic logging adjustments* on the observed agent. For instance, if `_analyze_run_for_anomalies` detects a pattern of `perception_retry`, the observer could signal the running agent to temporarily increase the verbosity of its perception module's logging or capture additional debug artifacts without interrupting the run.

4.  **Invariant Violations (No DOM/selectors, Atomic focus+type, Visual Servo):**

    *   **FLAG:** **Direct violation of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.** The module heavily features and processes "selector" related information, which directly contradicts Operon's stated invariant.
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_step_payload`
            *   **Violation:** The entire `"selector"` block and its sub-fields (`intent`, `candidate_count`, `top_candidates`, `selected_candidate`, `score_margin`, `recovery_attempted`, `recovery_strategy_used`, `final_decision`, `failure_reason`).
            *   **Violation:** `entry.perception.focused_element_id` and `entry.perception.visible_elements` with `element_type`s like "input", "button", "link". If these are derived from a DOM representation rather than purely visual analysis, it's a violation.
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_pre_step_payload`
            *   **Violation:** `focused_element_id` and `visible_elements` with `element_type`s (same concern as above).
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_selector_trace_payload`
            *   **Violation:** This entire helper function exists solely to parse and return "selector" trace data. Its very existence implies the agent generates selector traces.
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_partial_step_payload`
            *   **Violation:** The `"selector"` block.
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_partial_perception_payload`
            *   **Violation:** `elements = parsed_perception.get("visible_elements", [])` (same concern as above).
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_build_event_log`, `src\api\observer.py::_partial_step_events`
            *   **Violation:** Event types `selector_trace_written`, `selector_recovery_used`, `selector_recovery_failed` are explicitly logged and processed.
        *   **Recommendation:** If Operon truly has "no DOM/selectors", then all references to "selector" must be removed or rephrased to describe purely visual targeting mechanisms. The `focused_element_id` and `visible_elements` attributes must be guaranteed to be derived *only* from visual perception and not from DOM introspection.

    *   **FLAG:** **Potential ambiguity/implicit violation of "atomic focus+type".**
        *   **File Path & Function:** `src\api\observer.py::_step_payload` (specifically the `"execution"` block and `entry.executed_action.action`)
        *   **Concern:** While this module doesn't define the actions, the `action` field itself needs scrutiny. If the `Action` model allows for separate "click" and "type" actions, it might contradict the "atomic focus+type" invariant, which implies a single, unified action. If `action` is a single "TypeIntoElement" action, that's consistent. This is more of an indirect observation pointing to a dependency that needs checking.
        *   **Recommendation:** Verify that `src.models.common.Action` (or the underlying action representation) strictly enforces atomic focus+type interactions, meaning an action like "type" always includes the necessary focus/targeting as a single operation, without intermediate, separable clicks or focus changes.

    *   **No immediate violations identified for "visual servo" within this module.** The presence of `before_artifact_path`, `after_artifact_path`, and image dimension processing (`_image_dimensions`) aligns with an agent operating via visual feedback. The perception metrics also seem to be derived from visual elements.

## `src\api\routes.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference

*   **Task 1.1: Implement Eager Initialization or Warm-up for Agent Loops**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Functions:** `get_agent_loop`, `get_desktop_agent_loop`
    *   **Description:** The lazy initialization of `_agent_loop` and `_desktop_agent_loop` via global variables means the first `run-task` or `step` request will incur significant latency due to component instantiation (LLM clients, executors, stores). This drastically affects P99 for initial requests or after restarts.
    *   **Action:** Introduce a dedicated application startup event (e.g., FastAPI's ` lifespan` event) to eagerly call `get_agent_loop()` and `get_desktop_agent_loop()` on application startup, ensuring all core services are ready before the first inference request arrives.
*   **Task 1.2: Optimize Executor Import Latency**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Functions:** `_build_browser_executor`, `get_desktop_agent_loop`
    *   **Description:** The use of `importlib.import_module` within `_build_browser_executor` and `get_desktop_agent_loop` (for `DesktopExecutor`) introduces dynamic import overhead on the first call.
    *   **Action:** Move these imports to the top level of the module or ensure they are part of the eager initialization in Task 1.1. Consider if `DesktopExecutor` can be imported directly at the top if there are no circular dependencies or startup issues.
*   **Task 1.3: Ensure Asynchronous File I/O for Stores**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Dependencies:** `src/store/memory.py`, `src/store/run_store.py` (specifically `FileBackedMemoryStore`, `FileBackedRunStore`)
    *   **Description:** `FileBackedRunStore` and `FileBackedMemoryStore` are instantiated and used in `get_agent_loop` and `get_desktop_agent_loop`. If their underlying file operations (`get_run`, `set_status`, etc.) are synchronous or involve blocking calls, they can contribute to high P99 latency, especially under contention.
    *   **Action:** Verify that all file I/O operations within `FileBackedMemoryStore` and `FileBackedRunStore` are truly asynchronous (e.g., using `aiofiles` or running in a thread pool via `loop.run_in_executor`) to prevent blocking the event loop.
*   **Task 1.4: Implement Connection Pooling and Client-side Caching for LLM Clients**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Dependencies:** `src/clients/anthropic.py`, `src/clients/gemini.py`, `src/clients/gemini_computer_use.py`
    *   **Description:** Multiple `HttpClient` instances (`AnthropicHttpClient`, `GeminiHttpClient`, `GeminiComputerUseHttpClient`) are created. While `httpx` (likely used under the hood) provides pooling, explicit configuration for persistent connections and aggressive reuse can further reduce latency. Client-side caching for highly repetitive or deterministic LLM calls (e.g., initial prompt structuring) could also help.
    *   **Action:** Review and optimize the configuration of underlying HTTP clients for connection pooling. Investigate adding a lightweight, in-memory cache for LLM responses within the `PerceptionService` or `PolicyService` if certain prompts/observations yield consistently similar results over short periods.

#### 2. Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

*   **Task 2.1: Enhance `/run-task` for Idempotent Run Creation**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Function:** `run_task`, `desktop_run_task`
    *   **Description:** Currently, calling `/run-task` multiple times with the same intent will create multiple distinct runs. This lacks idempotency.
    *   **Action:** Introduce an optional `client_run_id` field in `RunTaskRequest`. If provided, the system should first check if a run with that ID already exists and is not in a terminal state. If it exists, return the existing run's state (200 OK or 202 Accepted, but with the existing run_id). Otherwise, create a new run with that ID. This requires modifying `AgentLoop.start_run` to handle an optional `run_id`.
*   **Task 2.2: Implement Conditional Updates for `/step` and `/resume`**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Functions:** `step_run`, `desktop_step_run`, `resume_run`, `desktop_resume_run`
    *   **Description:** Repeatedly calling `/step` will advance the run multiple times. Repeatedly calling `/resume` on an already resumed run might yield an error or a non-idempotent state change.
    *   **Action:** Augment `StepRequest` and `ResumeRequest` with an `expected_version` or `current_step_count` field. The `AgentLoop`'s `step_run` and `resume_run` methods should only proceed if the current server-side state matches the `expected_version` or `current_step_count` in the request. If not, return a `HTTP 409 Conflict` with the current state, indicating the client's state is stale.
*   **Task 2.3: Ensure Idempotent Cleanup Operations**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`
    *   **Functions:** `cleanup`, `desktop_cleanup`
    *   **Description:** The `executor.cleanup_run` method's behavior on repeated calls determines the idempotency of these endpoints.
    *   **Action:** Confirm that `executor.cleanup_run(run_id)` in the respective executor implementations is inherently idempotent, meaning it can be called multiple times without causing errors or unwanted side effects beyond the first successful call (e.g., returning 0 closed resources if already cleaned up). If not, modify the executor to ensure this behavior.

#### 3. Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Proactive Goal Re-planning and Adaptive Recovery**
    *   **File:** `src/agent/loop.py` (and related services instantiated in `routes.py`)
    *   **Description:** The `RuleBasedRecoveryManager` provides limited recovery. An Operon agent should proactively re-plan or adapt its strategy if the current plan deviates significantly from expectations or fails in unforeseen ways, leveraging its LLM capabilities.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Augment the `AgentLoop.step_run` logic to detect significant deviations (e.g., `VerifierService` failure, unexpected environment changes, loop detection, long execution times without progress).
        2.  If a deviation is detected, trigger a specialized `PolicyService` call (e.g., with a "diagnose_and_replan_prompt") that takes the current observation, the failed action, and the original intent to generate a new sub-plan or recovery strategy. This goes beyond simple rule lookups.
*   **Task 3.2: Integrate a "Human-in-the-Loop" (HITL) Decision Point**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py`, `src/agent/loop.py`, `src/models/common.py`
    *   **Description:** When the agent faces high uncertainty, critical ambiguity, or requires approval for sensitive actions, it should be able to explicitly pause and solicit human input, rather than failing or guessing. The `hitl_message` in `RunResponse` hints at this.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Add a `RunStatus.PAUSED_FOR_HUMAN_INPUT` enum value to `RunStatus`.
        2.  Modify `AgentLoop.step_run` to transition to this status, storing the specific question or decision point for the human.
        3.  Create a new `POST /run/{run_id}/human-input` endpoint that allows a human to provide input, which then triggers `AgentLoop.resume_run` with the provided context.
        4.  The `PolicyService` should have a mechanism to generate the human-facing prompt when HITL is invoked, and incorporate the human's response into subsequent planning.
*   **Task 3.3: Implement Continuous Learning from Run Traces**
    *   **File:** `src/store/run_store.py`, `src/agent/policy.py`, `src/agent/perception.py`
    *   **Description:** The system collects extensive run data. This data (observations, actions, LLM interactions, success/failure) is a valuable resource for improving agent performance over time.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  Design a mechanism within `FileBackedRunStore` (or a new `LearningStore`) to persist detailed interaction logs for each step (input observation, LLM prompt, LLM response, chosen action, outcome, verifier result).
        2.  Develop an offline process or a background agentic component that periodically analyzes these logs to identify common failure patterns, successful strategies, and areas for prompt engineering or model fine-tuning.
        3.  Integrate findings back into `PerceptionService` (e.g., better feature extraction) and `PolicyService` (e.g., improved prompt strategies or few-shot examples).

#### 4. Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants

*   **Task 4.1: Audit `BrowserJsonBackend` for DOM/Selector Abstraction Violations**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py` (Instantiation), `src/agent/browser_json.py` (Implementation)
    *   **Description:** Operon's invariant is "no DOM/selectors." The `BrowserJsonBackend` and its associated `browser_combined_prompt.txt` suggest processing a JSON representation of the browser state. If this JSON is derived from underlying DOM structures or exposes DOM elements (e.g., `element_id`, `xpath`, `css_selector`) as primary identifiers or action targets, it violates the spirit of a "vision-only, zero-abstraction" agent. It should instead rely on visual features (e.g., bounding boxes, OCR text, image features).
    *   **Action:** Initiate a deep dive into `src/agent/browser_json.py` and the structure of JSON data it processes. Verify that the JSON representation of the browser state (and the actions the LLM is prompted to produce) are exclusively based on visual properties (bounding boxes, text content, visual hierarchy) and not on programmatic DOM properties or selectors. If violations are found, refactor the perception/action space to adhere to pure visual abstractions.
*   **Task 4.2: Verify Executor Actions Adhere to Atomic Focus+Type and Visual Servo**
    *   **File:** `src/api/routes.py` (Instantiation), `src/executor/*` (Implementation)
    *   **Description:** The invariants "atomic focus+type" and "visual servo" directly relate to how the `Executor` (NativeBrowserExecutor, DesktopExecutor, BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor) implements actions and provides feedback. The `routes.py` module instantiates these executors.
    *   **Action:** Review the `execute` methods within all `src/executor/*.py` implementations. Confirm that:
        1.  Input actions (like typing) involve a distinct focus action (e.g., a click at an X,Y coordinate) followed by a separate typing action into the *currently focused* element, rather than directly setting an element's text content.
        2.  The executor provides sufficient visual feedback (`ScreenCaptureService`) after *every* action, enabling the `AgentLoop` to operate in a continuous visual servo loop. This implies that the executor does not perform compound actions without intermediate visual updates.

## `src\api\runtime_config.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Task**: Implement caching for runtime configuration loading to reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.
    *   **Description**: Repeated calls to `desktop_mode_config()` and `browser_mode_config()` currently re-read environment variables and re-instantiate `RuntimeModeConfig` objects. While `os.getenv` is fast, consistent re-evaluation can contribute to P99 latency variability, especially during frequent configuration access. Cache the results of these functions after the first call.
    *   **File**: `src\api\runtime_config.py`
    *   **Functions**: `desktop_mode_config`, `browser_mode_config`
    *   **Action**: Modify `desktop_mode_config` and `browser_mode_config` to memoize or cache their return values, ensuring `os.getenv` calls and `RuntimeModeConfig` instantiation occur only once per application lifecycle or until an explicit refresh. A simple `@lru_cache(maxsize=1)` decorator or a module-level variable to store the loaded config would suffice.

2.  **Task**: Enhance structural idempotency by ensuring `RuntimeModeConfig` instances are singleton-like or lazily initialized once.
    *   **Description**: While the current functions are functionally idempotent (multiple calls yield equivalent results), they are not structurally idempotent in terms of object creation and environment variable reads. This ties into the latency reduction task. Making the configuration objects effectively singletons prevents redundant operations.
    *   **File**: `src\api\runtime_config.py`
    *   **Functions**: `desktop_mode_config`, `browser_mode_config`
    *   **Action**: After implementing caching as described in Task 1, ensure that the caching mechanism effectively makes these configuration objects "structurally idempotent" by providing the same instance (or an immutable equivalent) upon repeated requests without re-computation.

3.  **Task**: Suggest agentic features for dynamic configuration and self-healing.
    *   **Description**: This module defines fallback models and backends. True agentic behavior would extend beyond static configuration to dynamic, adaptive management.
    *   **File**: `src\api\runtime_config.py` (and related integration points)
    *   **Functions**: N/A (conceptual, architectural suggestion)
    *   **Action**: (No direct code change in this file, but a design suggestion for where these configs are consumed)
        *   **Dynamic Model/Backend Switching**: Implement an agentic component that monitors real-time performance metrics (e.g., P99 latency, error rates, token throughput) of the `primary_model`/`backend`. If predefined thresholds are breached, this component should *automatically* initiate a switch to the `fallback_model`/`fallback_backend` defined in `RuntimeModeConfig` without manual intervention or predefined workflow steps.
        *   **Proactive Resource Management**: An agentic system could, based on predicted workload or user activity patterns, pre-load specific models or their weights (e.g., the `planner_model` or `verifier_model`) into memory/GPU before they are strictly needed, reducing cold-start latency for critical path operations.
        *   **Self-tuning Parameters**: Beyond just model switching, an agentic component could dynamically adjust model inference parameters (e.g., temperature, top_p, top_k) based on observed task success rates, user feedback, or environmental factors to optimize for specific objectives (e.g., speed vs. accuracy).

4.  **Task**: Flag potential indirect invariant violations and ensure downstream adherence.
    *   **Description**: This module defines configuration values that point to components (backends, models) which *must* uphold Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo. This module itself does not contain any operational logic that could violate these invariants. However, the string values chosen for `backend` (e.g., `"computer_use"`) imply the existence of downstream implementations.
    *   **File**: `src\api\runtime_config.py`
    *   **Functions**: `desktop_mode_config`, `browser_mode_config`
    *   **Action**:
        *   **Clarification**: No direct violations are present *within this configuration module*.
        *   **Mandate**: Emphasize that all backend implementations referenced by `backend` values (e.g., "json", "computer_use") and the models chosen (e.g., `gemini-2.5-computer-use-preview-10-2025`) must strictly adhere to Operon's core invariants:
            *   **No DOM/selectors**: The `computer_use` backend and any subsequent UI interaction layers must operate solely on vision-only input, without relying on DOM trees, CSS selectors, or accessibility APIs that abstract the visual surface.
            *   **Atomic focus+type**: Any interaction with text input fields must be managed as a single, atomic operation driven by visual servo, not by discrete keyboard events or DOM manipulation.
            *   **Visual servo**: All navigation and interaction must be driven by continuous visual feedback and closed-loop control, reflecting the "vision-only, zero-abstraction" principle.
        *   **Suggestion**: Consider adding runtime validation (e.g., assertion checks in the consuming code) to ensure that the configured `backend` and `model` values correspond to known implementations that are certified to uphold these invariants.

## `src\api\server.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

    *   **Task 1.1:** Optimize Environment Variable Loading for Production.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py`
        *   **Function:** `create_app`
        *   **Detail:** Remove the explicit call to `dotenv.load_dotenv(find_dotenv(usecwd=True), override=False)` from the `create_app` function. For production deployments, environment variables should be managed and pre-loaded by the deployment environment (e.g., Docker, Kubernetes, systemd) to eliminate synchronous file I/O during critical application startup. This improves cold start times which can impact P99 latency in highly dynamic environments.
    *   **Task 1.2:** Defer Benchmark Plugin Import.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py`
        *   **Function:** `create_app`
        *   **Detail:** The `import src.benchmarks.form_plugin` statement introduces a synchronous load for a module primarily intended for development or testing. Relocate this import into a conditional block (e.g., `if os.getenv("OPERON_ENV") == "development":`) or implement a mechanism for dynamic, lazy loading only when benchmarks are explicitly requested or enabled. This reduces the application's startup time and memory footprint for production inference workers, directly impacting P99 latency by allowing faster scaling and resource availability.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

    *   **Task 2.1:** Reinforce Idempotency for Future Configuration Additions.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py`
        *   **Function:** `create_app`
        *   **Detail:** The existing `load_dotenv(override=False)` is a good practice for idempotent environment loading. Establish a guideline and ensure that any future additions to `create_app` involving resource allocation, connection pooling, or global state initialization are designed to be idempotent. This ensures consistent application state and behavior even if the `create_app` function or parts of its setup logic are invoked multiple times due to unforeseen scenarios like module reloading or complex testing setups, preventing resource leaks or unexpected side effects.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **Task 3.1:** Implement Dynamic Configuration Reloading.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py` (and related configuration modules)
        *   **Function:** `create_app` (initial setup, with runtime hooks)
        *   **Detail:** Introduce a mechanism for Operon to dynamically reload or update its configuration parameters (e.g., inference model versions, logging levels, feature flags) at runtime without requiring a full application restart. This could involve integrating a dedicated configuration service client or exposing a secure, authenticated FastAPI endpoint to trigger a configuration refresh, enabling the agent to adapt its behavior in real-time based on operational feedback or environmental changes.
    *   **Task 3.2:** Integrate Enhanced Self-Healing Health Checks.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py` (and modules loaded by `router`)
        *   **Function:** `create_app` (initializes health check system)
        *   **Detail:** Extend standard FastAPI health check endpoints to incorporate domain-specific, self-healing capabilities. This means registering callbacks that, upon detecting a failure in a critical component (e.g., a vision model failing to load or an inference pipeline becoming unresponsive), automatically trigger remediation actions such as re-initializing the problematic component, switching to a fallback model, or adjusting resource allocation. This proactive self-correction goes beyond passive health reporting found in typical workflow engines.
    *   **Task 3.3:** Enable Runtime Control over Optional Modules.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py`
        *   **Function:** `create_app`
        *   **Detail:** Refactor the static `import src.benchmarks.form_plugin` into a system that allows dynamic loading, unloading, or activation/deactivation of optional modules (like benchmark plugins, experimental features, or alternative inference pipelines) at runtime. This can be controlled via configuration flags or dedicated API endpoints, enabling Operon to adapt its capabilities and resource usage without requiring application restarts, providing flexibility akin to an evolving agent.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**

    *   **Task 4.1:** Establish Architectural Guardrails for Operon Invariants.
        *   **File:** `src\api\server.py` (and all modules loaded by it, e.g., `src.api.routes`)
        *   **Function:** `create_app` (indirectly affects all loaded modules)
        *   **Detail:** `src\api\server.py` itself does not directly violate Operon's core invariants: "no DOM/selectors," "atomic focus+type," and "visual servo." However, as the application's bootstrap, it is critical that *all modules loaded by it* (especially `src.api.routes` and any core agent logic) adhere to these principles. Implement static analysis (e.g., a custom linter rule in a pre-commit hook) to detect and prevent disallowed imports or usage patterns (e.g., `selenium`, `playwright`, `beautifulsoup4`, or any library that provides access to DOM structures) within the core agent logic. This ensures the foundational vision-only, zero-abstraction approach is strictly enforced across the entire system.

## `src\benchmarks\form_plugin.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize Rule Engine Evaluation for `_get_rules`**
    *   **Action:** Evaluate the current rule engine's performance for policy rules like `form_submit_when_ready_rule`. If rule sets are expected to grow or become complex, refactor the rule execution mechanism to utilize a more efficient pattern (e.g., a decision tree, Rete-like network, or highly optimized predicate evaluation) to reduce P99 latency during action selection. This minimizes the time spent evaluating policies during critical inference loops.
    *   **Scope:** `src/benchmarks/form_plugin.py` (caller of `_get_rules`), `src/agent/policy_rules.py` (where rules are defined), and the core inference engine responsible for evaluating these rules.
*   **Task 1.2: Implement Efficient Success Token Matching**
    *   **Action:** The `success_tokens` are critical for determining task completion. Implement an optimized string matching algorithm (e.g., Aho-Corasick, or pre-compiled regular expressions if patterns are involved) for comparing `success_tokens` against extracted visual text. This will reduce latency when detecting completion signals, especially if screen text is large or many tokens need to be checked.
    *   **Scope:** The part of the Operon engine that utilizes `BenchmarkPlugin.success_tokens` for visual text comparison.
*   **Task 1.3: Index and Optimize Memory Seed Retrieval**
    *   **Action:** As the number of `memory_seeds` grows across various benchmarks, ensure that the retrieval mechanism for these `MemoryRecord` objects (e.g., by `key`, `hint`, or `stage`) is highly optimized. Implement efficient data structures (e.g., hash maps for direct key lookups, or an indexed vector store for semantic retrieval of hints) to guarantee low P99 latency for memory access during real-time inference.
    *   **Scope:** `src/benchmarks/form_plugin.py` (definition of `_seeds`), `src/models/memory.py` (MemoryRecord structure), and the agent's memory management component.

**2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

*   **Task 2.1: Ensure Idempotent Benchmark Plugin Registration**
    *   **Action:** Modify the `BENCHMARK_REGISTRY.register` method to be idempotent. If a `BenchmarkPlugin` with the same `name` is registered multiple times, the registry should either gracefully update/overwrite the existing entry with the new one, or ignore subsequent identical registrations, without causing errors or unintended side effects.
    *   **Scope:** `src/benchmarks/registry.py` (the `BENCHMARK_REGISTRY` implementation).
*   **Task 2.2: Guarantee Idempotent Memory Seed Addition**
    *   **Action:** When `memory_seeds` from a `BenchmarkPlugin` are loaded into Operon's active memory, ensure this operation is idempotent. If `MemoryRecord`s are added based on a unique identifier (e.g., `key` + `benchmark`), subsequent attempts to add the same record should not create duplicates but rather update or be ignored, maintaining a consistent memory state.
    *   **Scope:** The module responsible for loading and integrating `BenchmarkPlugin.memory_seeds` into Operon's operational memory store.

**3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

*   **Task 3.1: Develop Adaptive Rule Refinement from `MemoryOutcome`**
    *   **Action:** Design and implement a system where Operon can dynamically refine or generate new policy rules based on observed `MemoryOutcome`s, particularly `GUARDRAIL` failures. For instance, if "avoid\_identical\_type\_retry" frequently results in `GUARDRAIL`, the agent should adapt its "re-establish focus" logic proactively or generate more robust recovery strategies, moving beyond the static `_get_rules` definition.
    *   **Scope:** `src/agent/policy_rules.py`, `src/models/memory.py`, and the agent's core learning and adaptation module.
*   **Task 3.2: Implement Goal-Oriented Self-Correction with Visual Feedback**
    *   **Action:** Enhance the agent's planning and execution loop to continuously monitor the visual state against the `BenchmarkPlugin.expected_completion_signal`. If the observed visual state deviates from the expected signal, the agent should dynamically re-plan its actions, explore alternative paths, or trigger specific recovery sub-routines, rather than simply failing or following a fixed path.
    *   **Scope:** The agent's core planning and execution module, leveraging `BenchmarkPlugin.expected_completion_signal` and real-time visual perception data.
*   **Task 3.3: Introduce Proactive Guardrail Application Based on `MemoryRecord.hint`**
    *   **Action:** Develop a mechanism for Operon to proactively apply guardrails by using `MemoryRecord.hint` (e.g., "click the input before typing") to anticipate potential failure modes. Based on the current visual context and agent's `LoopStage` (`CHOOSE_ACTION`), the agent should preemptively take actions suggested by relevant `GUARDRAIL` hints, preventing errors before they occur, rather than reacting to a failure post-factum.
    *   **Scope:** The agent's action selection (`LoopStage.CHOOSE_ACTION`) and memory retrieval/application components.

**4. Violations of Operon's Invariants**

*   **Task 4.1: Verify `PageHint` Generation Adherence to "No DOM/Selectors"**
    *   **Action:** Conduct a thorough review of the underlying mechanisms that generate `PageHint` (e.g., `PageHint.FORM_PAGE`). **Crucially, ensure that `PageHint` derivation relies *exclusively* on visual analysis of the screen (pixels, detected text, visual layout, etc.) and does not incorporate or infer information from the Document Object Model (DOM), CSS selectors, accessibility trees, or any other non-visual, abstract representations of the webpage structure.** If violations are found, refactor the `PageHint` generation logic.
    *   **Scope:** `src/models/perception.py` (where `PageHint` is likely defined and generated) and the perception module responsible for screen analysis.
*   **Task 4.2: Audit `form_submit_when_ready_rule` for "No DOM/Selectors" Violation**
    *   **Action:** Review the complete implementation of `src.agent.policy_rules.form_submit_when_ready_rule` (and any other rules loaded by benchmarks) to confirm it strictly adheres to Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant. The rule's logic must operate solely on visual perception data (e.g., bounding boxes of detected elements, OCR text, visual cues) and explicitly avoid any direct or indirect use of DOM elements, CSS selectors, XPath, or similar non-visual web abstractions for identifying or interacting with page elements.
    *   **Scope:** `src/agent/policy_rules.py` (the implementation of `form_submit_when_ready_rule`).

## `src\benchmarks\registry.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Suggestions for P99 Latency Reduction

1.  **Task**: Introduce caching for `all_seeds` and `registered_names` if these methods are invoked frequently during real-time inference.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkRegistry.all_seeds`, `BenchmarkRegistry.registered_names`
    *   **Details**: Currently, `all_seeds` and `registered_names` iterate through all registered plugins, which is `O(N)` where N is the number of benchmarks. While this is acceptable for startup, frequent calls in a real-time inference loop could add latency as N grows. Implement an LRU cache (e.g., using `functools.lru_cache`) or a simple attribute-based cache (`_cached_all_seeds`, `_cached_registered_names`) that is invalidated upon `register` calls. This ensures `O(1)` access for subsequent reads between registrations.

2.  **Task**: Explore pre-computation or lazy loading for `BenchmarkRulePlugin` and `MemoryRecord` if their initialization or retrieval is computationally intensive.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkPlugin` (specifically `rules` and `memory_seeds` fields)
    *   **Details**: The `BenchmarkPlugin` dataclass holds lists of `BenchmarkRulePlugin` and `MemoryRecord`. While the registry itself provides fast access, the initialization cost or internal complexity of these referenced objects might contribute to P99 latency. If these objects are complex, consider lazy initialization within the `BenchmarkRulePlugin` or `MemoryRecord` classes themselves, or investigate pre-parsing/pre-computation of their essential attributes at registration time, storing optimized representations.

#### 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

1.  **Task**: Clarify and potentially enforce immutability for `BenchmarkPlugin` instances after registration.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkPlugin`, `BenchmarkRegistry.register`
    *   **Details**: The `BenchmarkRegistry.register` method overwrites existing plugins, which is idempotent for the plugin name. However, `BenchmarkPlugin` uses mutable types (`list`, `dict`) for `rules`, `memory_seeds`, and `section_map`. If a registered `BenchmarkPlugin` instance is modified externally after being passed to `register`, it could lead to unexpected non-idempotent behavior. To ensure strict idempotency and predictability, consider:
        *   Making `BenchmarkPlugin` truly immutable (e.g., using `frozenset` for `success_tokens`, `tuple` for `rules` and `memory_seeds`, `frozendict` for `section_map` - or convert to `tuple` of `(PageHint, str)`).
        *   Documenting that `BenchmarkPlugin` instances passed to `register` should be considered immutable thereafter.
        *   Optionally, having `register` make a deep copy of the `plugin` if modifications outside the registry are intended to *not* affect the registered state, though this adds overhead.

#### 3. Agentic Features

1.  **Task**: Implement dynamic loading/unloading mechanisms for benchmark plugins.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkRegistry`
    *   **Details**: Beyond passive import-time registration, an Operon agent could benefit from explicit methods to:
        *   `load_plugin_from_path(filepath: str)`: Dynamically load a benchmark module from a given file path, ensuring it registers itself.
        *   `unload_plugin(name: str)`: Remove a registered plugin, potentially freeing resources or allowing for hot-swapping benchmark definitions. This supports adaptive behavior and resource management for long-running agents.

2.  **Task**: Introduce versioning support for benchmarks within the registry.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkPlugin`, `BenchmarkRegistry`
    *   **Details**: Allow `BenchmarkPlugin` to carry a `version: str` attribute. The registry could then support `register_versioned(plugin: BenchmarkPlugin)` and `get_latest(name: str)` or `get_specific_version(name: str, version: str)`. This enables an agent to:
        *   A/B test different benchmark configurations or policy rules.
        *   Rollback to a previous known-good benchmark version (self-healing).
        *   Gradually deploy updated benchmark definitions.

3.  **Task**: Integrate callback hooks for lifecycle events (e.g., `on_registered`, `on_unregistered`).
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkRegistry.register`
    *   **Details**: Allow `BenchmarkPlugin` or an external listener to register callbacks that are triggered when a plugin is registered or unregistered. This enables agentic features like:
        *   **Self-configuration**: Automatically update agent's internal state or rules engine when a new benchmark is available.
        *   **Monitoring**: Log or notify external systems about changes in available benchmarks.
        *   **Resource allocation**: Pre-allocate resources for a newly registered benchmark.

#### 4. Operon Invariants Violations

1.  **CRITICAL VIOLATION FLAG**: Clarify or refactor `BenchmarkPlugin.section_map` to eliminate any implied reliance on DOM or traditional selectors.
    *   **File**: `src\benchmarks\registry.py`
    *   **Function/Class**: `BenchmarkPlugin.section_map`
    *   **Details**: Operon's core invariant states "no DOM/selectors". The description for `section_map` explicitly states: "Maps a `PageHint` to the element-section label used by the **selector**."
        *   **Action Required**:
            1.  **Remove or redefine "selector"**: The term "selector" must be removed from the documentation and any underlying implementation.
            2.  **Verify `PageHint` definition**: Ensure that `src.models.perception.PageHint` is *exclusively* derived from visual perception (e.g., bounding boxes, visual features, OCR results) and contains *no* information directly from the HTML DOM, accessibility tree, or any other structural representation of a webpage.
            3.  **Clarify "element-section label"**: This label must refer to an arbitrary, human-readable name for a *visual region* (identified purely by `PageHint`), and not implicitly refer to an HTML element ID, class, or tag.
        *   **Reasoning**: Any mapping that uses a "selector" violates Operon's fundamental vision-only, zero-abstraction principle. Operon perceives and interacts with the rendered pixels, not the underlying code structure. If `section_map` is intended to map a visual region to a semantic label, it must be ensured that this process is purely vision-driven.

## `src\benchmarks\webarena.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference

*   **TASK 1.1: Parallelize task execution within `_run_all_tasks`**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_run_all_tasks`
    *   **Description**: The current implementation runs tasks sequentially, leading to high P99 latency for the overall benchmark suite. Modify `_run_all_tasks` to run multiple `loop.run_live_benchmark` calls concurrently using `asyncio.gather` or a similar pattern, up to a configurable concurrency limit. This assumes the underlying `get_agent_loop` and its executor can handle concurrent `run_live_benchmark` calls.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Introduce a `concurrency_limit` parameter (e.g., via `args`).
        *   Create a list of coroutines, each calling `loop.run_live_benchmark` for a task.
        *   Use an `asyncio.Semaphore` to limit concurrent execution of these coroutines.
        *   Collect results as they complete.

*   **TASK 1.2: Refactor `_extract_final_url` to use `await` instead of `run_until_complete`**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_extract_final_url`
    *   **Description**: The use of `asyncio.get_event_loop().run_until_complete` within an `async` function (`_run_all_tasks` implicitly calls it via `executor.current_url_for_run` in the `elif` branch) is a blocking operation and an anti-pattern in `async` code, significantly increasing latency.
    *   **Action**: Change the standalone `_extract_final_url` function to be `async` and use `await executor.current_url_for_run(run_id)`. Then, ensure `_run_all_tasks` explicitly `await`s this new `async` helper if it uses it. Or, more simply, directly `await` the call within `_run_all_tasks`.

*   **TASK 1.3: Decouple result persistence from critical path**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_run_all_tasks`
    *   **Description**: Writing task results to disk (`task_path.write_text`) for each task is a synchronous I/O operation that blocks the main loop, adding to P99 latency. Decouple this by either:
        1.  Batching writes: Collect all `results` in memory and write them all at once after all tasks are completed.
        2.  Asynchronous writes: Use `loop.run_in_executor` or an equivalent to offload disk writes to a separate thread or process.
    *   **Action**: Implement batching: Remove `task_path.write_text` from the `for task in tasks` loop. Instead, after the loop (or after all concurrent tasks complete), iterate through the `results` list and write all `task_{task.task_id}.json` files at once.

### 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

*   **TASK 2.1: Implement atomic writes for task results**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_run_all_tasks` (and potentially `main` for summary)
    *   **Description**: Currently, `task_path.write_text` directly overwrites the result file. If the system crashes during the write operation, the file could be corrupted or incomplete. Atomic writes (write to a temporary file, then rename) ensure that result files are always either fully present or not present, which is crucial for reliability in a benchmark run where tasks might be retried or processed incrementally.
    *   **Action**: Modify the file writing logic for `task_path` to use a temporary file and rename it.
        ```python
        # Example within _run_all_tasks loop (after decoupling):
        # tmp_path = output_dir / f"task_{task.task_id}.json.tmp"
        # tmp_path.write_text(json.dumps(result.model_dump(), indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
        # tmp_path.rename(task_path)
        ```
        Apply similar logic for `summary_path` in `main`.

*   **TASK 2.2: Enable benchmark resumption by checking for existing results**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_run_all_tasks`
    *   **Description**: If a benchmark run is interrupted, all tasks must be re-run from scratch. To achieve idempotency at the benchmark suite level, check if a result file already exists for a task before executing `loop.run_live_benchmark`. This allows resuming partial runs efficiently.
    *   **Action**: Before calling `response = await loop.run_live_benchmark(...)` for each `task`, check `task_path = output_dir / f"task_{task.task_id}.json"`. If `task_path.exists()`, load the existing result, append it to `results`, and `continue` to the next task. Add an option (`--resume`) to `argparse` to enable/disable this behavior.

### 3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines

*   **TASK 3.1: Implement adaptive task retry with backoff and context logging**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_run_all_tasks`
    *   **Description**: The current system does not retry failed tasks. An agentic feature would be to automatically retry tasks that fail (e.g., `passed` is `False` or `stop_reason` indicates an error), possibly with an exponential backoff strategy. Crucially, each retry attempt should log relevant context (e.g., previous error, new parameters if adjusted) to inform future decisions.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Wrap the `loop.run_live_benchmark` call in a retry loop.
        *   Introduce a `max_retries` and `initial_backoff_seconds` parameter.
        *   Log the attempt number, `stop_reason`, and `eval_types_result` for each retry.
        *   Consider adjusting `max_steps` or other parameters for retries, learning from previous attempts.

*   **TASK 3.2: Introduce dynamic task prioritization based on historical performance or inferred difficulty**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `main` and `_filter_tasks`
    *   **Description**: Currently, tasks are run in the order they appear. An agentic feature would be to dynamically prioritize tasks based on factors like:
        *   Past success/failure rates (prioritize tasks that frequently fail for faster iteration, or prioritize easy tasks for quick wins).
        *   Estimated difficulty (e.g., by analyzing `difficulty` field or previous run durations).
        *   Resource availability (e.g., if a task is known to be memory-intensive, run it when fewer other tasks are concurrent).
    *   **Action**:
        *   After `_filter_tasks`, implement a `_sort_tasks_agentically` function.
        *   This function could consult historical `WebArenaSummary` data (if available) to inform sorting.
        *   Add an argument (`--sort-strategy`) to `argparse` to allow selecting different prioritization methods (e.g., `difficulty_asc`, `difficulty_desc`, `pass_rate_asc`).

*   **TASK 3.3: Implement self-healing for the agent loop (`get_agent_loop`)**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `main`, `_run_all_tasks`
    *   **Description**: If the underlying `loop` obtained via `get_agent_loop()` becomes unresponsive or crashes (e.g., during `run_live_benchmark` or `get_run`), the entire benchmark run could halt. A self-healing mechanism would detect this and attempt to re-initialize or restart the agent loop.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Wrap calls to `loop` methods (e.g., `run_live_benchmark`, `run_store.get_run`) in a `try...except` block that catches broad exceptions or specific `LoopUnavailableError` types.
        *   If an exception occurs, attempt to re-call `get_agent_loop()` a fixed number of times with a backoff.
        *   If re-initialization fails, log a critical error and gracefully shut down or mark the current task as unrunnable.
        *   Ensure any state associated with the failed `loop` is properly cleaned up before re-initialization.

### 4. Violations of Operon's Invariants

*   **FLAG 4.1: Potential violation of "vision-only, zero-abstraction" due to `visible_elements` structure**
    *   **File**: `src/benchmarks/webarena.py`
    *   **Function**: `_extract_final_text`
    *   **Description**: Operon is a "vision-only, zero-abstraction computer-use agent" with "no DOM/selectors." The function `_extract_final_text` processes `agent_state.observation_history[-1].visible_elements`, which contains structured `el.label` and `el.text` fields. While `_extract_final_text` itself doesn't *use* DOM/selectors, the very presence of pre-parsed, labeled `visible_elements` in the `agent_state` implies that an abstraction layer (potentially relying on DOM/accessibility tree parsing) exists somewhere upstream *before* the agent receives its observations or before they are stored. This violates the "zero-abstraction" principle for the *system providing the observations to the agent*.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Investigate the source of `agent_state.observation_history[-1].visible_elements`.
        *   If it's derived from DOM/accessibility APIs, it's a direct violation. The observation mechanism for Operon must be purely visual (e.g., raw pixels, bounding boxes with OCR results if derived visually, but not DOM-based `label`/`text` properties).
        *   If `visible_elements` must be present for evaluation, ensure its generation pipeline is purely vision-based (e.g., image segmentation + OCR) and *not* relying on browser internal structures. Otherwise, this feature of `agent_state` must be removed or modified to reflect raw visual processing outputs.
        *   **Recommendation**: For a truly zero-abstraction agent, `agent_state` observations should ideally consist primarily of raw or minimally processed visual data (e.g., screenshots, perhaps with detected bounding boxes and associated OCR *results* rather than pre-assigned `label`/`text` fields). The agent itself should be responsible for interpreting these.

## `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference:**
    *   **Task 1.1: Enhance `evaluate_task` for early failure exit.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Function:** `evaluate_task`
        *   **Description:** For scenarios where overall task success is paramount and required quickly (e.g., in a real-time feedback loop for the agent), modify `evaluate_task` to optionally return `False` immediately upon the first failure of an `eval_type`, rather than evaluating all types. This would reduce P99 latency for overall task failure detection. A flag like `fail_fast: bool = False` could control this behavior.
    *   **Task 1.2: Implement compiled regex for `string_match` if complexity increases.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Function:** `string_match`
        *   **Description:** While current `str.lower() in str.lower()` is efficient for simple checks, if `must_include` strings evolve to include complex patterns (e.g., wildcards, anchors) or if the list becomes very long, using pre-compiled regular expressions (e.g., `re.compile`) would significantly reduce P99 latency for repeated evaluations. Consider a future enhancement to switch to `re.search` with pre-compilation if patterns become more advanced.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency:**
    *   **Task 2.1: Document existing idempotency.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Functions:** `string_match`, `url_match`, `evaluate_task`
        *   **Description:** The functions `string_match`, `url_match`, and `evaluate_task` are already structurally idempotent. They are pure functions: given the same inputs, they will always produce the same outputs without causing any side effects. No modifications are needed to achieve idempotency within this module. Add a docstring or comment to `evaluate_task` explicitly stating its idempotent nature.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines:**
    *   **Task 3.1: Integrate `evaluate_task` for real-time agentic self-correction.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Function:** `evaluate_task`
        *   **Description:** Design upstream agent logic to leverage the detailed pass/fail results from `evaluate_task` beyond simple post-hoc grading. For Operon, this evaluation should trigger:
            *   **Contextual Retry/Re-planning:** If `evaluate_task` returns `False`, the agent should not just fail, but analyze *which* `eval_type` failed (e.g., "url_match" vs. "string_match"). This specific failure signal can inform a new action sequence, a targeted retry, or a re-evaluation of its current plan based on the perceived discrepancy (e.g., "I'm on the wrong page" vs. "The text I expect isn't visible").
            *   **Progress Monitoring & Early Stopping:** The `evaluate_task` logic (or a subset of it) should be callable at intermediate steps of an agent's task execution to verify progress towards sub-goals. If an intermediate `url_match` or `string_match` fails, the agent can abort a suboptimal path early, saving computational resources and reducing overall task latency, rather than completing a doomed sequence of actions.
    *   **Task 3.2: Implement adaptive learning from `evaluate_task` failures.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Function:** `evaluate_task`
        *   **Description:** Capture detailed telemetry (visual state, agent actions, `eval_type` results from `evaluate_task`) for every failure. Develop a learning mechanism (e.g., reinforcement learning, case-based reasoning) that analyzes these failures over time to identify common root causes and autonomously improve the agent's decision-making and planning heuristics for future tasks. This goes beyond simple retry by enabling the agent to become more robust and efficient.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants:**
    *   **Task 4.1: Confirm compliance with Operon's invariants.**
        *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py`
        *   **Description:** The current module `src\benchmarks\webarena_eval.py` *itself* does not violate Operon's core invariants:
            *   **No DOM/selectors:** It consumes `final_url` and `final_text` as parameters, implying these were extracted by an upstream process. It does not parse or manipulate a DOM.
            *   **Atomic focus+type:** This module is for evaluation, not interaction.
            *   **Visual servo:** This module is for evaluation, not control.
        *   **Action:** No code changes are required within this module. However, it is critical that the upstream components responsible for deriving `final_url` and `final_text` for Operon strictly adhere to the "vision-only, zero-abstraction" principle, meaning these values must be extracted purely from visual input without reliance on DOM or other high-level browser abstractions. The provision of these as direct string parameters to `evaluate_task` in this benchmark implies this prerequisite.

## `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
