1. Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

**Context:** Operon requires extremely low latency for its real-time inference loop. Pydantic model validation and instantiation can contribute to P99 latency, especially under high load or with complex data.

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize Model Instantiation with `slots=True`**
    *   **Action:** For all Pydantic models (`WebArenaEval`, `WebArenaTask`, `WebArenaTaskResult`, `WebArenaSummary`), add `slots=True` to their `model_config` to reduce memory footprint and improve attribute access speed, which can positively impact P99 latency.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaEval`, `WebArenaTask`, `WebArenaTaskResult`, `WebArenaSummary`
    *   **Example:**
        ```python
        class WebArenaEval(BaseModel):
            model_config = ConfigDict(extra="forbid", slots=True) # Add slots=True
            # ...
        ```
*   **Task 1.2: Consider Pre-computation/Caching for `WebArenaSummary`**
    *   **Action:** While `WebArenaSummary` itself is a model, its aggregation logic (not shown here) should leverage pre-computation or caching mechanisms if summaries are frequently requested or updated. If `WebArenaSummary` is often re-computed from a large list of `WebArenaTaskResult` instances, ensure the underlying aggregation logic is optimized and avoids redundant calculations. This is an architectural consideration for where this model is used.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py` (Indirectly, as it concerns how `WebArenaSummary` is populated)
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaSummary` (and any related summary generation logic)
    *   **Note:** This task focuses on the implications of the model's structure for latency during data aggregation, not the model definition itself.
*   **Task 1.3: Ensure Pydantic V2 Compiled Validation is Utilized**
    *   **Action:** Confirm that the deployment environment for Operon leverages Pydantic V2's Rust-compiled core for model validation and serialization. No code change is needed in this module, but it's a critical configuration for optimal P99.
    *   **File:** (Configuration/Deployment pipeline, not this module)
    *   **Function/Class:** All Pydantic models in `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`

---

### **2. Structural Idempotency**

**Context:** Operon's workflow involves potentially re-processing or re-submitting task results. Idempotent structures ensure that such operations do not lead to inconsistent or duplicate states.

*   **Task 2.1: Enforce Unique Task Run Identification**
    *   **Action:** Ensure that the combination of `task_id` and `run_id` in `WebArenaTaskResult` is treated as a primary key or unique identifier in any storage or processing layer. This allows for idempotent updates (overwrite existing result) rather than creating duplicates if a result is submitted multiple times.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTaskResult`
    *   **Note:** This is a guideline for how the model should be *used* in an external system (e.g., database, message queue consumer), not a direct change to the model definition itself, which already provides the necessary fields.
*   **Task 2.2: Idempotent Summary Aggregation**
    *   **Action:** When populating or updating `WebArenaSummary.tasks` (a list of `WebArenaTaskResult`), ensure the aggregation logic is idempotent. If `WebArenaTaskResult` instances are added to the list, they should be de-duplicated or merged based on `task_id` and `run_id` to prevent redundant entries and maintain accurate counts in `total`, `passed`, `by_category`, etc.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py` (Indirectly, concerns how `WebArenaSummary` is populated)
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaSummary` (and any related summary generation logic)

---

### **3. Agentic Features (Beyond Standard Workflow Engines)**

**Context:** Operon is an intelligent agent. Its task and result models should facilitate advanced agentic behaviors beyond simple execution and state tracking.

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Adaptive Strategy Refinement**
    *   **Action:** Develop an agentic feedback loop where the `eval_types_result`, `duration_seconds`, and `stop_reason` from `WebArenaTaskResult` are used to inform and adapt Operon's strategy for future tasks with similar `site`, `category`, and `intent`. For example, if a certain `eval_type` consistently fails for a given `category`, the agent should learn to prioritize alternative approaches for that category.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py` (The models provide the data; the agent uses it)
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTaskResult`, `WebArenaTask` (for context)
    *   **Detail:** This goes beyond simple retry logic; it implies learning and modifying the agent's internal planning or execution parameters.
*   **Task 3.2: Develop Proactive Anomaly Detection & Self-Diagnosis**
    *   **Action:** The agent should continuously monitor `duration_seconds` and `stop_reason` in `WebArenaTaskResult` data streams. Significant deviations from historical patterns (e.g., unusually long `duration_seconds` for a 'medium' difficulty task, or a novel `stop_reason`) should trigger internal self-diagnosis routines or alert mechanisms, allowing Operon to proactively investigate internal issues or external environment changes (e.g., website redesign).
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py` (The models provide the data)
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTaskResult`
*   **Task 3.3: Enable Goal-Oriented Re-planning upon Failure**
    *   **Action:** If `WebArenaTaskResult.passed` is `False`, the agent should not merely report failure. Instead, it should analyze the `WebArenaTask.intent` and the granular `WebArenaTaskResult.eval_types_result` to understand *why* the intent was not fulfilled. This analysis should lead to a targeted re-planning phase, potentially modifying the original `WebArenaTask` (e.g., by adding specific `tags` for new strategies or breaking down the `intent` into sub-goals) rather than a blind retry.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTask`, `WebArenaTaskResult`

---

### **4. Operon Invariants Violations**

**Context:** Operon operates under strict invariants: vision-only, zero-abstraction, no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, and visual servo. Any data field implying a deviation from these principles needs to be flagged.

*   **Task 4.1: Clarify `extracted_text_excerpt` Data Acquisition Method**
    *   **Action:** Review the intended method for populating `WebArenaTaskResult.extracted_text_excerpt`. Ensure that text excerpts are obtained *exclusively* via visual servo and OCR (i.e., by visually identifying a region on the screen and processing its pixels), without relying on DOM parsing, `innerText`, or similar abstraction layers. The term "excerpt" often implies content-centric extraction, which could implicitly suggest DOM access.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTaskResult.extracted_text_excerpt`
    *   **Flag Severity:** **High Potential Violation** (requires strict enforcement of visual-only acquisition).
*   **Task 4.2: Clarify `extracted_url` Data Acquisition Method**
    *   **Action:** Review the intended method for populating `WebArenaTaskResult.extracted_url`. Ensure that the extracted URL is obtained *exclusively* via visual servo (e.g., by OCRing the browser's address bar or visually identified link text/QR codes), and not through programmatic access to browser APIs or DOM `href` attributes.
    *   **File:** `src\benchmarks\webarena_models.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `WebArenaTaskResult.extracted_url`
    *   **Flag Severity:** **Medium Potential Violation** (requires strict enforcement of visual-only acquisition).

## `src\clients\anthropic.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Task**: Reduce P99 latency by converting blocking file I/O to asynchronous operations for image loading.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `generate_verification`
    *   **Action**: Modify `image_path.read_bytes()` to use an asynchronous file reading library (e.g., `aiofiles`) to prevent blocking the event loop. This ensures disk I/O does not contribute to P99 latency spikes.

2.  **Task**: Reduce P99 latency by offloading CPU-intensive image encoding.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `generate_verification`
    *   **Action**: For potentially large images, consider moving the `base64.b64encode` operation to a separate thread or process pool (e.g., using `run_in_executor`) to avoid blocking the main event loop, especially under heavy load. This prevents a single CPU-bound task from impacting overall real-time responsiveness.

3.  **Task**: Reduce P99 latency and improve perceived responsiveness by implementing streaming responses.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `_post_message`
    *   **Action**: Modify the `client.post` call and subsequent response handling to leverage Anthropic's streaming API (if applicable for the model's output type) and `httpx`'s async iteration over responses. This allows Operon to start processing partial results sooner, improving perceived latency for long generations. The `_extract_text` function will need to be adapted to handle streamed chunks.

4.  **Task**: Reduce P99 latency variability and improve resilience through a more robust retry strategy.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `_post_message`
    *   **Action**: Replace the fixed `retry_backoff_seconds * attempt` with a jittered exponential backoff strategy. This prevents thundering herd problems on retries and provides a more effective adaptive delay, which is critical for maintaining P99 performance under transient network or service issues.

5.  **Task**: Ensure structural idempotency and thread safety for internal state.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `_post_message`, `latest_usage`
    *   **Action**: The `_last_usage` instance variable is a mutable shared state. If multiple concurrent `_post_message` calls use the same `AnthropicHttpClient` instance, `_last_usage` can be non-deterministically overwritten, violating expected state consistency for `latest_usage()`. Rework this to either:
        *   Return `ModelUsage` directly from `generate_policy` and `generate_verification` methods.
        *   Use a thread-safe mechanism (e.g., `asyncio.Lock` if `latest_usage` is frequently accessed concurrently) or store usage statistics in a dedicated, per-request context object if usage tracking is critical across concurrent operations. This makes the internal state management more robust and predictable.

6.  **Task**: Introduce agentic dynamic model selection and routing.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `AnthropicHttpClient.__init__`, `generate_policy`, `generate_verification`
    *   **Action**: Implement logic that allows the agent to dynamically select or route to different Anthropic models (e.g., "claude-haiku" for low-latency, "claude-opus" for high-accuracy critical tasks, or even smaller local models not included here) based on inferred task complexity, current system load, user-defined latency budgets, or cost constraints. This goes beyond a fixed `self.model` and enables self-optimizing behavior.

7.  **Task**: Implement agentic adaptive retry and timeout adjustments.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `_post_message`
    *   **Action**: Augment the retry logic to adapt `timeout_seconds` and `retry_backoff_seconds` based on observed latency patterns, historical success rates, and specific error codes (e.g., increasing timeout slightly if `429 Too Many Requests` is frequent, or decreasing it aggressively if `50x Gateway Timeout` is sustained). This enables the client to "learn" and adjust its resilience strategy in real-time.

8.  **Task**: Enhance agentic error intelligence and recovery.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Function**: `_post_message`
    *   **Action**: Beyond basic `retryable` status codes, analyze the `detail = response.text` for specific error messages (e.g., "invalid input format," "context window exceeded"). An agent could then trigger corrective actions like:
        *   Automatically truncating or summarizing prompts.
        *   Reformatting input for a retry.
        *   Switching to a model with a larger context window.
        *   Escalating the error to a higher-level agent for human intervention or a different strategy.

9.  **Task**: Confirm adherence to Operon's invariants.
    *   **File**: `src\clients\anthropic.py`
    *   **Action**: No direct violations of Operon's invariants ("no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo") are present within this module. This module acts purely as an HTTP client for an external LLM, consuming prompts and image data (screenshots) and producing text outputs. It does not perform any UI interaction itself. It's crucial that the *components providing the screenshots* and *consuming the generated text policies/verifications* adhere to these invariants.

## `src\clients\gemini.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task:** Offload the `base64.b64encode` operation for large image/video payloads to a thread pool to prevent blocking the event loop. This is critical for P99 latency, especially with potentially large visual inputs.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `_build_perception_payload`
        *   **Action:** Modify `_build_perception_payload` to accept `image_bytes` (which is already pre-read/optimized) and use `await asyncio.to_thread(base64.b64encode, image_bytes)` for the encoding step.
    *   **Task:** Consider a more performant image processing library if `PIL` proves to be a P99 bottleneck under heavy load or with very large screenshots. While `asyncio.to_thread` helps, raw processing speed is still a factor.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `_optimize_screenshot`
        *   **Action:** Research and evaluate alternatives to `PIL` (e.g., `Pillow-SIMD` or other Rust/C++ bindings) for potential integration if profiling indicates `_optimize_screenshot` consistently dominates P99 latency. This is a longer-term investigation.
    *   **Task:** Evaluate the `retry_backoff_seconds` and `max_retries` configuration, particularly for P99 latency. While useful for robustness, a fixed `0.5s` backoff with `2` retries adds `0.5s` and `1.0s` (total `1.5s`) to the request path for tail latencies.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `GeminiHttpClient.__init__`, `_post_json_payload`
        *   **Action:** Add options for an exponential backoff strategy with jitter (e.g., `(2**attempt * retry_base_backoff) + random_jitter`) for retries in `_post_json_payload`. This makes retries more efficient and less likely to overwhelm the downstream service while providing robustness. Update `retry_backoff_seconds` to `retry_base_backoff`.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task:** Enhance client-side traceability for retried requests by generating a unique client-side request ID and including it in logs. While the Gemini API itself doesn't offer direct idempotency keys for `generateContent` in the payload, adding a client-side ID to logs helps in debugging and understanding request lifecycle, even if the backend processes multiple instances.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `_post_json_payload`
        *   **Action:** Generate a `uuid.uuid4()` at the beginning of `_post_json_payload` and include it in all warning/error logs related to retries. This helps correlate multiple attempts of the "same" logical request.
    *   **Task:** Consider adding an optional, configurable input caching mechanism for `generate_perception` and `generate_policy` if the agent logic frequently sends identical prompts/screenshots within a short timeframe. This would make repeated identical requests effectively idempotent at the client level.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `generate_perception`, `generate_policy`
        *   **Action:** Implement a simple in-memory `LRU` cache (e.g., using `functools.lru_cache` or a custom `dict` with size limits) that maps a hash of `(prompt, screenshot_path/video_path)` to the last successful response. Include a `ttl` for cache entries to prevent stale data. This should be an opt-in feature, as most Operon perceptions are likely unique per frame.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **Task:** Implement a dynamic model selection/fallback mechanism. This enables the agent to adapt to changing performance, cost, or availability of Gemini models.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `GeminiHttpClient.__init__`, `_post_json_payload`
        *   **Action:**
            1.  Modify `__init__` to accept a list of `model_preferences: list[str]` instead of a single `model`.
            2.  In `_post_json_payload`, iterate through `model_preferences` on failure (e.g., timeout, 429, 5xx) to attempt the request with an alternative model, logging the switch. The first model in the list is the preferred one.
            3.  Introduce a mechanism (e.g., an internal `disabled_models` set with a `re-enable_timeout`) to temporarily "blacklist" models that are consistently failing, allowing them to recover before being retried.
    *   **Task:** Implement a circuit breaker pattern for the Gemini API connection. This prevents the agent from continually hammering a failing upstream service and allows for recovery.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `_post_json_payload`
        *   **Action:** Integrate a circuit breaker library (e.g., `pybreaker` or custom logic) around the `client.post` call in `_post_json_payload`. Configure it to open the circuit after a threshold of consecutive failures, block requests for a set period, and then allow a single "half-open" request to test for recovery.
    *   **Task:** Introduce adaptive prompt refinement or re-planning on structured response parsing failures. If the LLM consistently returns invalid JSON or "no text part," the agent should try to self-correct its interaction strategy.
        *   **File:** `src/clients/gemini.py`
        *   **Function:** `extract_text`, `_post_json_payload`
        *   **Action:**
            1.  In `extract_text` (and similar parsing logic), if a `GeminiClientError` related to JSON parsing or missing content occurs, enrich the error with the raw `response_body` (truncated if too large).
            2.  In `_post_json_payload`, catch `GeminiClientError` specifically for parsing issues. If caught, consider automatically adding a "strict JSON formatting" instruction to the prompt for a subsequent retry (if the prompt is for policy/perception generation and not video verification). This is a higher-level agentic response.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Invariant Check:** No direct violations of Operon's invariants (`no DOM/selectors`, `atomic focus+type`, `visual servo`) are present within this `src/clients/gemini.py` module.
    *   **Rationale:**
        *   The module acts as a low-level interface to an external LLM, handling input/output formats (screenshots, JSON) that are consistent with Operon's principles.
        *   It does not perform any interaction with the environment itself, nor does it interpret DOM structures.
        *   The `generate_perception` and `generate_policy` methods facilitate the "observe" and "decide" steps of a visual servo loop.
        *   The module expects and produces JSON, which is a neutral format. The *content* of this JSON (e.g., policy instructions) would need to adhere to the `atomic focus+type` invariant when consumed by other Operon modules, but this client does not generate or process DOM/selectors itself.
    *   **Action:** No specific action required within this module regarding invariants. However, downstream modules consuming the JSON output *must* ensure that the generated policy adheres to `atomic focus+type` and avoids `DOM/selectors`.

## `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Category:** P99 Latency Reduction
    **Task:** Implement asynchronous file I/O for reading image bytes to prevent blocking the event loop.
    **Function(s) Affected:**
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_build_user_content`
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::build_function_response_content`
    **Details/Reasoning:** `image_path.read_bytes()` is a synchronous operation that can become a bottleneck for larger images, increasing P99 latency. Use `asyncio.to_thread` or an `aiofiles` library for non-blocking file access.

2.  **Category:** P99 Latency Reduction
    **Task:** Offload the base64 encoding process to a separate thread for improved concurrency, especially for larger image payloads.
    **Function(s) Affected:**
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_build_user_content`
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::build_function_response_content`
    **Details/Reasoning:** `base64.b64encode(...).decode("utf-8")` is a CPU-bound operation. Performing it synchronously can block the event loop, contributing to higher P99 latency. Wrap this operation with `asyncio.to_thread`.

3.  **Category:** P99 Latency Reduction
    **Task:** Optimize image processing by introducing image resizing and/or compression before base64 encoding to reduce payload size.
    **Function(s) Affected:**
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_build_user_content`
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::build_function_response_content`
    **Details/Reasoning:** Smaller image payloads lead to faster network transmission and potentially quicker model inference. While Operon is vision-only, there's a trade-off between visual fidelity and latency. Introduce configurable image processing steps (e.g., using Pillow) to find the optimal balance. This processing should also be offloaded to a thread pool.

4.  **Category:** P99 Latency Reduction
    **Task:** Consider pre-warming the `httpx.AsyncClient` connection pool upon client initialization if inference requests are bursty.
    **Function(s) Affected:** `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_get_client`
    **Details/Reasoning:** The `_get_client` method initializes the client on first use. For real-time applications with bursty demand, the initial connection setup can add to the P99 latency of the very first request. A small, asynchronous pre-warm could mitigate this.

5.  **Category:** P99 Latency Reduction
    **Task:** Review and fine-tune `max_retries` and `retry_backoff_seconds` for real-time constraints.
    **Function(s) Affected:**
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::__init__`
    *   `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_post_payload`
    **Details/Reasoning:** While retries improve reliability, they directly increase latency on failure paths. For highly real-time scenarios, it might be beneficial to fail faster or use more aggressive backoff (e.g., shorter delays) for specific transient errors, or even implement a more sophisticated circuit breaker (see agentic features).

6.  **Category:** Structural Idempotency
    **Task:** No specific structural changes for idempotency are needed within this module beyond current implementation.
    **Function(s) Affected:** N/A
    **Details/Reasoning:** The `_build_payload`, `_build_user_content`, `build_function_response_content`, and `_normalize_response` methods are pure functions of their inputs, ensuring their idempotency. The `_last_usage` state is updated conditionally upon successful API response, which is appropriate. The API call `generateContent` itself, while producing new inference results, is effectively idempotent for identical inputs (given `temperature=0`). The retry mechanism in `_post_payload` handles transient errors robustly.

7.  **Category:** Agentic Features
    **Task:** Implement an adaptive retry strategy and a circuit breaker pattern for `_post_payload`.
    **Function(s) Affected:** `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_post_payload`
    **Details/Reasoning:** Instead of fixed retries, dynamically adjust backoff and `max_retries` based on error types (e.g., exponential for 429/5xx, fail-fast for authentication 4xx). A circuit breaker (e.g., using `pybreaker`) will prevent hammering a failing API, allowing it to recover and improving overall system stability. This goes beyond standard workflow engines by dynamically adapting to external service health.

8.  **Category:** Agentic Features
    **Task:** Introduce dynamic adjustment of `httpx.Limits` based on observed latency and system resource utilization.
    **Function(s) Affected:** `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::_get_client`
    **Details/Reasoning:** The current `max_connections` and `max_keepalive_connections` are static. An agentic system would monitor its own performance (e.g., P99 latency for API calls, CPU load) and adapt these limits. For instance, if latency is high but CPU is idle, it might cautiously increase limits; if CPU is saturated, it might reduce them.

9.  **Category:** Agentic Features
    **Task:** Explore implementing an intelligent, short-term, in-memory cache for highly repetitive or common `generate_turn` requests.
    **Function(s) Affected:** `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::generate_turn`
    **Details/Reasoning:** For "visual servo" actions, there might be recurring visual states or prompts that frequently lead to the same function call (e.g., "scroll down" on a static page). Caching these responses locally could drastically reduce latency for such turns. The cache invalidation strategy would be critical, possibly tied to detected visual changes or an explicit model instruction.

10. **Category:** Agentic Features
    **Task:** Enhance error reporting from `GeminiComputerUseError` to include structured error codes or richer context.
    **Function(s) Affected:** `src\clients\gemini_computer_use.py::GeminiComputerUseError` (and its raising points)
    **Details/Reasoning:** A more sophisticated agent can implement self-healing workflows if it understands the *nature* of a failure. For example, if a specific error code indicates an issue with image format, the agent could automatically try a different compression. If it indicates an API quota issue, it could implement a fallback or pause. This provides the agent higher fidelity signals for adaptive recovery.

11. **Category:** Invariants Violation
    **Task:** No violations of Operon's invariants (no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo) detected in this module.
    **Function(s) Affected:** N/A
    **Details/Reasoning:** This module acts as a communication layer with the Gemini model. It correctly sends visual input (screenshots) and expects structured function calls in return. It does not perform any DOM manipulation or rely on selectors itself. The functions it enables (`_build_user_content` and `build_function_response_content` sending screenshots, `_normalize_response` parsing function calls) are foundational for a vision-only, visual servo-driven agent. The responsibility for "atomic focus+type" and the actual "visual servo" loop lies with the higher-level Operon agent components that *consume* the output of this client.

This will reduce the cold-start latency for the first action. Consider a configurable pool size.

        *   **Description:** Replace hardcoded `asyncio.sleep` values (e.g., `self._post_action_delay`, `_action_delay`, `await asyncio.sleep(1.0)` after `NAVIGATE`, `await asyncio.sleep(1.5)` after `_bring_browser_to_foreground`, `await asyncio.sleep(0.5)` in `_foreground_if_fresh_session`, and the `0.2s` retries in `_bring_browser_to_foreground`) with intelligent waits. These waits should block until a visual stability metric is met, a specific visual change is detected (e.g., perceived loading animation disappearance, target element becoming interactable visually), or Playwright's `networkidle` event occurs, rather than arbitrary time. This will ensure actions proceed as soon as the environment is ready, not after a fixed, often over-cautious, delay.
    *   **Task:** Optimize screenshot capture latency for `capture` and `_capture_after`.

Ensure `_write_blank_png` is handled asynchronously if it involves substantial CPU/disk I/O or replace `cv2.imwrite` with an asynchronous equivalent if it becomes a bottleneck.

        *   **Description:** Wrap the file writing operation `with open(output_path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as fh:` within `await asyncio.to_thread(...)` to prevent blocking the event loop, especially for large file writes.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency:**
    *   **Task:** Implement executor-level retry logic for transient Playwright errors.
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`

        *   **Description:** Augment the `try...except Exception` block in `execute` to distinguish between transient (e.g., network timeout, element detached, browser crash) and permanent failures. For transient failures, implement a configurable number of retries with exponential backoff. This adds robustness to individual action execution, making the executor more resilient to flaky browser states.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines:**
    *   **Task:** Integrate visual-based action verification and adaptive recovery.
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (post-action logic)
        *   **Description:** After any action that modifies the UI (e.g., `CLICK`, `TYPE`, `NAVIGATE`), capture a `CaptureFrame` and pass it to an external visual perception module. The executor should then, based on the *visual feedback* from this module, confirm the action's success. If the visual feedback indicates failure or an unexpected state (e.g., a popup appeared, element didn't disappear), the executor should be able to trigger a pre-defined adaptive recovery sequence (e.g., close popup, scroll, re-evaluate action target based on current visual state). This moves beyond simple Playwright exceptions to intelligent, visual-driven self-healing.
    *   **Task:** Implement proactive, context-aware browser session management.
