        *   **Description:** Extend the session management to support more complex scenarios:
            *   **Pre-authenticated sessions:** Allow `_ensure_session` to accept authentication credentials or pre-configured cookies, so an agent can request a session that's already logged in to specific services.
            *   **Session "tagging":** Allow `run_id`s or sessions to be tagged with semantic meaning (e.g., "shopping-cart-session," "admin-panel-session"). The executor could then apply specific browser configurations (e.g., user-agent, proxy) or even retain these "persistent" sessions across multiple `run_id`s for efficiency, beyond just closing "other" sessions.
    *   **Task:** Dynamic and learned post-action delays.
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `_action_delay`
        *   **Description:** Replace the static `delays` dictionary with a mechanism that allows the agent to dynamically adjust post-action delays based on observed system performance, network conditions, or even learned patterns from past execution successes/failures. This could involve an external feedback loop that provides optimal delays.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants:**
    *   **Violation Type:** No DOM/selectors
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.CLICK)
        *   **Code Line:** `await page.locator(action.selector).first.click(timeout=5000)`
        *   **Description:** Direct use of CSS `selector` for clicking. This violates the "no DOM/selectors" invariant. All element targeting must be visual-servo driven or by atomic visual ID.
    *   **Violation Type:** No DOM/selectors
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.UPLOAD_FILE)
        *   **Code Line:** `await page.locator("input[type=file]").first.click(force=True)`
        *   **Description:** Direct use of CSS `selector` for clicking an input. This violates the "no DOM/selectors" invariant.
    *   **Violation Type:** No DOM/selectors
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.READ_TEXT)
        *   **Code Line:** `css = action.selector or "main, article, #content, body"` and subsequent `await page.evaluate(..., css)`
        *   **Description:** Direct use of CSS `selector`s and `document.querySelector` for text extraction. This is a clear violation of the "no DOM/selectors" invariant. Text extraction must derive from a visual understanding or a direct programmatic accessibility API that does not rely on DOM structure.
    *   **Violation Type:** No DOM/selectors
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.UPLOAD_FILE_NATIVE)
        *   **Code Line:** `elif action.selector is not None: await page.locator(action.selector).first.click()` and `elif action.target_element_id is not None: await page.locator(self._target_element_locator(action.target_element_id)).first.click()`
        *   **Description:** Both `action.selector` and the internal construction of a CSS selector via `_target_element_locator` for `target_element_id` violate the "no DOM/selectors" invariant.
    *   **Violation Type:** Visual Servo (General)
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.CLICK, HOVER, TYPE, PRESS_KEY, DRAG, UPLOAD_FILE, UPLOAD_FILE_NATIVE)
        *   **Code Line:** All operations that rely on `action.x, action.y` or `_action_point` (derived from `target_context.original_target`).
        *   **Description:** Relying on fixed `x,y` coordinates or bounding box centroids (derived from `original_target`) for interaction is a violation of the "visual servo" invariant. Visual servo implies real-time visual localization and tracking of the target element, adapting to its movement or changes in layout. The current implementation assumes static coordinates or that Playwright's selectors handle dynamic positioning, neither of which is a true visual servo.
    *   **Violation Type:** Atomic Focus+Type
        *   **File:** `src\executor\browser_native.py`
        *   **Function:** `execute` (ActionType.TYPE, PRESS_KEY)
        *   **Code Line:** `if point is not None: await page.mouse.click(*point)` followed by `await page.keyboard.type(action.text)` or `await page.keyboard.press(key)`
        *   **Description:** This sequence is two distinct operations (click then type/press), not an atomic one. If the click fails to focus the *intended* element, or focuses an incorrect element due to UI changes, the subsequent typing will occur in the wrong place. True "atomic focus+type" would ensure focus on the visually identified target and then perform the typing in a single, verified step.

## `src\executor\browserbase_native.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**

1. **Optimize Browserbase Session Creation Workflow**
    *   **Problem:** The `_ensure_session` method sequentially makes multiple remote calls (`bb.sessions.create`, then `bb.sessions.debug`) to provision a Browserbase session and retrieve its CDP URL. This adds cumulative latency.
    *   **Suggestion:** Investigate whether the Browserbase API offers a single, more efficient call to create a session and directly return the CDP WebSocket URL, or if these calls can be parallelized or batched.
    *   **Action:** Refactor `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_ensure_session` to minimize the number of sequential remote Browserbase API calls required for session setup.

2. **Implement Asynchronous Browserbase API Client**
    *   **Problem:** The current `browserbase` library calls (`bb.sessions.create`, `bb.sessions.debug`, `bb.sessions.update`) are synchronous, blocking the asyncio event loop and potentially increasing P99 latency.
    *   **Suggestion:** Develop or integrate an asynchronous client for Browserbase API interactions to ensure all remote calls are non-blocking and compatible with the existing `asyncio` environment.
    *   **Action:** Create an `async` wrapper or an entirely new asynchronous client for Browserbase API operations within `src/executor/browserbase_native.py`, and modify `_ensure_session` and `_stop_bb_session` to use it.

3. **Implement Proactive Session Pre-warming**
    *   **Problem:** Browserbase sessions are created on demand in `_ensure_session`, leading to significant cold-start latency for the first action of a new `run_id`.
    *   **Suggestion:** Introduce logic to proactively create and maintain a small pool of "ready" Browserbase sessions in the background, making them available for immediate assignment to new `run_id`s, thereby reducing initial action latency.
    *   **Action:** Add a new asynchronous method, e.g., `_prewarm_session_pool`, to `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor`, to be initiated during executor startup or by an external orchestrator. This method should manage a configurable number of pre-connected `_BrowserSession` objects.

4. **Refine Asynchronous Teardown in Error Handling**
    *   **Problem:** The `asyncio.get_event_loop()` and `loop.run_until_complete()` logic in `_evict_dead_session` is fragile. It might block the event loop if called incorrectly or lead to errors if no loop is running or if `create_task` is used in an unsuitable context.
    *   **Suggestion:** Ensure graceful, non-blocking asynchronous teardown of the Playwright session handle that doesn't rely on specific event loop state assumptions. A more robust approach would be to always schedule cleanup as an `asyncio.Task` if an event loop is known to be active, or ensure `playwright.stop()` is handled within an already-running loop.
    *   **Action:** Refactor `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_evict_dead_session` to use a more resilient and non-blocking Playwright `stop()` mechanism, potentially scheduling it as a detached task if an event loop is present.

5. **Introduce Tunable Timeouts for All Remote Operations**
    *   **Problem:** Critical remote operations (Browserbase API calls, Playwright CDP connection) lack explicit, configurable timeouts, which can cause long tail latencies if external services are slow or unresponsive.
    *   **Suggestion:** Implement distinct, configurable timeouts for each remote call, allowing for aggressive tuning to meet real-time inference requirements.
    *   **Action:** Modify `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_ensure_session` and `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_stop_bb_session` to accept and apply timeout parameters to `bb.sessions.create`, `bb.sessions.debug`, `playwright.chromium.connect_over_cdp`, and `bb.sessions.update`.

---

**2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

1. **Ensure Idempotent Browserbase Session Creation**
    *   **Problem:** While `_ensure_session` checks for an existing local session, if multiple concurrent calls for the same `run_id` occur *before* a local session is established but *after* the `bb.sessions.create` call, it could lead to multiple Browserbase sessions being requested for the same logical run.
    *   **Suggestion:** Implement a mechanism (e.g., an `asyncio.Lock` or a dictionary mapping `run_id` to a pending `asyncio.Task`) within `_ensure_session` to ensure only one Browserbase session creation request is in flight for a given `run_id` at any moment.
    *   **Action:** Add a concurrency control mechanism to `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_ensure_session` around the `bb.sessions.create` and `bb.sessions.debug` calls to prevent redundant Browserbase API calls for the same `run_id`.

2. **Verify and Handle Idempotent Browserbase Session Release**
    *   **Problem:** `_stop_bb_session` locally manages `_bb_session_ids` to prevent redundant `Browserbase` API calls. The `bb.sessions.update(bb_sid, status="REQUEST_RELEASE")` call to Browserbase should ideally be idempotent at the API level (i.e., calling it multiple times on an already-released session should have no ill effect).
    *   **Suggestion:** Confirm with Browserbase API documentation or through testing that calling `bb.sessions.update(bb_sid, status="REQUEST_RELEASE")` on an already-released session is a no-op or handled gracefully. If not, add explicit client-side checks to prevent redundant API requests.
    *   **Action:** Document the idempotency behavior of Browserbase session release or add a conditional check within `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_stop_bb_session` to prevent re-releasing an already-released Browserbase session if the API isn't inherently idempotent.

---

**3. Agentic Features (Beyond Standard Workflow Engines)**

1. **Proactive Session Health Monitoring and Self-Healing**
    *   **Problem:** Session eviction (`_evict_dead_session`) is purely reactive, triggered only *after* an agent action fails due to a closed session. This introduces latency and wastes computational effort.
    *   **Suggestion:** Implement a background asynchronous task that periodically pings or performs lightweight health checks on *active* Browserbase CDP connections (e.g., `page.evaluate('1+1')`) to detect impending failures or connection issues proactively. Unhealthy sessions should be gracefully replaced with new pre-warmed sessions *before* an agent attempts to use them.
    *   **Action:** Add a new asynchronous method, e.g., `_monitor_session_health`, to `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor`, to run concurrently and proactively manage the health of active `_BrowserSession` instances.

2. **Adaptive Session Allocation and Cost Optimization**
    *   **Problem:** The current session management is reactive and does not explicitly optimize for resource cost or dynamically adapt to varying workloads.
    *   **Suggestion:** Implement logic that dynamically adjusts the number of pre-warmed sessions (Task 1.3) based on observed inference request rates, historical patterns, or predictive models. Introduce configurable idle timeouts to automatically release Browserbase sessions that remain unused for a specified period, balancing latency with cost efficiency.
    *   **Action:** Extend `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor` with configuration for session idle timeouts and implement a new internal method, e.g., `_manage_session_pool_size`, to dynamically adjust the number of active/idle sessions.

3. **Intelligent Failure Analysis and Adaptive Strategy**
    *   **Problem:** The `_is_session_closed` check is a simple pattern match, treating all session closure exceptions uniformly. This limits the system's ability to learn and adapt.
    *   **Suggestion:** Enhance failure analysis to categorize exceptions more granularly (e.g., transient network issue, Browserbase service error, Playwright internal error). Log this detailed telemetry. Use this data to inform adaptive retry strategies (e.g., exponential backoff for network issues, immediate re-provisioning from a different region for hard service failures) or even to dynamically select Browserbase instance types for future sessions.
    *   **Action:** Augment `src/executor/browserbase_native.py::_is_session_closed` and the exception handlers in `capture` and `execute` to perform more detailed error parsing, categorization, and logging, providing hooks for more sophisticated adaptive logic.

---

**4. Violations of Operon's Invariants**

1. **Ensure Zero DOM/Selectors Usage in AgentAction and Parent Executor**
    *   **Problem:** Operon's core invariant is "vision-only, zero-abstraction," meaning no DOM, selectors, or direct element references are used by the agent. While `BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor` itself does not directly use selectors, it provides a Playwright `page` object capable of DOM interaction. The integrity of this invariant relies on the `AgentAction` model (`src/models/policy.AgentAction`) and the parent `NativeBrowserExecutor`'s implementation of `execute()` (`src/executor/browser_native.py`).
    *   **Suggestion:** Rigorously audit `src/models/policy.AgentAction` and `src/executor/browser_native.py::NativeBrowserExecutor.execute` to ensure no DOM selectors, XPath expressions, element IDs, or other browser-internal abstractions are present in the `AgentAction` model or used by the executor. All interactions must be strictly based on visual coordinates or other vision-derived primitives.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Inspect:** Examine `src/models/policy.AgentAction` for any fields (e.g., `selector`, `element_id`, `xpath`) that would imply DOM interaction.
        2.  **Inspect:** Examine `src/executor/browser_native.py::NativeBrowserExecutor.execute` (the parent's method that this module calls via `super().execute()`) to verify it only uses `page` methods that accept visual coordinates (e.g., `page.mouse.click(x, y)`) and avoids any methods that query or interact with the DOM using selectors (e.g., `page.click('css=button')`, `page.fill('#my_input', 'text')`).
        3.  **Refactor (if necessary):** If any violations are found in `AgentAction` or `NativeBrowserExecutor.execute`, modify them to strictly adhere to vision-only, coordinate-based interaction.

2. **Verify Atomic Focus+Type and Visual Servo Enforcement**
    *   **Problem:** Operon requires interactions like focusing an element and typing into it to be atomic from the agent's perspective, driven by continuous visual servo feedback. The `BrowserbaseNativeBrowserExecutor` provides the low-level `page` object, but the `NativeBrowserExecutor.execute()` method, and by extension the `AgentAction` model, must ensure these principles are upheld.
    *   **Suggestion:** Confirm that the `AgentAction` model and the `NativeBrowserExecutor.execute()` implementation expose and use action primitives that are compatible with or enforce atomic focus+type and visual servo principles (e.g., a single action representing a visually-guided click followed by text input, with implicit visual confirmation).
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Inspect:** Review `src/models/policy.AgentAction` to ensure that input actions (e.g., typing) are designed to be atomic with their preceding focus/click events, ideally expressed as a single, visually-derived instruction.
        2.  **Inspect:** Review `src/executor/browser_native.py::NativeBrowserExecutor.execute` to confirm that it executes `AgentAction`s in a manner consistent with atomic focus+type (e.g., combining Playwright's `click` and `type` into a single, visually confirmed operation) and that all interaction coordinates are subject to potential visual servo adjustments.
        3.  **Refactor (if necessary):** If `NativeBrowserExecutor.execute` currently executes focus and type as separate, potentially non-atomic steps without explicit visual servo feedback mechanisms, refactor it to strictly enforce these invariants.

## `src\executor\desktop.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **TASK**: **Refactor `_capture_burst_sync` to reduce fixed delay for visual velocity calculation.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_capture_burst_sync`
    *   **Description**: The current implementation introduces a fixed 200ms delay (`_time.sleep(0.1)` twice) for the burst capture to calculate visual velocity. While a subsequent `asyncio.sleep(0.3)` is conditional, this initial delay is always present. For real-time inference, this burst should be as fast as possible.
    *   **Action**: Modify `_capture_burst_sync` to capture only two frames with the *absolute minimum* delay possible between them (e.g., `_time.sleep(0.01)` or directly after the `mss.grab` if it's CPU-bound, or use a non-blocking `mss` alternative if available) to calculate velocity. The conditional `asyncio.sleep(0.3)` in `capture()` should be the primary mechanism for waiting out high velocity.

2.  **TASK**: **Implement adaptive post-action delays based on visual velocity.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `DesktopExecutor.__init__`, `_ok` (and all `_exec_*` methods calling `_ok`)
    *   **Description**: `self._post_action_delay` (0.15s) and `self._post_launch_delay` (0.8s) are fixed sleeps that directly contribute to P99 latency. These delays should be dynamic, waiting only as long as necessary for the UI to settle visually.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Remove `self._post_action_delay` and `self._post_launch_delay` attributes.
        *   Modify each `_exec_*` method that currently calls `await asyncio.sleep(self._post_action_delay)` or `await asyncio.sleep(self._post_launch_delay)` to instead call a new helper function `_wait_for_visual_stability()`.
        *   Create `async def _wait_for_visual_stability(self, min_delay: float = 0.05, max_delay: float = 1.0) -> None:` that repeatedly calls `self.capture()` (which already handles velocity-based waiting) or a lighter `_check_stability_sync()` method, until visual velocity is below a threshold or `max_delay` is reached.
        *   Consider the minimum effective sleep for `pyautogui` actions; some small delay might always be necessary for OS event loops.

3.  **TASK**: **Optimize `subprocess.run` calls for cleanup.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `cleanup_run`
    *   **Description**: The `taskkill` calls in `cleanup_run` are synchronous and could add to the cleanup time, impacting the readiness for the next run. While currently not in the critical path for real-time inference, optimizing this can improve overall system responsiveness.
    *   **Action**: Convert `subprocess.run` calls for `taskkill` into `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` to run them concurrently if multiple apps need to be killed. Ensure proper non-blocking `await` for their completion.

### Structural Idempotency

1.  **TASK**: **Introduce application status check for `_exec_launch_app`.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_exec_launch_app`
    *   **Description**: Launching an already running application is generally not idempotent and can lead to multiple instances, resource waste, or unexpected behavior.
    *   **Action**: Before calling `subprocess.Popen` or `os.startfile`, add a platform-specific check (e.g., using `psutil` or `tasklist` on Windows, `pgrep` on Linux/macOS) to determine if an application with `command` (or its `exe_name`) is already running. If it is, log a message and return success without re-launching, or implement a policy to close and re-open if desired.

2.  **TASK**: **Enhance `_exec_type` for content-based idempotency (partial).**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_exec_type`
    *   **Description**: While `clear_before_typing` helps, it doesn't guarantee the *final content* of the input field. True idempotency for "set text" would involve verifying the text after typing. This is complex for a desktop agent.
    *   **Action**: Since direct text reading from arbitrary desktop applications is hard, focus on making the *action* idempotent. If `action.clear_before_typing` is True, use `pyautogui.hotkey('ctrl', 'a')` followed by `pyautogui.press('delete')` instead of just `ctrl+a` to ensure the field is truly empty before pasting. This provides a stronger guarantee for the "clear" part of the action. (Already uses `ctrl+a` and then pastes over, so `delete` is not strictly needed for common text fields, but might be for others. Re-evaluating, the current clipboard paste over `ctrl+a` selection is already quite robust for "setting" text). Let's refine this to explicitly *verify* focus.

3.  **TASK**: **Generalize visual verification for action success beyond just `_exec_click`.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Functions**: `_exec_click`, `_exec_double_click`, `_exec_right_click`, `_exec_drag`, `_exec_scroll`, `_exec_type`, `_exec_hover`
    *   **Description**: For true idempotency (and self-healing), the agent should visually verify the *effect* of an action, not just its execution.
    *   **Action**: Introduce a post-action visual verification step. For example:
        *   In `_exec_click`, after clicking, capture the screen and compare it to a pre-click capture (or a region around the click target) to confirm a change occurred, or that the intended UI element is now in a "clicked" state (e.g., highlighting, disappearance).
        *   For `_exec_drag` and `_exec_scroll`, verify that the target area visually moved or scrolled as expected.
        *   For `_exec_type`, after typing, attempt to visually detect the presence of the entered text (this is very hard and might require OCR, consider for future). For now, verify the cursor is still in the input field.

### Agentic Features Not in Standard Workflow Engines

1.  **TASK**: **Implement an advanced "atomic focus and type" mechanism with visual feedback.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_exec_type`
    *   **Description**: The current `_exec_type` clicks and then samples a region, but doesn't guarantee the intended element *received* focus before typing. A robust agent would continually verify focus.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Modify `_exec_type` to iteratively click the target coordinates until visual feedback (e.g., a flashing cursor, a change in border color, or a significant visual change in the region around `x,y` distinct from a general screen update) indicates that the element has likely gained focus.
        *   Add a timeout to this focus-acquisition loop to prevent infinite retries.
        *   Only proceed with clipboard copy/paste once focus is visually confirmed.

2.  **TASK**: **Integrate proactive monitoring for critical application state.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Class**: `DesktopExecutor`
    *   **Description**: Beyond simple process cleanup, an agent should be aware if a critical application it's interacting with (e.g., a browser, an IDE) unexpectedly crashes or becomes unresponsive during a task.
    *   **Action**:
        *   Add a background task or hook to `DesktopExecutor` that periodically checks the process status (e.g., `proc.poll()`) of applications launched via `_exec_launch_app`, especially if they are in `_PROTECTED_PROCESSES`.
        *   If a critical application terminates unexpectedly during a run, raise a specific `AgenticRecoveryError` or log a high-priority event that the overall agent workflow can use to decide on recovery actions (e.g., re-launch, notify user, abort task).

3.  **TASK**: **Implement contextual failure recovery and retry strategies.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Functions**: `_exec_click`, `_fail`
    *   **Description**: When `_region_has_content` fails for a click, the agent currently just reports a failure. An agentic system should attempt to recover.
    *   **Action**:
        *   In `_exec_click` (and other relevant `_exec_*` methods), if `_region_has_content` (or a similar visual servo check) returns `False`, instead of immediately failing, implement a retry mechanism.
        *   This retry could involve:
            *   Re-perceiving the screen to find the element again (if coordinate was from a previous perception).
            *   Trying a slightly offset click (`x+delta`, `y+delta`).
            *   Waiting a short period and re-attempting the original action.
        *   Integrate this with the `ExecutionAttemptTrace` to record multiple attempts and their outcomes.

### Violations of Operon's Invariants

1.  **FLAG**: **Atomic Focus + Type: Insufficient visual confirmation of focus acquisition.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_exec_type`
    *   **Invariant**: Atomic focus+type.
    *   **Description**: The current `_exec_type` performs a click, then samples a region to detect *any* visual change. This does not atomically confirm that the *intended* element has received focus and is ready for typing. The `pre_pixels == post_pixels` check for retrying a click is a good start but doesn't explicitly verify focus indicators like a flashing cursor or active input field border.
    *   **Action**: (Refer to "Agentic Features" task 1 above) Enhance the focus verification loop in `_exec_type` to actively look for visual cues that confirm the input field is ready.

2.  **FLAG**: **Visual Servo: `_region_has_content` is not applied to all coordinate-based actions.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Functions**: `_exec_double_click`, `_exec_right_click`, `_exec_drag`, `_exec_scroll`, `_exec_hover`
    *   **Invariant**: Visual servo.
    *   **Description**: The `_region_has_content` visual servo check (to verify the target element is still present and not a uniform blank area) is only applied to `_exec_click`. Other actions that depend on target coordinates, like double-click, right-click, drag start/end, scroll point, and hover, would also benefit from this pre-action stability check.
    *   **Action**: Integrate `await asyncio.to_thread(self._region_has_content, x, y)` into `_exec_double_click`, `_exec_right_click`, `_exec_hover`. For `_exec_drag`, apply it at both the start `(x,y)` and end `(x_end, y_end)` coordinates. For `_exec_scroll`, apply it at `(x,y)`. If the check fails, return a `FailureCategory.EXECUTION_TARGET_NOT_FOUND`.

3.  **FLAG**: **Visual Servo: Fixed `_time.sleep` in `_capture_burst_sync` adds unnecessary latency for velocity measurement.**
    *   **File**: `src\executor\desktop.py`
    *   **Function**: `_capture_burst_sync`
    *   **Invariant**: Visual servo (implies rapid, low-latency visual feedback).
    *   **Description**: The 200ms fixed delay for a burst capture to calculate visual velocity directly impacts the latency of the visual servo loop.
    *   **Action**: (Refer to "P99 Latency Reduction" task 1 above) Reduce the fixed delay in `_capture_burst_sync` to the absolute minimum necessary for sequential screen grabs, or explore non-blocking capture methods if `mss` supports them for even faster feedback.

## `src\executor\os_picker_macro.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**

    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `_poll_for_picker`, `_poll_for_picker_closed`
        **ACTION**: Implement an adaptive polling strategy instead of a fixed `interval_s`. Consider starting with a smaller `interval_s` (e.g., 0.05s), and if no window is found, gradually increase it using an exponential backoff approach, capping at the current `interval_s` (0.1s) or slightly higher. This would reduce the average wait time for quick-appearing dialogs without excessive CPU load for slow ones.
        **DETAIL**: This minimizes worst-case latency by reacting faster when possible, while gracefully handling slower system responses.
    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **ACTION**: Re-evaluate the necessity of `time.sleep(0.2)` after `pyautogui.write(file_path, interval=0.02)`. This fixed delay adds directly to P99 latency. If this sleep is to allow UI reflection, explore replacing it with a visual servo-driven confirmation (see point 4) or a more dynamic, minimal wait.
        **DETAIL**: Fixed delays are prime targets for latency reduction.
    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **ACTION**: Reduce the `interval` parameter in `pyautogui.write(file_path, interval=0.02)`. Test if `interval=0.01` or `interval=0` is sufficiently stable across target applications, as this directly affects the typing speed.
        **DETAIL**: Typing speed is a direct contributor to macro duration.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **ACTION**: Enhance the input mechanism to ensure the file path field is in a known, idempotent state before typing. Before `pyautogui.write(file_path, ...)`, add a step to clear the input field. This could involve `pyautogui.hotkey('ctrl', 'a')` followed by `pyautogui.press('backspace')` (or platform equivalents) *if* a visual servo confirms an input field is present and focused.
        **DETAIL**: This ensures that re-running the macro due to an upstream failure (e.g., "Enter" not registered) doesn't result in `filepathfilepath` being typed. This relies on future visual servo capabilities.
    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **ACTION**: Consider adding a mechanism to detect if the "Enter" key press was successful *before* polling for the window to close. For example, if a visual servo mechanism could confirm the "OK/Open" button visually highlights or visually disappears briefly upon press. This is an advanced idempotency for confirmation.
        **DETAIL**: This would make the confirmation step more robust and idempotent by validating the action's immediate visual feedback.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py` (Higher-level integration, not direct code change)
        **ACTION**: Introduce adaptive context-aware retries and error handling for `PickerOutcome.PICKER_NOT_DETECTED`. If the picker doesn't appear, a higher-level agent should be able to:
            1.  Re-evaluate the UI state (using visual servo) to ensure the original upload button is still present.
            2.  Attempt to re-click the upload button, perhaps with a slight coordinate offset or different click method.
            3.  If the picker title keywords are insufficient, perform visual OCR on prominent dialog text to identify if a different type of file dialog has appeared.
        **DETAIL**: Moves beyond fixed timeouts to intelligent, adaptive recovery based on observed UI state.
    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py` (Higher-level integration, not direct code change)
        **ACTION**: Implement self-healing for `PickerOutcome.FILE_NOT_REFLECTED`. If the picker doesn't close after "Enter":
            1.  Visually detect any error messages on the file picker dialog (e.g., "File not found", "Invalid characters").
            2.  Based on the error, an LLM-guided reasoning agent could suggest an alternative `file_path` (e.g., correct a typo, suggest a different directory) and re-attempt the `run_os_picker_macro`.
            3.  If no error is visible, the agent could attempt to visually locate and click an "OK" or "Open" button if `pyautogui.press('enter')` failed to trigger it.
        **DETAIL**: Enables the system to diagnose and attempt to fix issues rather than simply reporting failure.
    *   **TASK**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py` (Higher-level integration, not direct code change)
        **ACTION**: Incorporate a feedback loop mechanism. Log the `appear_timeout_s` and `close_timeout_s` values and the actual observed times for picker appearance/closure. Over time, an agent could learn application-specific or environment-specific optimal timeouts and dynamically adjust them for future invocations, reducing fixed delays where possible.
        **DETAIL**: Allows the system to learn and optimize its own parameters over time.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants: No DOM/Selectors, Atomic Focus+Type, Visual Servo**

    *   **FLAG**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `_find_picker_window`, `_poll_for_picker`, `_poll_for_picker_closed`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **VIOLATION**: **Missing Visual Servoing**
        **DETAIL**: This module relies entirely on `pygetwindow` for window detection and `pyautogui` for blind input to the focused window. There is no visual feedback loop to confirm:
            1.  The *visual appearance* of a file picker window (only title matching).
            2.  The *visual location* of the filename input field within the picker.
            3.  The *visual confirmation* that the `file_path` has been successfully typed into the field.
            4.  The *visual confirmation* that pressing "Enter" triggered the expected UI change (e.g., button press, window closure).
        **ACTION**: Integrate visual servoing capabilities. This macro should be augmented by a visual model that, after detecting a window by title, visually confirms it's a file picker, visually locates the input field, visually confirms typing, and visually confirms closure. For instance, the `_poll_for_picker_closed` function should visually assert the picker is no longer present on screen, not just relying on `pygetwindow`.
    *   **FLAG**: `src/executor/os_picker_macro.py`, `run_os_picker_macro`
        **VIOLATION**: **Non-Atomic Focus+Type (Minor)**
        **DETAIL**: While `pyautogui.write` simulates typing character by character, which is typical for OS interaction, Operon's "atomic focus+type" implies a single logical operation for the agent. The `time.sleep(0.2)` between typing and pressing enter also breaks immediate atomicity.
        **ACTION**: While `pyautogui` itself isn't atomic for typing, the goal is for the *agent's perception* of the action to be atomic. The `time.sleep(0.2)` should be replaced with a visual servo-driven wait (e.g., "wait until text appears and settles") to maintain the logical atomicity of "type and confirm." The `activate()` call for focus could also be augmented with visual confirmation of focus.

## `src\models\benchmark.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**
    *   **TASK**: Introduce `latency_ms: float | None = None` and `latency_p99_ms: float | None = None` fields to `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics`.
        *   **Reasoning**: While this module defines schemas for *benchmark results* rather than real-time inference, these metrics are crucial for understanding and optimizing the agent's performance. Adding direct latency measurements (e.g., end-to-end action latency, or perception-to-action latency) will provide granular data to identify and address P99 latency bottlenecks in the agent's execution.
    *   **TASK**: Introduce `average_latency_ms: float | None = None` and `p99_latency_ms: float | None = None` fields to `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary`.
        *   **Reasoning**: Aggregating latency metrics at the suite level allows for high-level monitoring and trend analysis, enabling architects to quickly spot regressions or improvements in overall agent responsiveness.
    *   **TASK**: Consider adding granular timestamp fields within `RunMetrics` (e.g., `perception_start_ms`, `perception_end_ms`, `action_start_ms`, `action_end_ms`) if a more detailed breakdown of component latencies is required for deeper analysis.
        *   **Reasoning**: Capturing timestamps for critical operational phases would allow for precise post-hoc analysis of bottlenecks contributing to P99 latency, such as vision model inference time versus action execution time.

2.  **Structural Idempotency**
    *   **TASK**: Ensure that when `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics` instances are persisted, the combination of `run_id` and `task_id` is treated as a unique composite identifier.
        *   **Reasoning**: This allows for idempotent "upsert" operations where re-submission of the same run's metrics for a given task will either create a new record if it doesn't exist or update an existing one without creating duplicates, ensuring data consistency.
    *   **TASK**: Ensure that `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary` instances, when generated or updated, are derived idempotently from a consistent set of `RunMetrics`. The `suite_id` should serve as the primary key for idempotent summary storage.
        *   **Reasoning**: Aggregate summaries should always produce the same result given the same underlying source data (`RunMetrics`). This allows for safe re-computation or regeneration of summaries without side effects, crucial for data integrity and recovery.
    *   **TASK**: Emphasize the use of `task_id` and `suite_id` in `BenchmarkTaskSpec` and `BenchmarkSuiteSpec` respectively as idempotent identifiers for task and suite definitions in any persistent storage layer.
        *   **Reasoning**: These IDs are explicitly designed as unique identifiers and should be leveraged to ensure that task and suite definitions can be stored or retrieved idempotently.

3.  **Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **TASK**: Enhance the agent's real-time decision-making with `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics` data. Implement a **Dynamic Action Re-evaluation Module** that uses `no_progress_events` and `loop_detected` metrics *in real-time* to trigger a full re-evaluation of the agent's goal and current visual state, rather than just simple retries.
        *   **Reasoning**: Instead of following a pre-defined recovery path, an Operon agent should dynamically generate a new plan from scratch when encountering states of no progress or loops, leveraging its vision-only capabilities to perceive the current environment anew and devise a novel sequence of actions. This goes beyond standard workflow engine 'retry' logic.
    *   **TASK**: Implement a **Self-Adaptive Perception Strategy** based on `perception_retry_count` and `stale_target_events` from `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics`. If these counts exceed thresholds, the agent should dynamically adjust its visual attention, object detection parameters, or visual grounding confidence thresholds.
        *   **Reasoning**: An agentic system for Operon would learn from its perception failures. If targets are frequently stale or require many perception retries, the agent should adapt its visual processing pipeline (e.g., increase frame rate analysis, refine object tracking, or re-scan the entire screen) rather than just repeating the same perception step.
    *   **TASK**: Develop an **Intent-Driven Remediation System** using `src\models\benchmark.py::FailureCategory` and `final_stop_reason`. When specific failure patterns emerge (e.g., `FocusFailure` on a `FORM_FILL` task), the agent should autonomously explore alternative, visually-guided interaction techniques (e.g., different visual cues for "focus," alternative input methods detected visually) that are tailored to the detected failure category and original intent, without relying on pre-scripted recovery paths.
        *   **Reasoning**: Standard engines trigger predefined error handlers. An Operon agent should analyze the *type* of failure and the *original intent* (from `BenchmarkTaskSpec.intent`) to dynamically invent new approaches to achieve the goal using its vision-only interface, effectively "learning" to workaround novel issues.
    *   **TASK**: Introduce a **Proactive Strategy Adaptation Module** that leverages historical `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary` data (especially `overall_success_rate`, `failure_breakdown_by_stop_reason`, and `tag_summary`) to adjust its execution strategy for new tasks based on their `difficulty_tags` and `task_type` *before* execution begins.
        *   **Reasoning**: An agent should learn from past failures across many runs. If a certain `task_type` or `difficulty_tag` consistently leads to `click_no_effect_events`, the agent should automatically adopt a more robust clicking strategy (e.g., longer wait after click, visual confirmation of element state change) when encountering similar tasks in the future.

4.  **Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **FLAG**: Remove `selector_recovery_count: int` from `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **VIOLATION of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.** Operon is a vision-only, zero-abstraction agent. It must not rely on, or even acknowledge the existence of, DOM elements or selectors. This field explicitly indicates a mechanism tied to DOM selectors.
    *   **FLAG**: Remove `average_top_selector_score: float | None` from `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics` and `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **VIOLATION of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.** Scoring selectors directly contradicts Operon's core principle of operating purely on visual input without abstraction to the underlying webpage structure.
    *   **FLAG**: Remove `average_selector_margin: float | None` from `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics` and `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **VIOLATION of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.** Similar to selector scores, selector margins imply a reliance on DOM-based targeting.
    *   **FLAG**: Remove `selector_failure_count: int` from `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **VIOLATION of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.** This field directly tracks failures related to selectors, which are an abstraction Operon must not use.
    *   **FLAG**: Clarify the definition and usage of `focus_failures: int` in `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **POTENTIAL VIOLATION or AMBIGUITY regarding "atomic focus+type" and "zero-abstraction" invariants.** If "focus" refers to the browser's internal DOM focus state, it's a violation. If it strictly means the agent failed to visually confirm an input target was ready for typing *after* a visual targeting action, and before `type` was initiated as part of the `atomic focus+type` operation, then it could be compliant. This requires strict adherence to a visual-only interpretation. If `focus_failures` implies a separate, non-visual action distinct from the atomic "focus+type" concept, it's a violation. The agent should ensure visual readiness for input as part of the atomic action.
    *   **FLAG**: Review `average_total_elements`, `average_labeled_elements`, `average_unlabeled_elements`, `average_usable_elements` in `src\models\benchmark.py::RunMetrics` and `src\models\benchmark.py::BenchmarkSuiteSummary`.
        *   **Reasoning**: **POTENTIAL VIOLATION or AMBIGUITY regarding "zero-abstraction" invariant.** While these *could* be interpreted as visually distinct regions, the term "elements" strongly implies DOM elements. If these refer to DOM elements rather than perceptually distinct visual regions identified by the vision system, they are violations. Renaming or clarifying these fields (e.g., `average_total_visual_regions`, `average_labeled_visual_regions`) would ensure compliance.

## `src\models\capture.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize Frame Transfer to In-Memory**
    *   **Description:** Currently, `artifact_path` implies disk-based storage and retrieval, which introduces I/O latency. For real-time inference, frames should ideally be transferred in-memory.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Modify `CaptureFrame`:** Add an optional field `frame_buffer_id: str | None = Field(default=None)` to hold an identifier for a shared memory region (e.g., a shmem name, UUID, or handle) where the raw image data resides.
        2.  **Recommendation:** The `artifact_path` field should become optional or be used for fallback/persistence only. The inference engine should prioritize `frame_buffer_id` for lowest latency.
    *   **File:** `src\models\capture.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `CaptureFrame`

*   **Task 1.2: Implement Zero-Copy Metadata Serialization**
    *   **Description:** While `CaptureFrame` is small, serialization/deserialization overhead can accumulate across many frames. Using efficient, zero-copy serialization for this metadata when transmitting to the inference engine can further reduce latency.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Recommendation:** For inter-process communication (IPC) of `CaptureFrame` instances, explore direct memory mapping or specialized binary serialization libraries (e.g., FlatBuffers, Cap'n Proto, or Protobuf) that allow for zero-copy deserialization where data structures can be directly accessed from the buffer without full deserialization. This is an external system recommendation, but implies the `CaptureFrame` Pydantic model might need a `model_dump_as_binary` method or similar for these formats.
        2.  **Consideration:** If `artifact_path` is still used for larger frames, ensure the file I/O is asynchronous and non-blocking in the capture pipeline.
    *   **File:** `src\models\capture.py` (Indirectly impacts how `CaptureFrame` is used)
    *   **Function/Class:** N/A (Applies to usage pattern)

**2. Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

*   **Task 2.1: Introduce Content-Addressable `artifact_path`**
    *   **Description:** To ensure idempotency in frame storage and retrieval, the `artifact_path` should ideally be derived from the content of the image itself (e.g., a cryptographic hash of the image data). This guarantees that storing the same image multiple times will result in the same path, and retrieving from that path will always yield the identical content, regardless of how many times the "store" operation was logically invoked.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Modify `CaptureFrame`:** Add a comment to the `artifact_path` field, explicitly stating that it *should* represent a content-addressable identifier (e.g., `artifact_path: str = Field(min_length=1, description="Content-addressable path (e.g., SHA256 hash) to the stored image artifact.")`).
        2.  **Implementation Guideline:** The capture mechanism producing this `CaptureFrame` should compute this hash.
    *   **File:** `src\models\capture.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `CaptureFrame`

*   **Task 2.2: Add a Unique and Deterministic Frame Identifier**
    *   **Description:** While `artifact_path` handles image content idempotency, a frame might have identical content but be captured at different logical times or with slightly different metadata. A unique ID helps idempotently identify and process a *specific instance* of a captured frame.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Modify `CaptureFrame`:** Add a new field `frame_id: str = Field(min_length=1, description="Unique identifier for this specific capture frame instance (e.g., UUID or timestamp+hash of metadata).")`.
        2.  **Implementation Guideline:** This ID should be generated deterministically if possible (e.g., based on timestamp + hash of `width`, `height`, `monitor_left`, `monitor_top`) or as a UUID if absolute uniqueness is paramount and re-capture of *identical* metadata is unlikely/undesirable.
    *   **File:** `src\models\capture.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `CaptureFrame`

**3. Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Adaptive Capture Rate Based on `visual_velocity`**
    *   **Description:** An Operon agent should dynamically adjust the frame capture frequency. When `visual_velocity` is high, indicating active screen changes, the agent should increase the capture rate to ensure responsiveness. When `visual_velocity` is low (static screen), the rate can decrease to save resources and reduce processing load.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Architectural Recommendation:** Design an "Adaptive Capture Agent" service that consumes `CaptureFrame` objects (specifically `visual_velocity`), analyzes trends, and sends control signals back to the frame capture mechanism to modify its capture interval.
        2.  **Consideration:** This agent could also dynamically adjust the "burst frames" interval mentioned in the `visual_velocity` description.
    *   **File:** N/A (External Agent, but uses `CaptureFrame`)
    *   **Function/Class:** N/A

*   **Task 3.2: Introduce Proactive Frame Quality/Resolution Adjustment**
    *   **Description:** Based on real-time feedback (e.g., inference engine load, network latency to model server, or resource constraints), an Operon agent should be able to dynamically adjust the `width`, `height`, or `mime_type` (e.g., switch to JPEG for lower quality/size) of future frames to optimize for performance or resource usage, without explicit human intervention.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Architectural Recommendation:** Design a "Resource Optimization Agent" that monitors system health and inference pipeline metrics. It should then signal the frame capture mechanism to adjust `width`, `height`, or `mime_type` parameters for subsequent captures.
    *   **File:** N/A (External Agent, but modifies how `CaptureFrame` fields are populated)
    *   **Function/Class:** N/A

*   **Task 3.3: Develop Capture Source Health Monitoring and Self-Healing**
    *   **Description:** An Operon agent should continuously monitor the capture process for anomalies and attempt self-healing. This goes beyond simple error handling in a workflow.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Architectural Recommendation:** Design a "Capture Health Agent" that monitors streams of `CaptureFrame` data for:
            *   `visual_velocity` stuck at 0.0 for an extended period despite expected user interaction (indicates a frozen screen or capture bug).
            *   Repeated failures to populate `artifact_path` or `frame_buffer_id`.
            *   Unexpected changes or zeros in `width` or `height`.
        2.  **Self-Healing Actions:** If anomalies are detected, the agent could:
            *   Log critical alerts.
            *   Attempt to restart the capture service/process.
            *   Switch to an alternative capture method if available.
            *   Automatically reduce capture frequency to reduce load if a resource bottleneck is suspected.
    *   **File:** N/A (External Agent, but uses `CaptureFrame` for monitoring)
    *   **Function/Class:** N/A

**4. Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**

*   **Task 4.1: Verify Operon Invariants Adherence**
    *   **Description:** Review `CaptureFrame` against Operon's core invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, and visual servo.
    *   **Action:**
        1.  **Conclusion:** The `CaptureFrame` schema is fully compliant with Operon's invariants.
            *   It deals with raw visual data (`artifact_path`, `width`, `height`, `mime_type`) and does not interact with or expose DOM elements or selectors.
            *   It is an input schema, not an interaction mechanism, thus not violating "atomic focus+type".
            *   The `visual_velocity` field directly supports and enables the "visual servo" principle by providing a real-time metric of screen dynamism, crucial for adaptive agents.
        2.  **No changes needed** for invariant compliance within this module.
    *   **File:** `src\models\capture.py`
    *   **Function/Class:** `CaptureFrame`

## `src\models\common.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns for Reducing P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference

*   **Task 1.1: Optimize Data Serialization/Deserialization for DTOs.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (applies to all `StrictModel` instances)
    *   **Action:** Evaluate the current serialization method (Pydantic's default, typically JSON) for all `StrictModel` DTOs used in high-frequency or latency-sensitive communication (e.g., inter-process communication, API endpoints for `StepRequest`). For critical paths, consider switching to faster, more compact binary serialization protocols like MessagePack, Protocol Buffers, or FlatBuffers. This will reduce payload size and CPU cycles spent on (de)serialization.
    *   **Reasoning:** Minimizing data transfer and parsing overhead directly contributes to reducing P99 latency, especially in real-time inference loops where DTOs like `RunTaskRequest`, `StepRequest`, and `RunResponse` are exchanged frequently.

*   **Task 1.2: Implement Early Exit Conditions within Inference Loop.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (related to `LoopStage`, `RunStatus`, `StopReason`)
    *   **Action:** In the core control loop that utilizes `LoopStage` and determines `RunStatus`, ensure that mechanisms exist to detect terminal `StopReason`s (e.g., `MAX_STEP_LIMIT_REACHED`, `RETRY_LIMIT_REACHED`) or critical `FailureCategory`s as early as possible *within* each stage of the inference pipeline. This should pre-empt unnecessary computation in downstream stages (e.g., skipping `PERCEIVE` or `CHOOSE_ACTION` if a run is already known to be `FAILED`).
    *   **Reasoning:** Preventing redundant work for runs that are already in a terminal state or have exhausted retries reduces wasted computation time, thereby improving overall system responsiveness and P99 latency.

*   **Task 1.3: Explore Batching for Inference Service Requests.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (relevant to usage of `RunTaskRequest`, `StepRequest`)
    *   **Action:** While this module defines individual DTOs, analyze the usage patterns of requests that trigger ML inference (e.g., from `PERCEIVE` or `CHOOSE_ACTION` stages). If multiple `StepRequest`s or independent inference queries can accumulate within a short window, design the system to batch these requests when interacting with backend ML services.
    *   **Reasoning:** Batching inference requests can significantly improve throughput and reduce P99 latency by more efficiently utilizing hardware (e.g., GPUs) and amortizing fixed overheads in ML serving infrastructure.

### 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

*   **Task 2.1: Enhance `RunTaskRequest` for Idempotent Task Initiation.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`, `RunTaskRequest`
    *   **Action:** Introduce an optional `client_request_id: str` field to `RunTaskRequest`. If provided, the system should check for an existing active run associated with this `client_request_id` (and potentially `intent`/`start_url`). If a matching run is found, return its `run_id` and current status, effectively making repeated `RunTaskRequest` with the same ID idempotent. Consider an additional flag like `force_new_run: bool` for explicit override.
    *   **Reasoning:** Ensures that repeated external requests to start the same task (e.g., due to client-side retries) do not lead to the creation of multiple redundant agent runs, improving resource efficiency and predictability.

*   **Task 2.2: Define Strong Idempotency for `StepRequest` Processing.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`, `StepRequest`
    *   **Action:** For the backend processing of a `StepRequest`, ensure its idempotency semantic is clearly defined and enforced. If `StepRequest` is merely an instruction to advance the run by one logical stage, multiple identical `StepRequest`s in a row should only cause a single progression. If `StepRequest` implies re-attempting the *current* operation until success, this needs explicit tracking. Consider adding an optional `expected_state_hash: str` or `current_loop_stage: LoopStage` to `StepRequest` to allow the server to verify the run's state before processing, preventing actions based on stale client information.
    *   **Reasoning:** Critical for reliable recovery and retry mechanisms, ensuring that transient network errors or client retries of `StepRequest` do not cause unintended skips, duplicated actions, or state corruption.

*   **Task 2.3: Ensure Idempotency of Terminal Run Operations.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`, `StopRunRequest`, `CleanupRequest`
    *   **Action:** Explicitly design and verify that operations triggered by `StopRunRequest` and `CleanupRequest` are fully idempotent. Calling `stop_run` on an already stopped or failed run should result in the same outcome (e.g., success with no state change) without raising an error. Similarly, `cleanup` on an already cleaned-up run should indicate no further actions were taken (e.g., `closed_count=0`).
    *   **Reasoning:** These operations are frequently invoked in "finally" blocks or error handling logic, where repeated calls are common. Idempotency simplifies system design and prevents errors in such scenarios.

### 3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Proactive Plan Adaptation and Dynamic Re-planning.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (informed by `LoopStage`, `FailureCategory`, `StopReason`)
    *   **Action:** Augment the `RECOVER` stage beyond simple retries. When the agent encounters persistent issues (`REPEATED_FAILURE_LOOP`, `NO_MEANINGFUL_PROGRESS_ACROSS_STEPS`, `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`), it should trigger a meta-level planning component. This component should leverage the agent's full context and visual history to dynamically adjust the current plan, generate alternative sub-goals, or even perform a complete re-planning of the remaining task based on the original `intent`.
    *   **Reasoning:** Standard workflows are typically rigid. An intelligent agent needs to autonomously adapt its strategy, not just recover from atomic step failures, demonstrating higher-order reasoning capabilities essential for real-world robustness.

*   **Task 3.2: Introduce Contextual Learning from `FailureCategory` Events.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (utilizing `FailureCategory`)
    *   **Action:** Develop a persistent learning system that records `FailureCategory` events (e.g., `PERCEPTION_LOW_QUALITY`, `TARGET_LOST_BEFORE_ACTION`, `CLICK_NO_EFFECT`) along with the complete visual and internal state context. This historical data should be actively used to:
        *   Refine perception models for specific visual patterns or UI elements.
        *   Modify `CHOOSE_ACTION` policies to avoid previously problematic interaction sequences.
        *   Inform the proactive re-planning strategies in Task 3.1, leading to continuous self-improvement.
    *   **Reasoning:** Operon, as an agent, should learn from its experiences. This goes beyond simple error handling in traditional workflows by feeding failure data back into its decision-making and perception systems for long-term improvement.

*   **Task 3.3: Enable Interactive Learning and Demonstration via `WAITING_FOR_USER`.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py` (`RunStatus.WAITING_FOR_USER`, `StopReason.WAITING_FOR_USER`, `HUMAN_INTERVENTION_REQUIRED`)
    *   **Action:** When a run reaches a `WAITING_FOR_USER` or `HUMAN_INTERVENTION_REQUIRED` state, design the system to not just pause, but to actively solicit and integrate human input as a learning opportunity. This includes:
        *   Recording user demonstrations to acquire new action primitives or sequences.
        *   Allowing users to visually label or annotate problematic elements to improve perception models.
        *   Receiving explicit instructions that modify the agent's current plan or knowledge base.
    *   **Reasoning:** An advanced agent should leverage human intervention not just for task completion but for continuous learning, aiming to reduce the frequency of future human interventions for similar tasks.

### 4. Violations of Operon's Invariants

*   **Task 4.1: Eliminate Reliance on "Selectors" - Direct Invariant Violation.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`
    *   **Functionality:** The `FailureCategory` enum includes `SELECTOR_SCORE_BELOW_THRESHOLD`, `SELECTOR_NO_CANDIDATES_AFTER_FILTERING`, `SELECTOR_RECOVERY_USED`, `SELECTOR_RECOVERY_FAILED`. These are also present in `StopReason`.
    *   **Violation:** These failure categories explicitly refer to "selectors," which directly contradicts Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant. Operon is strictly "vision-only" and "zero-abstraction," meaning it should operate purely on pixel data and visual understanding, not on underlying structural abstractions like DOM, accessibility trees, or any form of explicit selectors.
    *   **Action:** Immediately audit all code paths that generate or consume these `SELECTOR_*` failure categories. Redesign the target identification and grounding mechanisms to be purely vision-based (e.g., visual feature matching, OCR, object detection). Replace these `SELECTOR_*` `FailureCategory` and `StopReason` values with new, vision-centric categories that reflect failures in visual perception and grounding (e.g., `VISUAL_TARGET_AMBIGUOUS`, `VISUAL_GROUNDING_FAILED`, `NO_PERCEIVED_CANDIDATES`).

*   **Task 4.2: Re-evaluate "Atomic Focus+Type" with Current Failure Categories.**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`
    *   **Functionality:** `FailureCategory` includes `FOCUS_VERIFICATION_FAILED`, `CLICK_BEFORE_TYPE_FAILED`, `TYPE_VERIFICATION_FAILED`.
    *   **Potential Violation:** The invariant "atomic focus+type" implies that the agent's fundamental action for entering text into an input field is a single, indivisible operation. The presence of separate `FOCUS_VERIFICATION_FAILED`, `TYPE_VERIFICATION_FAILED`, and particularly `CLICK_BEFORE_TYPE_FAILED` suggests that the agent's underlying interaction model or its verification process breaks down this atomic action into discrete, sequential steps (e.g., `click` then `focus` then `type`). If these represent distinct agent-initiated actions rather than internal verification points within a single atomic primitive, this is a violation.
    *   **Action:** Clarify the precise definition and implementation of "atomic focus+type." If the agent performs `click`, then `focus`, then `type` as separate, observable actions, refactor the agent's core action primitives to encapsulate the entire focus-and-type operation into a single, atomic primitive from the agent's perspective. The failure categories should then reflect the *outcome* of this single primitive (e.g., `INPUT_ACTION_FAILED_TO_VERIFY_FOCUS`, `INPUT_ACTION_FAILED_TO_VERIFY_TYPE`) rather than implying distinct attempts.

*   **Task 4.3: Validate "Visual Servo" Consistency (No Identified Violations).**
    *   **File:** `src/models/common.py`
    *   **Functionality:** `LoopStage` (especially `CAPTURE`, `PERCEIVE`, `CHOOSE_ACTION`, `EXECUTE`, `VERIFY`), and `FailureCategory` values like `TARGET_SHIFTED_BEFORE_ACTION`, `TARGET_LOST_BEFORE_ACTION`, `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`.
    *   **Observation:** The enumerated stages and failure conditions are consistent with the "visual servo" invariant. They imply a continuous feedback loop where visual perception informs subsequent actions and the agent actively tracks and responds to dynamic changes in the visual environment.
    *   **Action:** No immediate action required on this specific module. Ensure that the actual implementation of the agent's control loop and action execution strictly adheres to this principle, continuously using visual feedback to guide and adjust operations.

## `src\models\episode.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**
    *   **Task:** Evaluate the use of a more compact and faster binary serialization format (e.g., MessagePack, FlatBuffers) instead of JSON for storing and retrieving `src\models\episode.py::Episode` and `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep` objects in the persistence layer. This will reduce data size and I/O overhead during real-time inference lookups.
        *   **Reasoning:** Large Pydantic models with nested structures and numerous string fields can incur significant serialization/deserialization latency, especially at P99, when retrieving entire episodes for replay.
    *   **Task:** Analyze the composition of `src\models\perception.py::PageHint` (a dependency of `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep`). If `PageHint` frequently contains large data blobs (e.g., raw image data, complex visual feature vectors), consider optimizing its storage strategy: either compress it aggressively within the `EpisodeStep` or store it separately and fetch it asynchronously/on-demand during replay to avoid blocking the primary `EpisodeStep` retrieval.
        *   **Reasoning:** `PageHint` is the most likely variable-sized component that could introduce latency spikes if not efficiently handled.
    *   **Task:** Recommend enforcing proper indexing on `episode_id` for `src\models\episode.py::Episode` and a composite index on (`episode_id`, `step_index`) for `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep` in the backing data store.
        *   **Reasoning:** Fast primary key lookups are critical for real-time inference.

2.  **Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task:** Ensure the persistence layer defines `episode_id` as the primary key for `src\models\episode.py::Episode` to allow for idempotent upserts.
        *   **Reasoning:** Saving an `Episode` multiple times with the same `episode_id` should result in the same stored state, not duplicate records.
    *   **Task:** If `EpisodeStep` objects are stored separately from their parent `Episode`, define a composite primary key using (`episode_id`, `step_index`) for `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep` to guarantee idempotent updates or insertions.
        *   **Reasoning:** This ensures that each `EpisodeStep` is uniquely identifiable and updatable without creating duplicate entries.
    *   **Task:** Clarify the semantics of `src\models\episode.py::Episode::success_count` and `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeReplayState::deviations`. If these fields are intended as atomic counters, the *increment operation itself* is not idempotent. Consider designing the system such that the *final value* is set idempotently (e.g., recalculating the total success count or deviations based on immutable event logs) rather than relying on repeated non-idempotent increment operations.
        *   **Reasoning:** In distributed or retry-heavy systems, non-idempotent operations like incrementing a counter can lead to inconsistent state. Re-evaluating or setting the absolute value ensures idempotency.
    *   **Task:** Update `src\models\episode.py::Episode::created_at` to use `datetime` instead of `str` for improved type safety and consistency, ensuring it's set once on creation (e.g., by the database or application logic) and remains immutable for that episode.
        *   **Reasoning:** `datetime` objects provide better handling for timestamps and allow for consistent storage (e.g., UTC) to support idempotent creation logic.

3.  **Agentic Features**
    *   **Task:** Enhance `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeReplayState` or introduce a new model (e.g., `DeviationLogEntry`) to capture more detailed context when `deviations` occurs. This should include: the actual perceived `PageHint` at the deviation point, the intended `action_type`, the actual outcome/error, and potentially alternative actions attempted by the agent.
        *   **Reasoning:** Rich deviation context is crucial for intelligent self-healing, root cause analysis, and allowing the agent to learn from failures and dynamically adjust its strategy.
    *   **Task:** Consider extending `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep` with optional fields to support conditional branching or dynamic step selection during replay. Examples include: `alternative_next_step_indices: dict[str, int]` (mapping a perceived condition to a jump index) or `fallback_episode_id: str | None`.
        *   **Reasoning:** Standard workflow engines are linear. An agentic system needs to adapt to dynamic environments, choosing different paths based on visual feedback to achieve a goal, rather than just failing.
    *   **Task:** Introduce a mechanism for `Episode` objects to be dynamically evaluated and refined. This could involve adding a field like `reliability_score: float` to `src\models\episode.py::Episode`, which is updated based on replay success rates and deviation counts tracked in `EpisodeReplayState` and deviation logs.
        *   **Reasoning:** Allows the agent to prioritize reliable episodes, deprecate unreliable ones, and actively seek to improve or replace steps that frequently lead to deviations.

4.  **Operon Invariants Violations**
    *   **Task:** Review the definition of `src\models\perception.py::PageHint` to explicitly confirm it *only* contains visual information (e.g., bounding boxes, OCR text, visual features, semantic labels derived from vision) and *does not* include any HTML DOM elements, IDs, CSS selectors, or XPath expressions.
        *   **Reasoning:** The invariant "no DOM/selectors" is fundamental to Operon. `PageHint` is a critical dependency, and its internal structure must strictly adhere to this.
    *   **Task:** Clarify the expected content of `src\models\episode.py::EpisodeStep::target_description`. Document that this field must solely represent a visually discernible characteristic of the target (e.g., "blue button with text 'Submit'", "input field next to label 'Username'") and *must not* contain any DOM-specific identifiers like HTML IDs, classes, or selectors.
        *   **Reasoning:** While `target_description` itself doesn't violate the invariant, its interpretation and content could easily lead to violations if not strictly defined.
    *   **Task:** Review the definition of `src\models\policy.py::ActionType` to explicitly confirm it *only* includes actions based on visual coordinates or atomic interaction primitives (e.g., `CLICK_VISUAL_REGION`, `TYPE_TEXT`, `SCROLL_VIEWPORT`) and *does not* include any DOM-specific interaction types like `CLICK_DOM_ELEMENT`, `SELECT_BY_CSS`, or `EXECUTE_JAVASCRIPT`.
        *   **Reasoning:** `ActionType` directly dictates how the agent interacts, and must align with the "atomic focus+type" and "visual servo" invariants.

**3. Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

    *   **Action:** Leverage the `failure_category`, `no_progress_detected`, and detailed `verification_result` strings (e.g., "element obscured", "wrong content", "low confidence match") across multiple action traces to train an inference model. This model should predict the likelihood of an upcoming action failing *before* execution, allowing for pre-emptive alternative action generation or re-planning.
    *   **Reasoning:** Standard workflows react to failure; an agent predicts and adapts. This goes beyond simple retries by enabling proactive strategy changes.
*   **Task 3.2: Implement Adaptive Reresolution Learning.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
    *   **Class:** `ExecutionReresolutionTrace`
    *   **Action:** The agent should analyze historical `ExecutionReresolutionTrace` data (e.g., `trigger_reason`, `succeeded`, `detail`, and the context of `original_intent`) to learn which re-resolution strategies are most effective under specific conditions. It can then dynamically adjust its re-resolution approach (e.g., trying a different visual search heuristic, increasing search radius, or abandoning re-resolution if historically futile).
    *   **Reasoning:** Rather than a static re-resolution pipeline, the agent learns and optimizes its own healing mechanisms.
*   **Task 3.3: Introduce Goal-Oriented Progress Monitoring with Visual Feedback.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
    *   **Classes:** `ExecutedAction`, `ExecutionTargetSnapshot`, `no_progress_detected`
    *   **Action:** Extend the agent's monitoring capabilities beyond `success: bool`. By combining `ExecutionTargetSnapshot` (visual state, text content, coordinates) and `page_signature`, the agent should continuously evaluate its current state against the overall task goal. If `no_progress_detected` remains true despite individual actions succeeding, or if visual cues indicate stagnation, the agent should trigger a higher-level replanning or anomaly detection, not just a simple retry.
    *   **Reasoning:** Standard workflows only check task completion. An agent understands if it's *moving towards* the goal, even if intermediate steps succeed.
*   **Task 3.4: Implement Environmental Anomaly Detection and Remediation using `AnchorSnapInfo`.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
    *   **Class:** `AnchorSnapInfo`
    *   **Action:** Continuously monitor `drift_px` values across multiple `AnchorSnapInfo` records over time and across different tasks. If a consistent pattern of unusually high `drift_px` is detected, it suggests a systemic issue (e.g., display scaling change, environmental perception degradation). The agent should flag this as a critical environmental anomaly and potentially trigger self-diagnostic routines, recalibration, or alert human operators, rather than treating each drift as an isolated action failure.
    *   **Reasoning:** The agent learns about its operating environment and can respond to systemic changes, not just task-specific failures.

**4. Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants**

*   **Invariant: No DOM/selectors, zero-abstraction**
    *   **Task 4.1: Remove or rename `dom_id`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
        *   **Classes:** `ExecutionTargetSnapshot`
        *   **Action:** Remove the `dom_id: str | None` field. Operon explicitly operates without DOM abstractions. If an internal ID for a visual object is needed, rename `target_element_id` to something like `visual_object_id` and ensure its derivation is purely from visual perception, not browser DOM.
        *   **Reasoning:** `dom_id` is a direct violation of the "no DOM" and "zero-abstraction" invariants.
    *   **Task 4.2: Clarify/refactor `target_element_id` fields.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
        *   **Classes:** `ExecutionTargetSnapshot`, `ExecutionReresolutionTrace`
        *   **Action:** For `target_element_id`, `original_target_element_id`, and `final_target_element_id`, clarify in documentation and (if possible) rename to `visual_object_id` or `perceived_entity_id`. These IDs *must* be internal identifiers assigned by Operon to perceived visual entities, not browser-supplied element IDs. If they are currently derived from DOM, this constitutes a violation and requires re-architecting their source.
        *   **Reasoning:** The names strongly imply a DOM relationship, violating "zero-abstraction" if not purely vision-derived.
    *   **Task 4.3: Remove `SelectorTrace` and `OriginalTargetSignature` references.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
        *   **Classes:** `ExecutionReresolutionTrace`
        *   **Action:** Remove `selector_trace: SelectorTrace` and `original_target_signature: OriginalTargetSignature`. These are imported from `src.models.selector`, which directly contradicts Operon's "no selectors" invariant. The re-resolution process must be based purely on visual intent and visual feedback. Replace `OriginalTargetSignature` with a truly visual signature type (e.g., `VisualFeatureSet` or `PerceptualHash`) if such a concept is needed.
        *   **Reasoning:** Explicit use of `SelectorTrace` and `OriginalTargetSignature` from `src.models.selector` is a direct violation of "no DOM/selectors."

*   **Invariant: Atomic focus+type**
    *   **Task 4.4: Re-evaluate `focus_verification_result` within atomic actions.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
        *   **Class:** `ExecutionAttemptTrace`
        *   **Action:** If agent actions like "type" implicitly include "focus" as an atomic part of the interaction, then `focus_verification_result` should not exist as a separate top-level field that implies a separable step in the agent's logic. Instead, any focus verification failure should be subsumed into the overall `verification_result` for the *atomic* action. The agent should express high-level atomic intents (e.g., "type 'hello' into the text field at X,Y"). The underlying execution system handles the sub-steps like focusing.
        *   **Reasoning:** The presence of a separate `focus_verification_result` suggests the agent is conceptualizing "focus" and "type" as distinct, potentially non-atomic steps, which violates the "atomic focus+type" invariant.

*   **Invariant: Visual servo**
    *   **Task 4.5: Ensure all target identification and interaction is vision-driven.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\execution.py`
        *   **Classes:** All classes interacting with target identification.
        *   **Action:** Audit the entire system to ensure that despite the `target_element_id` and `original_intent` fields (which, if retained, must be purely internal, vision-derived constructs), the fundamental mechanism for identifying and interacting with targets is based on visual coordinates (`x`, `y`, `width`, `height`), visibility, and interactability, as reflected in `ExecutionTargetSnapshot` and `AnchorSnapInfo`. Any residual reliance on abstract, non-visual identifiers for core interaction logic is a violation.
        *   **Reasoning:** The "no DOM/selectors" invariant directly supports "visual servo." If targets are ultimately resolved via non-visual means, the visual servoing becomes secondary, violating the principle.

If an artifact's content changes, the hash in the log record would no longer match, making the log entry more robustly self-describing and auditable, contributing to strong idempotency regarding reproducibility.

    *   **Reasoning**: As Operon evolves, log schema changes are inevitable. An explicit `schema_version` in each log record allows parsing systems to correctly interpret older or newer log entries, ensuring idempotent processing across schema migrations.
