## `src\models\memory.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **Task 1.1: Implement a caching layer for `MemoryHint` retrieval.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and related data access layers)
        *   **Function:** N/A (system-level pattern)
        *   **Action:** Design and implement an in-memory cache (e.g., an LRU cache) for `MemoryHint` objects, keyed by `key`. Since `MemoryHint`s are frequently accessed for rule evaluation and LLM prompts, caching them will significantly reduce database lookup latency. Ensure cache invalidation or refresh mechanisms are in place when underlying `MemoryRecord` data (affecting `count` or `weight`) changes.
    *   **Task 1.2: Implement asynchronous, batched updates for `MemoryRecord`s.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and related data access layers)
        *   **Function:** N/A (system-level pattern)
        *   **Action:** When updating `MemoryRecord`s (especially `count` and `weight`), queue these updates in an asynchronous buffer and perform batched writes to the persistent store. This amortizes I/O costs and prevents individual write operations from blocking the real-time inference loop.
    *   **Task 1.3: Pre-materialize `MemoryHint`s for fast query.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and related data processing)
        *   **Function:** N/A (system-level pattern)
        *   **Action:** Create a dedicated "read-model" or materialized view for `MemoryHint`s. A background process should periodically aggregate relevant `MemoryRecord`s to compute `count` and `effective weight` for each `MemoryHint`, storing these pre-computed values in a highly optimized, denormalized data store (e.g., a key-value store or a document database optimized for reads). This avoids on-demand aggregation during inference.
    *   **Task 1.4: Optimize storage indexes for `MemoryRecord` access.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and related database schema)
        *   **Function:** N/A (system-level pattern)
        *   **Action:** Ensure the persistent storage for `MemoryRecord`s is indexed efficiently, particularly on `key`, `benchmark`, and potentially `page_hint` (if it's a searchable identifier) to enable rapid retrieval of relevant records during inference or hint generation.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task 2.1: Revise `MemoryRecord` update mechanism for `count` and `weight` to ensure idempotency.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and consuming services)
        *   **Function:** N/A (impacts how these models are updated)
        *   **Action:** The `count` and `weight` fields are stateful and modified with incremental/decremental operations. For idempotent updates, traditional increment/halving operations are problematic if retried. Implement updates using one of the following strategies:
            *   **Conditional Update (CAS):** When updating `weight` (e.g., halving), use a compare-and-swap (CAS) operation or optimistic locking. Read the current `weight` and `count`, compute the new value, and update only if the `current_weight` hasn't changed since it was read. Include a `version` field (e.g., `update_version: int = Field(default=0, ge=0)`) in `MemoryRecord` to facilitate this.
            *   **Event-Sourcing inspired:** Instead of updating `count` and `weight` directly, store individual immutable "memory events" (e.g., `MemoryUsedEvent`, `VerificationFailedEvent`). A projection or aggregation service would then compute the `count` and `weight` from these events, making the update logic idempotent at the event processing layer.
            *   **Idempotency Key:** For each operation that modifies `MemoryRecord`, require a unique `idempotency_key` from the caller. The system would then ensure that only the first operation with a given key is processed for a specific record.
    *   **Task 2.2: Add an `event_id` or `operation_id` to `MemoryRecord` for tracking.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py`
        *   **Function:** `MemoryRecord`
        *   **Action:** Consider adding a field like `event_id: UUID = Field(default_factory=uuid.uuid4)` to `MemoryRecord` to uniquely identify the specific occurrence that led to its creation or a significant update. This ID can be used in conjunction with idempotency keys (Task 2.1) to prevent duplicate processing of the same underlying event, especially for updates to `count` and `weight`.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **Task 3.1: Implement adaptive hint prioritization based on `weight` and `outcome`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and `get_hints()` logic)
        *   **Function:** N/A (implies a service consuming these models)
        *   **Action:** Leverage the `weight` field to dynamically prioritize `MemoryHint`s. Hints with `weight` below a threshold (e.g., 0.1 as specified) should be actively deprioritized or pruned. Furthermore, integrate a learning mechanism that, based on `MemoryOutcome.SUCCESS` vs. `MemoryOutcome.FAILURE` for a given `key`, adjusts the `weight` more aggressively or applies boosts for consistently successful hints. This allows the agent to self-optimize its advisory knowledge base.
    *   **Task 3.2: Implement automated fallback and retry strategies based on `failure_category` and `subgoal`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and policy/execution engine)
        *   **Function:** N/A (implies a service consuming these models)
        *   **Action:** The agent should analyze sequences of `MemoryRecord`s. If a specific `(page_hint, subgoal, action_type)` combination consistently leads to a `FAILURE` with a known `failure_category` (e.g., "element_not_found" or "timeout"), the agent should automatically:
            *   **Switch tactics:** Refer to other `MemoryRecord`s for the same `subgoal` that had `SUCCESS` with a different `action_type`.
            *   **Modify `subgoal`:** Break down the current `subgoal` into smaller, potentially more robust steps, or attempt an alternative `subgoal` if available.
            *   **Re-perceive:** Trigger a deeper visual perception pass before retrying the action. This goes beyond simple retries by dynamically adapting the execution plan.
    *   **Task 3.3: Develop proactive meta-learning for `hint` generation and refinement.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and hint generation logic)
        *   **Function:** N/A (implies a service consuming these models)
        *   **Action:** Beyond just using hints, the agent should actively learn *how* to generate better hints. If `MemoryHint`s generated by a specific `source` consistently lead to `FAILURE` (low `weight`), the agent should trigger an analysis of that `source`'s methodology, potentially:
            *   Suggesting adjustments to the hint generation algorithm.
            *   Requesting human feedback on problematic hints.
            *   Exploring alternative `hint` formulations for similar `page_hint` and `subgoal` contexts.
    *   **Task 3.4: Enable contextual generalization and transfer learning across `benchmarks`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py` (and learning/inference engine)
        *   **Function:** N/A (implies a service consuming these models)
        *   **Action:** Utilize the `benchmark` and `key` fields to identify patterns that generalize. If the agent successfully learns a specific `subgoal` execution strategy for a `page_hint` within one `benchmark`, it should proactively attempt to apply or adapt that knowledge to visually similar `page_hint`s or semantically similar `subgoal`s in other `benchmarks`, even if no `MemoryRecord` explicitly links them. This requires robust visual similarity matching for `PageHint`s.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Task 4.1: Remove `target_element_id` field due to direct violation of "no DOM/selectors" invariant.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\memory.py`
        *   **Function:** `MemoryRecord`
        *   **Action:** The `target_element_id` field explicitly references an "element ID", which implies a structural abstraction like a DOM element or a similar underlying object model. Operon's core invariant is "no DOM/selectors" and "zero-abstraction". A vision-only agent interacts with *visual regions* or *perceptual features*, not abstract element IDs. This field must be removed or rephrased to refer to purely visual coordinates or features (e.g., `target_visual_region: BoundingBox | None`).
    *   **Task 4.2: Scrutinize `PageHint` definition for potential violations of "no DOM/selectors".**
        *   **File:** `src\models\perception.py` (where `PageHint` is defined)
        *   **Function:** `PageHint`
        *   **Action:** While `PageHint` itself is not defined in this module, its name and typical usage patterns in other systems often involve structural page information. Given the explicit `target_element_id` in `MemoryRecord`, there is a high risk that `PageHint` also incorporates DOM-derived or structural abstractions. Review the definition of `src.models.perception.PageHint` to ensure it exclusively relies on visual properties (e.g., perceptual hashes, visual feature vectors, coordinates of regions of interest) and contains absolutely no references to DOM elements, CSS selectors, XPath, or similar structural concepts. If it does, refactor `PageHint` to be purely vision-based.

## `src\models\perception.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference**
    *   **Task:** Optimize `UIElement._populate_canonical_fields` to avoid redundant dictionary copies and computations when possible.
        *   **Reasoning:** The `model_validator(mode="before")` currently creates a `dict(data)` copy and recomputes `primary_name`, `name_source`, `is_unlabeled`, and `usable_for_targeting` on every instantiation, even if the input `data` dictionary already contains these canonical fields (e.g., if `UIElement` is being created from a serialized `UIElement` dictionary). While the logic is fast, repeated copying and derivation on large lists (`ScreenPerception.visible_elements`) can accumulate latency.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  Modify `src/models/perception.py::UIElement._populate_canonical_fields` to first check if canonical fields (`primary_name`, `name_source`, `is_unlabeled`, `usable_for_targeting`) are already present and valid in `data`. If so, skip their re-derivation.
            2.  Consider adding a factory method like `UIElement.from_raw_data(raw_data: RawUIElement)` that explicitly performs the transformation once from a `RawUIElement` instance or its dictionary representation, ensuring the `_populate_canonical_fields` validator is optimized for raw input.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task:** Clarify and ensure the idempotency of `UIElement` transformations when data might already be in a partially canonical form.
        *   **Reasoning:** The `_normalize_optional_text` function is structurally idempotent, which is good. However, the `UIElement._populate_canonical_fields` validator, when applied via `mode="before"`, will *always* recompute `primary_name`, `name_source`, `is_unlabeled`, and `usable_for_targeting`. If `UIElement` is ever instantiated from a dictionary that *already represents* a `UIElement` (e.g., deserialized JSON), these derivations are redundant. True structural idempotency for the `UIElement` transformation means applying the transformation to an already transformed `UIElement` (represented as a dictionary) should not change its canonical fields.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  Refine `src/models/perception.py::UIElement._populate_canonical_fields` to explicitly check if `primary_name` and `name_source` (and derived fields) are already set and consistent within the input `data` dictionary. If they are, avoid recomputing them. This will make the model validation truly idempotent for inputs that are already in or near canonical form.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**
    *   **Task:** Implement dynamic learning and adaptation for `UIElementType` and `PageHint` classifications.
        *   **Reasoning:** The `_missing_` methods for `UIElementType` and `PageHint` gracefully handle unknown string values by marking them `UNKNOWN`. This is a good foundation, but an Operon agent can go further. An agent could learn from these `UNKNOWN` classifications over time to refine its perception model.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  **src/models/perception.py:** While not directly in this file, consider adding a system to `src/models/perception.py::UIElementType` and `src/models/perception.py::PageHint` that, when `_missing_` is triggered, logs the unknown `value` along with context (e.g., screenshot path, surrounding elements, current task).
            2.  **Agentic Feature (Conceptual):** Introduce a meta-learning service that analyzes these logs. If a particular "unknown" `UIElementType` or `PageHint` string consistently appears and correlates with successful subsequent agent actions, the system could propose adding it as a new valid enum member (e.g., via a model update or dynamic registration), or automatically map it to an existing type with high confidence.

    *   **Task:** Introduce adaptive targeting logic based on element confidence and `is_unlabeled` status.
        *   **Reasoning:** `UIElement.confidence` and `UIElement.is_unlabeled` provide strong signals about the reliability and clarity of element perception. Standard workflow engines typically follow rigid rules. Operon, as an agent, can adapt its behavior based on these signals.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  **src/models/perception.py:** While the direct implementation would be in the action-selection/targeting components, ensure that the `confidence` and `is_unlabeled` fields are readily accessible and used by the agent's decision-making logic.
            2.  **Agentic Feature (Conceptual):** Design the agent to:
                *   Prioritize elements with high `confidence` and `usable_for_targeting=True`.
                *   If target elements have low `confidence` or are `is_unlabeled=True`, the agent could trigger a re-perception with different parameters (e.g., higher visual acuity, different detection models), or try alternative targeting strategies (e.g., text search for elements with synthetic names if a specific pattern is observed).
                *   For `is_unlabeled=True` elements, the agent could proactively attempt to infer a more semantic `primary_name` by analyzing surrounding `TEXT` or `LABEL` elements, or by leveraging context from the current task goal.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants**
    *   **Invariant:** `no DOM/selectors` (vision-only, zero-abstraction).
    *   **Task:** Clarify the origin and derivation of `name` and `role` fields to ensure strict adherence to the "vision-only" invariant.
        *   **Reasoning:** The fields `label`, `text`, `placeholder` are clearly tied to visual elements. However, `name` (e.g., HTML `name` attribute) and `role` (e.g., ARIA `role` attribute) are typically DOM-specific attributes. If these fields (`RawUIElement.name`, `RawUIElement.role`, `UIElementNameSource.NAME`, `UIElementNameSource.ROLE`) are derived from parsing a DOM structure or accessibility tree, this violates Operon's core "no DOM/selectors" and "zero-abstraction" invariants. They *must* be derived purely from visual analysis (e.g., OCR, visual classification, layout analysis inferring semantic role).
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  **Documentation:** Add explicit comments or docstrings to `src/models/perception.py::RawUIElement` and `src/models/perception.py::UIElementNameSource` clarifying that `name` and `role` are *visually inferred semantic equivalents* and never sourced from DOM attributes. For example: "The 'name' field represents a visually inferred semantic name for the element, distinct from any underlying DOM 'name' attribute."
            2.  **Renaming (Consideration):** If ambiguity persists, consider renaming `name` to `visual_name` and `role` to `inferred_role` in `RawUIElement` and `UIElementNameSource` to visually emphasize their non-DOM origin. This might be a more robust solution to prevent future deviations.

    *   **Invariant:** `atomic focus+type`.
    *   **Task:** Confirm `element_id` is a purely visual/internal identifier, not a DOM-based one.
        *   **Reasoning:** The `element_id` is crucial for uniquely identifying elements for atomic actions. If `element_id` originates from a DOM attribute (e.g., HTML `id` attribute), it would violate the "no DOM/selectors" invariant. Given "vision-only, zero-abstraction", it must be an internal identifier generated by the visual perception system.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:**
            1.  **Documentation:** Add a docstring to `src/models/perception.py::RawUIElement.element_id` (and `UIElement.element_id`) explicitly stating that this is an internal, visually-derived, or system-generated unique identifier and is *not* sourced from any underlying DOM `id` attribute.

    *   **Invariant:** `visual servo`.
    *   **Task:** No direct violations observed; coordinates and `monitor_origin` are present and consistent with visual servoing.
        *   **Reasoning:** The presence of `x`, `y`, `width`, `height` in `RawUIElement` and `UIElement`, and `monitor_origin` in `RawScreenPerception` and `ScreenPerception`, directly supports the visual servoing invariant by providing necessary positional information for precise interaction.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** None, as this invariant is well-supported by the current schema.

## `src\models\policy.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 latency for real-time inference**

    *   **Task 1.1: Refactor `AgentAction` using Pydantic discriminated unions.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction`, `ActionType`, `validate_payload`
        *   **Description:** The `validate_payload` method in `AgentAction` is a large, complex, and imperative validator. It introduces significant runtime overhead due to its extensive conditional checks for every `AgentAction` instantiation. To reduce P99 latency for real-time inference, refactor `AgentAction` into a Pydantic discriminated union.
        *   **Action:**
            1.  Define a base `AgentActionBase(StrictModel)` class (or rename `AgentAction` to `AgentActionBase`).
            2.  For each `ActionType` (or groups of similar `ActionType`s), create a specific Pydantic model that inherits from `AgentActionBase`.
            3.  Move the specific validation logic (required fields, forbidden fields) from `validate_payload` into the field definitions and `model_validator`s of these new action-specific models.
            4.  Modify the main `AgentAction` definition to be a `pydantic.Field(discriminator='action_type')` union of these specific models.
            5.  Delete the `validate_payload` method from the original `AgentAction` (or `AgentActionBase`). This leverages Pydantic's optimized parsing and validation based on the `action_type` field, eliminating the monolithic `if/elif` chain.

2.  **Identify opportunities for structural idempotency**

    *   **Task 2.1: Add an `idempotency_key` field to `AgentAction`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction`
        *   **Description:** For an agent to robustly recover from errors or re-execute actions without unintended side effects, the execution layer needs a mechanism to identify and track whether an action's intended effect has already been achieved. Adding an `idempotency_key` allows the agent to provide a unique identifier for a logical action instance.
        *   **Action:** Add `idempotency_key: str | None = Field(default=None, min_length=1)` to the `AgentAction` model. This key would be supplied by the agent and used by the executor to check for prior completion.

    *   **Task 2.2: Consider an `expected_post_condition` field for `AgentAction` (optional, for later stages).**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction`
        *   **Description:** While not directly structural *idempotency* in the `AgentAction` model itself, enabling the agent to specify an `expected_post_condition` for an action would allow the executor to verify if the action's goal is already met. If the post-condition is observed before execution, the action can be treated as a no-op, contributing to robust, idempotent-like behavior.
        *   **Action:** Evaluate adding `expected_post_condition: str | None = Field(default=None)` to `AgentAction`. This would require a clear definition of how `expected_post_condition` strings are parsed and evaluated by the executor. (This is a more advanced agentic feature that supports idempotency, potentially for a later iteration).

3.  **Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines**

    *   **Task 3.1: Introduce an `on_failure_strategy` field to `AgentAction`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction`
        *   **Description:** Standard workflow engines typically fail upon action execution errors. Agentic systems should be able to specify self-healing or adaptive responses. An `on_failure_strategy` field would allow the agent to dictate how the executor should react to a specific action failure, enabling rudimentary self-correction.
        *   **Action:**
            1.  Define a new `FailureStrategy(StrEnum)` or similar model (e.g., `RETRY_N_TIMES`, `LOG_AND_CONTINUE`, `PROMPT_USER`, `REPLAN`, `STOP`).
            2.  Add `on_failure_strategy: FailureStrategy | None = None` to the `AgentAction` model.

    *   **Task 3.2: Add `WAIT_FOR_VISUAL_CONDITION` `ActionType`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `ActionType`, `AgentAction`
        *   **Description:** The existing `WAIT` action uses a fixed duration. An agentic system benefits from adaptive waiting based on perceptual changes. `WAIT_FOR_VISUAL_CONDITION` would allow the agent to pause execution until a specific visual state (e.g., element appears, text matches, image region changes) is observed, leading to more robust and context-aware workflows.
        *   **Action:**
            1.  Add `WAIT_FOR_VISUAL_CONDITION = "wait_for_visual_condition"` to `ActionType`.
            2.  When refactoring `AgentAction` (Task 1.1), create a specific model for `WAIT_FOR_VISUAL_CONDITION` that includes fields like `target_region: BoundingBox | None`, `expected_text: str | None`, `timeout_ms: int`, `poll_interval_ms: int`. (You might need to define a `BoundingBox` schema in `common.py` or directly use `x, y, x_end, y_end` for target region).

    *   **Task 3.3: Introduce `priority` field to `PolicyDecision`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `PolicyDecision`
        *   **Description:** For multi-objective or complex agent systems, conveying the relative importance or urgency of a decision can be crucial for task scheduling, resource allocation, and conflict resolution.
        *   **Action:** Add `priority: int = Field(default=50, ge=0, le=100)` to the `PolicyDecision` model, where a higher number indicates higher priority.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants**

    *   **Task 4.1: Clarify/rename `selector` and `TargetSelectionContext` due to "no DOM/selectors" invariant.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction`, `TargetSelectionContext`
        *   **Description:** Operon's invariant strictly states "no DOM/selectors". The field `selector: str | None` in `AgentAction` and the imported `TargetSelectionContext` are highly ambiguous given this invariant. If `selector` refers to a traditional DOM-based selector (CSS, XPath), it is a direct violation. If `TargetSelectionContext` contains any DOM-specific information, it's also a violation. Even if they are *intended* to be visual descriptors, the naming itself contradicts the "zero-abstraction" principle by using terminology commonly associated with DOM.
        *   **Action:**
            1.  **If `selector` is indeed a DOM selector:** **FLAG AS DIRECT VIOLATION.** Remove `selector` and `TargetSelectionContext` and replace them with purely coordinate-based (`x, y, x_end, y_end`) or visual-label-based (e.g., `visual_label: str`, `image_pattern_id: str`) targeting mechanisms.
            2.  **If `selector` is *not* a DOM selector but a visual descriptor (e.g., text, visual pattern ID):** Rename `selector` to something explicit like `visual_label: str | None` or `visual_pattern_id: str | None` to prevent confusion and explicitly align with "vision-only, zero-abstraction".
            3.  Ensure the definition of `TargetSelectionContext` (in `src/models/selector.py`) contains *only* visual, coordinate, or semantic (non-DOM) information. If it contains DOM elements or attributes, **FLAG AS DIRECT VIOLATION.**

    *   **Task 4.2: Address "targetless TYPE" implication for "atomic focus+type" invariant.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\policy.py`
        *   **Function/Class:** `AgentAction.validate_payload` (or the new `TYPE` specific model)
        *   **Description:** The invariant is "atomic focus+type". The validator for `ActionType.TYPE` explicitly states: "Targetless TYPE is allowed: executor types into the currently focused element." This creates a potential decoupling of the "focus" and "type" operations from the agent's decision-making perspective. If an agent emits a `TYPE` action without a target, it relies on a previously focused element, implying `focus` might have been a separate, non-atomic decision or implicitly assumed.
        *   **Action:**
            1.  **Stronger Enforcement:** To strictly enforce "atomic focus+type," *every* `TYPE` action should explicitly or implicitly include its own focusing mechanism. This means a `TYPE` action should *always* require a target (`selector`, `target_element_id`, or `x,y`) to ensure the focus operation is part of the atomic `TYPE` execution.
            2.  **Remove Targetless `TYPE`:** Modify the validation logic to require a target for `ActionType.TYPE`. If the intent is to type into whatever is *currently* focused, this "focusing" still needs to be an atomic part of the `TYPE` action, implying the `TYPE` action might have an implicit target of "current focus" rather than explicit `None`. However, allowing `None` for target contradicts the spirit of *atomic* focus+type by making focus a prerequisite rather than part of the action itself.

## `src\models\recovery.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.**
    *   **Task 1.1: Implement caching for `RecoveryDecision` instances.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Indirectly, applies to systems consuming this model)
        *   **Description:** For frequently encountered `FailureCategory` and `LoopStage` combinations, consider pre-computing and caching `RecoveryDecision` objects. This avoids re-evaluation of recovery logic and Pydantic model instantiation overhead, reducing decision latency in critical paths.
        *   **Action:** Add a mechanism to cache and retrieve `RecoveryDecision` instances based on failure context, rather than re-calculating them every time.
    *   **Task 1.2: Optimize Pydantic serialization/deserialization where `RecoveryDecision` is a bottleneck.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Indirectly, applies to data transfer)
        *   **Description:** If `RecoveryDecision` objects are frequently serialized or deserialized across process boundaries or for logging, and this becomes a P99 bottleneck, investigate faster serialization formats (e.g., Avro, MessagePack) or Pydantic's `model_dump_json(mode='json')` vs. `json.dumps(model_dump())` optimizations. For simple models like this, initial Pydantic overhead is usually low, but it's a general latency consideration.
        *   **Action:** Monitor serialization/deserialization performance of `RecoveryDecision`. If it appears in P99 traces, investigate alternative methods.
    *   **Task 1.3: Explore asynchronous signaling for `WAIT_AND_RETRY` scenarios.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `retry_after_ms` field)
        *   **Description:** Instead of a blocking wait dictated by `retry_after_ms`, consider an asynchronous signaling mechanism where the recovery loop can transition to a "waiting" state and process other tasks or prepare for the retry without actively blocking, thereby reducing perceived latency or improving resource utilization.
        *   **Action:** Design a recovery orchestrator that can handle `WAIT_AND_RETRY` strategies non-blockingly, allowing other agent processes to continue during the wait period.

2.  **Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.**
    *   **Task 2.1: Ensure execution of `CONTEXT_RESET` and `SESSION_RESET` is idempotent.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `RecoveryStrategy` enum)
        *   **Description:** The strategies `CONTEXT_RESET` and `SESSION_RESET` fundamentally aim to bring the system to a known, clean state. Applying these strategies multiple times should consistently result in that same clean state, without unintended accumulation of effects or errors.
        *   **Action:** Verify that the underlying implementation for `CONTEXT_RESET` and `SESSION_RESET` performs a true reset to a fixed, reproducible state, making repeated applications harmless.
    *   **Task 2.2: Design `RETRY_SAME_STEP` and `RETRY_DIFFERENT_TACTIC` for idempotent side-effects.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `RecoveryStrategy` enum)
        *   **Description:** While the *decision* to retry is idempotent, the *execution* of the retried step or tactic must be designed to be as idempotent as possible. This prevents unintended state changes, duplicate actions (e.g., submitting a form twice), or resource consumption if a step fails partially after a side effect.
        *   **Action:** When implementing steps that can be retried, ensure they are transactional, or that their side-effects are idempotent by design (e.g., using "UPSERT" logic instead of "INSERT").
    *   **Task 2.3: Verify terminal `RecoveryDecision` states are consistently idempotent.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `terminal` field and `STOP` strategy)
        *   **Description:** Once a `RecoveryDecision` with `terminal=True` (e.g., `STOP`) is applied, the system should consistently remain in that terminal state regardless of how many times the decision is processed or checked. This ensures predictable system behavior after unrecoverable failures.
        *   **Action:** Confirm that the system's state machine correctly handles terminal decisions such that repeated attempts to "stop" or "process a terminal state" do not lead to further actions or state changes.

3.  **Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.**
    *   **Task 3.1: Implement adaptive learning for `RecoveryStrategy` selection and `retry_after_ms`.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `RecoveryStrategy`, `retry_after_ms`, `failure_category`, `failure_stage` fields)
        *   **Description:** Beyond static rules, Operon could learn and adapt its recovery behavior. For a given `FailureCategory` and `LoopStage`, the system could track the success rate of different `RecoveryStrategy` options and dynamically adjust the `retry_after_ms` or prioritize strategies that have historically proven most effective, thus self-optimizing its recovery.
        *   **Action:** Design a feedback loop mechanism that records outcomes of `RecoveryDecision` applications and uses this data to inform future recovery strategy selection and parameter tuning (e.g., using Bayesian optimization or reinforcement learning).
    *   **Task 3.2: Integrate predictive failure analysis to trigger proactive recovery.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `failure_category`, `failure_stage` fields)
        *   **Description:** Instead of waiting for a failure, Operon could use observed patterns (e.g., specific sequences of `LoopStage` leading to certain `FailureCategory` in the past, or external system health metrics) to predict an imminent failure and proactively apply a `RecoveryStrategy` (e.g., `CONTEXT_RESET` or `ADVANCE` to skip a known problematic step) *before* the failure occurs.
        *   **Action:** Develop a predictive model that correlates current `LoopStage` and environmental observations with historical `FailureCategory` data to recommend or trigger proactive `RecoveryDecision`s.
    *   **Task 3.3: Enable dynamic, multi-step recovery plan generation.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to `RecoveryStrategy` enum)
        *   **Description:** Instead of just picking a single `RecoveryStrategy`, an advanced agent could generate a *sequence* of strategies (e.g., "RETRY_SAME_STEP" then "BACKOFF" then "CONTEXT_RESET") tailored to the observed failure and system state. This allows for more sophisticated and nuanced self-healing workflows than standard engines.
        *   **Action:** Design a planning component that, given a failure context, can synthesize a short recovery plan composed of multiple `RecoveryStrategy` steps, rather than just selecting one.
    *   **Task 3.4: Leverage vision-only input for recovery decisioning based on visual anomalies.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py` (Relates to all fields, especially `message`, `failure_category`)
        *   **Description:** Given Operon's vision-only nature, recovery decisions shouldn't solely rely on internal error codes but also on visual observations. For instance, a `FailureCategory` could be inferred from a visually unresponsive UI, a persistent loading spinner, or unexpected visual artifacts, triggering a `RecoveryDecision` based on this visual evidence. The `message` field could then detail the visual anomaly.
        *   **Action:** Integrate vision-based perception modules to analyze screen content for indicators of failure (e.g., UI freezes, error dialogs, unexpected elements) and use these as inputs for generating `RecoveryDecision`s.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**
    *   **Task 4.1: Confirm module adheres to invariants and add future implementation caution.**
        *   **File:** `src\models\recovery.py`
        *   **Description:** The `src\models\recovery.py` module defines Pydantic schemas and enums; as such, it does not directly contain any operational logic that could violate Operon's invariants (no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo).
        *   **Action:** No direct action is required on this module.
        *   **Cautionary Note:** The *implementation* of the recovery strategies (e.g., the code that executes `RETRY_SAME_STEP` or `ADVANCE`) must stringently adhere to these invariants. Any code that acts upon a `RecoveryDecision` must operate solely through vision-based perception and atomic, low-level interactions without relying on DOM, selectors, or non-visual input abstractions.

## `src\models\selector.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference:**
    *   **Task:** Evaluate the impact of `TargetEvidence` list sizes (e.g., `top_candidates` in `SelectorTrace` and `TargetSelectionContext`, `matched_signals`, `rejected_by` in `TargetEvidence`) on P99 latency.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** Consider if `top_candidates` requires full serialization of all `TargetEvidence` for real-time inference or if a lighter summary (e.g., top N scores, or just the `selected_candidate_evidence`) is sufficient for the core decision path, with full evidence only for debug/replay. If `TargetEvidence` is large, explore reducing the number of candidates retained or returned for hot paths.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `SelectorTrace.top_candidates`, `TargetSelectionContext.top_candidates`, `TargetEvidence.matched_signals`, `TargetEvidence.rejected_by`.
    *   **Task:** Investigate the performance implications of the `SelectorRecoveryStrategy` mechanism.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** The sequential application of recovery strategies (implied by `recovery_attempted`, `recovery_strategy_used`, `adjusted_acceptance_threshold`, `adjusted_ambiguity_margin`) can increase P99 latency. Implement a mechanism to prioritize recovery strategies based on `FailureCategory` and `TargetIntent` to avoid iterating through less effective strategies. Consider parallelizing evaluation of some recovery strategies if the underlying computations are independent.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `SelectorRecoveryStrategy`, `SelectorTrace` fields related to recovery.
    *   **Task:** Optimize string normalization in `TargetIntent`.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** For very high-frequency path, evaluate if `_normalize_optional_text` field validator adds measurable overhead. If so, consider moving `strip()` operations to the point of data ingestion rather than model validation, or ensuring the upstream data source provides pre-normalized strings. Pydantic v2 validators are generally efficient, but extreme P99 scenarios warrant a check.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `TargetIntent._normalize_optional_text`.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency:**
    *   **Task:** Enhance `TargetSelectionContext` for deterministic re-resolution.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** To ensure that re-applying the selection logic with the same `TargetSelectionContext` (and visual input) yields the same `selected_candidate_evidence`, strengthen `original_page_signature`. This field should ideally be a cryptographic hash or a robust perceptually-based signature of the *entire visual state* (e.g., screenshot hash, visual element hash) at the time of original selection, not just a textual identifier. This helps guarantee idempotency of the visual input for re-resolution.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `TargetSelectionContext.original_page_signature`.
    *   **Task:** Ensure the selector's decision-making process, given identical inputs, is idempotent.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** The `SelectorTrace` represents a snapshot of the decision. For true idempotency, ensure that the *algorithm* generating this trace (including scoring, filtering, thresholding, and recovery strategies) is deterministic. Any randomness or non-deterministic aspects should be removed or made controllable by a fixed seed. If a selection fails and then recovers, replaying the exact scenario should lead to the same recovery and final decision.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - All selector-related models, especially `SelectorTrace`.
    *   **Task:** Formalize what "re-resolution" means in an idempotent context.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** Define explicitly that `SelectorMode.RERESOLUTION` should, given identical `TargetSelectionContext` and *visual environment*, aim to identify the *same logical target*, even if its pixel coordinates have slightly shifted. This implies the underlying visual matching algorithm should be robust to minor layout changes and be able to consistently re-identify the target based on its learned signature or `original_target` details.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `SelectorMode`.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines:**
    *   **Task:** Implement adaptive recovery strategy learning.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** Leverage `SelectorTrace` data (e.g., `initial_failure_reason`, `recovery_strategy_used`, `final_decision`, `recovery_changed_selected_candidate`) to train a reinforcement learning agent or a heuristic model. This agent could proactively select the *most probable effective* `SelectorRecoveryStrategy` for a given `FailureCategory` and `TargetIntent` rather than applying them sequentially or exhaustively. It could also dynamically adjust `adjusted_acceptance_threshold` and `adjusted_ambiguity_margin` based on past success rates for similar scenarios.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `SelectorTrace`, `SelectorRecoveryStrategy`, `FailureCategory`.
    *   **Task:** Integrate predictive failure and pre-emptive adjustment.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** An agent could monitor the `score_margin` of initial selections. If `score_margin` is consistently low for certain `TargetIntent` types, the agent could proactively trigger a "soft recovery" (e.g., a slight threshold relaxation) *before* an actual `FAILURE` is declared, predicting potential instability. This moves beyond reactive recovery to proactive self-healing.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `SelectorTrace.score_margin`, `SelectorTrace.initial_failure_reason`.
    *   **Task:** Enable explainable agent reasoning for failures and recoveries.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** The `decision_reason`, `rejection_reason`, `matched_signals`, `rejected_by` fields are excellent for debug. Extend this for user-facing explainability. For `final_decision: FAILURE`, the agent should generate a concise, human-readable summary of *why* it failed and *what strategies were attempted and why they failed*, to facilitate human debugging or re-instruction. For `SUCCESS` after recovery, explain *why* recovery was needed and *how* it succeeded.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `TargetEvidence`, `SelectorTrace`.

4.  **Flag Any Violations of Operon's Invariants:**
    *   **Invariant:** "no DOM/selectors"
        *   **Flagged Violation/Ambiguity:** The fields `element_id`, `element_type`, `primary_name`, `role` in `OriginalTargetSignature` and `TargetEvidence` are highly ambiguous regarding this invariant. If `element_id` is derived from a DOM ID, an accessibility tree ID, or any other non-visual, non-zero-abstraction means, it is a **direct violation**. Similarly, `UIElementType` (e.g., "button", "input") and `role` (e.g., "submit", "checkbox") must be derived *solely from visual perception and layout analysis* (e.g., "looks like a button because of its shape, text, and common placement") without relying on underlying DOM or accessibility tree information.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** Add explicit documentation or runtime assertions to enforce that these identifiers and types are generated purely from visual/perceptual cues (e.g., visual hash, coordinate-based ID, OCR + layout analysis) and never from DOM attributes or selectors. Renaming `element_id` to `visual_id` or `perceptual_id` could reinforce this.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `OriginalTargetSignature.element_id`, `OriginalTargetSignature.element_type`, `OriginalTargetSignature.primary_name`, `OriginalTargetSignature.role`, and corresponding fields in `TargetEvidence`.
    *   **Invariant:** "atomic focus+type"
        *   **Flagged Violation/Ambiguity:** The `TargetIntentAction` enum includes `SELECT`, `CHECK`, and `UNCHECK`. These are higher-level actions than "atomic focus+type." While `CLICK` and `TYPE` can be directly decomposed into atomic actions (mouse click, key presses), `SELECT` (e.g., from a dropdown) and `CHECK`/`UNCHECK` (e.g., for a checkbox) imply a higher level of abstraction about UI elements and their state. If these actions are implemented by calling platform-specific APIs (e.g., browser-level `select` event, accessibility API to toggle checkbox state) rather than rigorously decomposing them into atomic visual servoing, focus, and type operations, it would be a **violation**.
        *   **Actionable Suggestion:** Clarify the downstream implementation strategy for `SELECT`, `CHECK`, and `UNCHECK` actions. Each must be decomposed into a sequence of purely visual-servoing, atomic focus/type/click operations. For instance, `SELECT` might involve visually locating a dropdown, clicking it, visually locating an option, and clicking that. `CHECK`/`UNCHECK` would involve visually identifying the checkbox's state and then clicking it if the state needs to change.
        *   **File/Function:** `src/models/selector.py` - `TargetIntentAction.SELECT`, `TargetIntentAction.CHECK`, `TargetIntentAction.UNCHECK`.

## `src\models\state.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.**

*   **Task 1.1: Implement partial state passing for inference context.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and associated inference/planner modules)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState`
    *   **Details:** The `observation_history`, `action_history`, and `verification_history` lists can grow substantially, making full transmission to an LLM inference endpoint a P99 latency bottleneck. Introduce methods or helper functions to `AgentState` that provide a *context-windowed view* of recent history (e.g., last N observations/actions) or a *summarized/compressed representation* of older history (e.g., via embeddings or key event extraction) for LLM prompts. This ensures the LLM receives only immediately relevant information without processing the entire run log.

*   **Task 1.2: Implement asynchronous state persistence.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and the persistence layer responsible for saving `AgentState`)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState`
    *   **Details:** If `AgentState` updates are frequently persisted to disk or a remote store, blocking I/O operations will directly impact the agent's step-time latency. Decouple persistence from the agent's critical path by implementing an asynchronous write-behind cache or an event-driven persistence mechanism. The agent logic should update the in-memory `AgentState` instance, and persistence should occur in the background.

*   **Task 1.3: Explore state compression for history fields.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py`
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.observation_history`, `AgentState.action_history`, `AgentState.verification_history`
    *   **Details:** For historical data that isn't always needed in its raw form (e.g., older observations), investigate compression techniques. This could include run-length encoding for repetitive data, delta encoding between successive entries, or storing only critical metadata for older entries while offloading full content to secondary storage. This reduces memory footprint and deserialization/transfer costs when parts of the history are accessed.

**2. Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.**

*   **Task 2.1: Implement state updates as immutable transformations.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and agent core logic interacting with `AgentState`)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState`
    *   **Details:** Instead of directly mutating `AgentState` attributes in-place (e.g., `state.step_count += 1`), encourage a pattern where updates generate a *new* `AgentState` instance (e.g., using `state.copy(update={'step_count': state.step_count + 1})`). This functional approach ensures that each `AgentState` object represents an immutable snapshot, simplifying reasoning about state transitions, enabling easier rollback, and making persistence naturally idempotent (saving a new state completely replaces the previous one).

*   **Task 2.2: Ensure history appends are handled as idempotent batch operations at the persistence layer.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and persistence layer for `AgentState`)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.observation_history`, `AgentState.action_history`, `AgentState.verification_history`
    *   **Details:** While appending to a list is not intrinsically idempotent, the *storage strategy* can be. When persisting `AgentState` with updated histories, ensure the persistence layer either replaces the entire history list (if using an immutable approach per Task 2.1) or uses a mechanism (e.g., transaction IDs, `upsert` semantics based on unique identifiers for historical entries) that prevents duplicate entries if a write operation is retried. This guarantees consistency even under intermittent storage failures.

**3. Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.**

*   **Task 3.1: Implement adaptive retry strategies based on `last_rule_trace` and `stop_reason`.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and agent core logic, planner)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.retry_counts`, `AgentState.target_failure_counts`, `AgentState.stop_reason`, `AgentState.last_rule_trace`
    *   **Details:** Enhance the retry mechanism beyond simple fixed counts. Leverage the `last_rule_trace` to provide specific context to the LLM or a deterministic recovery module. For instance, if `last_rule_trace` indicates a specific UI element disappeared, the agent could try a different navigation path or force a screen refresh (via `force_fresh_perception`) with a targeted delay. If `stop_reason` is `NO_PROGRESS`, trigger a higher-level re-evaluation of the current `subgoal` by the LLM instead of a naive retry, allowing for dynamic strategy shifts.

*   **Task 3.2: Develop a learned recovery mechanism using `force_fresh_perception` success/failure.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and agent core logic, learning modules)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.force_fresh_perception`, `AgentState.progress_state`
    *   **Details:** Create a feedback loop where the success or failure of `force_fresh_perception` in resolving `NO_PROGRESS` situations is recorded. Over time, the agent can learn the contexts in which this recovery rule is effective versus when more drastic measures (e.g., backtracking, explicit re-initialization of the browser session via `start_url`, or querying a human via `hitl_message`) are required. This moves from a hardcoded rule to an adaptive, experience-driven recovery.

*   **Task 3.3: Introduce proactive anomaly detection using `observation_history`.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and perception, inference modules)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.observation_history`
    *   **Details:** Develop an agentic component that continuously analyzes the `observation_history` for unexpected visual patterns or deviations from anticipated screen states *for the current `current_subgoal`*. This could involve visual similarity metrics, OCR-based change detection, or LLM-driven interpretation of screen descriptions to identify "stuck" states, unexpected pop-ups, or navigation errors *before* a explicit progress-tracking rule flags `NO_PROGRESS`. This allows for earlier intervention and self-correction.

*   **Task 3.4: Implement dynamic goal re-composition based on `progress_state` and `verification_history`.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and agent core logic, planner)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.progress_state`, `AgentState.verification_history`, `AgentState.current_subgoal`, `AgentState.intent`
    *   **Details:** If `progress_state` indicates stagnation (e.g., `is_stuck` is true for too long) or `verification_history` shows repeated failures for a `current_subgoal`, the agent should trigger a meta-level planning step. The LLM or a specialized re-planning module should dynamically re-evaluate the `current_subgoal`'s feasibility, break it down into smaller, alternative steps, or even suggest an entirely different path towards fulfilling the original `intent`. This goes beyond simple retries to adaptive problem-solving.

*   **Task 3.5: Enable learning from `hitl_message` and subsequent human intervention.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and HITL feedback loop, learning modules)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.hitl_message`
    *   **Details:** When a human intervenes based on `hitl_message`, capture not only the human's solution or feedback but also the *context* leading to the intervention and the *outcome* of the human's actions. This rich dataset can be used to fine-tune the LLM, enabling it to learn from human expertise to better handle future similar scenarios autonomously, reduce the need for `hitl_message` in the long run, and generate more effective messages when intervention is truly necessary.

**4. Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**

*   **Task 4.1: Verify `ScreenPerception` and `ExecutedAction` schemas uphold invariants.**
    *   **File:** `src\models\state.py` (and `src\models\perception.py`, `src\models\execution.py`)
    *   **Function:** `AgentState.observation_history`, `AgentState.action_history`
    *   **Details:** The `AgentState` module itself is a data schema and does not directly violate Operon's invariants. However, its composite types, `ScreenPerception` and `ExecutedAction`, are critical. It is imperative that their definitions (in `src\models\perception.py` and `src\models\execution.py` respectively) strictly adhere to:
        *   **No DOM/selectors:** `ScreenPerception` must *not* contain any DOM elements, CSS selectors, XPath, or similar web page structural abstractions. Its content must be derived exclusively from visual data (e.g., image, OCR text, visual bounding boxes, perceived affordances).
        *   **Atomic focus+type:** `ExecutedAction` must represent atomic, indivisible operations that conceptually combine focusing on a visual target and then performing an action (e.g., typing text, clicking), without reliance on intermediate browser states or low-level input events that break the atomicity.
        *   **Visual servo:** `ExecutedAction` must define actions in terms of visually perceived targets (e.g., coordinates relative to a recognized visual element, or an object ID from a vision model), *not* absolute pixel coordinates or DOM-derived positions, directly embodying the visual servo principle.
    *   **Current Module Status:** No direct violations found within `src/models/state.py` itself. The integrity of the invariants relies entirely on the correct implementation of the `ScreenPerception` and `ExecutedAction` schemas.

## `src\models\usage.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-Time Inference

## Current state: `_pricing_for_model` uses sequential `if/elif` checks. Pydantic validation/serialization can introduce overhead in high-throughput scenarios.

- Task: Refactor `src/models/usage.py::_pricing_for_model` to use a dictionary lookup for model pricing rates.
  Description: Replace the current `if/elif` chain with a pre-initialized dictionary (e.g., `_PRICING_RATES`) where keys are `(provider, normalized_model_name)` tuples and values are `(input_rate, output_rate)`. This changes the lookup complexity from O(N) to O(1) average case, significantly reducing P99 latency for cost estimation, especially as the number of supported models grows.
  Example pseudo-code for the change:
  ```python
  _PRICING_RATES: dict[tuple[ModelProvider, str], tuple[float, float]] = {
      ("anthropic", "claude-sonnet-4-20250514"): (3.0, 15.0),
      ("gemini", "gemini-3-flash-preview"): (0.50, 3.00),
      ("gemini", "gemini-2.5-flash"): (0.30, 2.50),
      ("gemini", "gemini-2.5-computer-use-preview-10-2025"): (1.25, 10.00),
      # Add other models here
  }

  def _pricing_for_model(*, provider: ModelProvider, model: str) -> tuple[float | None, float | None]:
      normalized = model.strip().lower()
      return _PRICING_RATES.get((provider, normalized), (None, None))
  ```

- Task: Investigate and optimize the serialization/deserialization performance of `src/models/usage.py::ModelUsage` and `src/models/usage.py::UsageAggregate`.
  Description: For high-frequency recording of model usage, the default Pydantic/JSON serialization might introduce measurable latency. Explore using faster serialization libraries (e.g., `orjson`, `msgpack`, `protobuf`) if these models are frequently serialized for inter-process communication, message queues, or storage. This is an investigation to be triggered if profiling reveals Pydantic overhead on the critical path.

- Task: Implement asynchronous or batched processing for recording `ModelUsage` instances.
  Description: If the creation and storage of `ModelUsage` instances occur synchronously on the critical path of real-time inference, it can increase P99 latency. Design a mechanism to decouple the recording of `ModelUsage` from the main inference flow, possibly by using an asynchronous queue, worker threads/processes, or buffering multiple instances for periodic batched writes to persistence. (This task implies an external logging/persistence component, but its design should consider this module's data.)

# 2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency

## Current state: `estimate_usage_cost` is a pure function. `ModelUsage` is a data schema. `UsageAggregate` is a data schema representing aggregated values.

- Task: Ensure aggregation logic leveraging `src/models/usage.py::UsageAggregate` is idempotent during persistence.
  Description: While `UsageAggregate` itself is a data structure, its use in an aggregation workflow must be idempotent. If `UsageAggregate` objects are updated in a persistent store, the update operations (e.g., incrementing `request_count`, summing `input_tokens`) should be designed to yield the same result whether applied once or multiple times. This often requires database-level atomic increment/upsert operations or ensuring the upstream event processing system can identify and deduplicate events during retry scenarios. This is a design consideration for the aggregation service interacting with `UsageAggregate`.

# 3. Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines

## Current state: The module provides fundamental data for tracking model usage and costs (`ModelUsage`, `UsageAggregate`) and a cost estimation helper. The `thoughts_tokens` field suggests internal agent reasoning.

- Task: Develop a dynamic model switching and fallback mechanism based on real-time cost and performance derived from `src/models/usage.py::ModelUsage` and `src/models/usage.py::UsageAggregate`.
  Description: Design an agentic capability to evaluate the `estimated_cost_usd` or `total_tokens` of model usage in real-time. The agent should dynamically switch to a more cost-effective or performant model (e.g., a "flash" model for simple tasks) for subsequent operations if current usage approaches or exceeds predefined budget thresholds or latency targets, without explicit human intervention.

- Task: Implement a self-correction and introspection loop for excessive `thoughts_tokens`.
  Description: Leverage the `thoughts_tokens` field within `src/models/usage.py::ModelUsage` to monitor the agent's internal reasoning cost. If `thoughts_tokens` for a specific task type or over a given period exceed an adaptive threshold, the agent should proactively trigger a self-correction mechanism (e.g., prompt simplification, switching to a more constrained reasoning style, or generating an internal alert for analysis) to optimize its "thought" process.

- Task: Integrate real-time cost-aware task prioritization and dynamic decomposition using `src/models/usage.py::estimate_usage_cost`.
  Description: Enhance the agent's planning capabilities to use `estimate_usage_cost` to project the cost of different task execution paths or decompositions *before* committing to them. The agent should dynamically prioritize lower-cost paths, explore alternative, cheaper ways to achieve goals, or, if a projected cost exceeds a configurable limit, automatically seek user confirmation or attempt to reformulate the task.

- Task: Implement adaptive caching strategies informed by `src/models/usage.py::cache_creation_input_tokens` and `src/models/usage.py::cache_read_input_tokens`.
  Description: Design an agentic feature that continuously analyzes the efficiency of the caching mechanism by comparing `cache_creation_input_tokens` against `cache_read_input_tokens`. If the effective cache hit rate is low or the cost of cache creation is too high, the agent should autonomously adjust caching policies (e.g., invalidate older entries faster, change cache eviction strategies, or reconsider what data is cached) to optimize for overall cost and performance.

# 4. Violations of Operon's Invariants

## Operon Invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.
## Current state: The module `src/models/usage.py` is a backend data model and utility module.

- Task: No direct violations identified within `src/models/usage.py`.
  Description: The provided module defines data schemas and pure functions; it does not contain any code that interacts with the Document Object Model (DOM), uses selectors, or directly participates in UI focus, typing, or visual servo loops.

- Task: Mandate that any system interacting with `src/models/usage.py` (e.g., logging `ModelUsage`) must ensure minimal latency impact to uphold Operon's real-time interaction invariants.
  Description: While the module itself is compliant, downstream systems responsible for recording `ModelUsage` data or performing cost estimations using `estimate_usage_cost` must be designed to execute these operations asynchronously or with extremely low latency to avoid disrupting the atomic nature of Operon's `focus+type` actions or the real-time feedback loops inherent in `visual servo` operations. Any synchronous logging on the critical path that introduces perceptible delay would be an indirect violation of Operon's operational principles.

## `src\models\verification.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.**
    *   **Task 1.1:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationResult` - For fields like `reason`, `recovery_hint`, `video_detail`, and `critic_fallback_reason`, consider introducing or allowing for `StrEnum` alternatives (e.g., `SpecificFailureReasonEnum | str`) for common, high-frequency critical paths. This would enable faster programmatic interpretation and branching by the agent, reducing string parsing overhead compared to arbitrary strings, while retaining `str` for less frequent or debugging scenarios.
    *   **Task 1.2:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationResult` - Explore pre-instantiating immutable `VerificationResult` objects for common, simple success or failure states (e.g., `VerificationResult.SUCCESS_NO_OP`, `VerificationResult.TRANSIENT_LOADING`) as static constants. This can reduce Pydantic validation and object creation overhead in hot loops where these states are frequently reported.

2.  **Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.**
    *   **Task 2.1:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationResult` - Explicitly document and enforce that instances of `VerificationResult` should be treated as immutable snapshots of a *single* verification attempt. If a process involves retries (as implied by `patience_retries`), each retry should ideally generate a *new* `VerificationResult` instance to represent the updated state. This ensures that the recorded outcome for any given attempt is idempotent, preventing unintended side effects from re-processing or re-broadcasting the same result.

3.  **Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.**
    *   **Task 3.1:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationResult` - Enhance the `recovery_hint` field from a free-form `str` to a more structured type, such as a dedicated `RecoveryStrategyEnum` (e.g., `RecoveryStrategyEnum.RETRY_LAST_ACTION`, `RecoveryStrategyEnum.RECALIBRATE_VISUALS`, `RecoveryStrategyEnum.RELOAD_PAGE`). This allows the agent to programmatically interpret and execute specific, sophisticated self-healing workflows directly from the verification result, enabling more robust and adaptive recovery behaviors.
    *   **Task 3.2:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationResult` - Introduce a `confidence_score: float = Field(..., ge=0.0, le=1.0)` field to indicate the agent's certainty about the `status` of the verification (e.g., 0.95 for strong success, 0.4 for uncertain failure). This enables the agent to dynamically trigger meta-actions like self-diagnosis, re-observation cycles, or proactive probing (e.g., slight mouse movements to elicit UI reactions) when confidence is below a predefined threshold, especially relevant for `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`.
    *   **Task 3.3:** `src/models/verification.py::VerificationFailureType` - For `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`, consider adding an associated field to `VerificationResult` such as `diagnostic_attempts_count: int = 0` or `probes_performed: list[str]`. This tracks the agent's active efforts to resolve visual ambiguity, allowing for smart escalation or different recovery paths if uncertainty persists after several diagnostic actions.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**
    *   **Task 4.1:** `src/models/verification.py` - Confirm that the interpretation and generation of values for `VerificationFailureType` (e.g., `ACTION_FAILED`, `UNCERTAIN_SCREEN_STATE`) and any imported enums (`FailureCategory`, `LoopStage`, `StopReason`) strictly adhere to Operon's vision-only principle. Specifically, ensure that no underlying DOM/selector-based information or abstract element references are used to derive these states, and all verifications are based purely on visual servo feedback. The current model definition itself is compliant, but continuous enforcement in the agent's implementation is crucial.

## `src\store\background_writer.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference**
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `BackgroundWriter.enqueue`, `BackgroundWriter.append`
        *   **Action**: Refactor the future management in `_pending` to avoid O(N) list operations. The current `list.remove()` in `add_done_callback` runs on the event loop and can block if `_pending` grows large, directly impacting P99 latency.
        *   **Suggestion**: Consider using a `collections.deque` or a `set` for future tracking (if order doesn't matter for `gather`) or implement a periodic sweep (e.g., using `asyncio.create_task` for a background cleanup coroutine) to clean `_pending` more efficiently than per-future `remove()`. Alternatively, if the list is guaranteed to be small, ensure `list.remove` is acceptable overhead.
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `_thread_pool`
        *   **Action**: Evaluate the default `max_workers=2` for the `ThreadPoolExecutor`. If artifact generation is bursty or individual writes are slow, this small pool can lead to a long queue within the executor, increasing P99 latency for writes to *start* processing.
        *   **Suggestion**: Consider increasing `max_workers` based on empirical testing with expected load, or introduce adaptive sizing (see Agentic Features).
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `_append_line` (inner function within `BackgroundWriter.append`)
        *   **Action**: Remove the `fh.flush()` call. For debug artifacts, explicit flushing usually isn't critical for data integrity and can introduce unnecessary disk sync delays, increasing write latency and potentially P99.
        *   **Rationale**: Operating system buffers are generally efficient for batching writes. `flush()` forces immediate write to disk, which is slower.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `_write_file`
        *   **Observation**: `path.write_text(content, encoding="utf-8")` overwrites existing files. For its purpose as an artifact writer (e.g., writing a snapshot of a debug state), this behavior is functionally idempotent in that a subsequent write with the *same content* results in the same file state. If the content changes, the *effect* changes, but the operation itself (overwrite) is consistent. No changes required here as it aligns with artifact snapshotting.
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `_append_line` (inner function within `BackgroundWriter.append`)
        *   **Observation**: Appending content to a file is generally *not* strictly idempotent; repeating the operation adds the content again. This is the expected behavior for logs and trace files. No changes required as this aligns with the typical use case for appending debug information.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines**
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `_thread_pool`, `BackgroundWriter`
        *   **Action**: Implement dynamic scaling of the `_thread_pool` `max_workers` based on real-time system metrics.
        *   **Suggestion**: Monitor the `_thread_pool._work_queue.qsize()` and average task execution time. If the queue length consistently exceeds a threshold, and system resources (CPU, I/O) permit, increment `max_workers` up to a configured limit. Conversely, if the pool is underutilized, scale down. This allows the writer to self-optimize for varying load conditions.
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `BackgroundWriter.enqueue`, `BackgroundWriter.append`
        *   **Action**: Introduce an adaptive backpressure mechanism for artifact generation.
        *   **Suggestion**: If the internal `_thread_pool`'s work queue size exceeds a critical threshold, the `enqueue`/`append` methods could:
            1.  Log a warning indicating overload.
            2.  Optionally return a flag indicating the write was skipped (for non-critical artifacts).
            3.  Provide a mechanism for the main agent loop to detect this backpressure and temporarily reduce the rate of artifact generation.
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, `BackgroundWriter`
        *   **Action**: Implement self-healing capabilities for persistent write failures.
        *   **Suggestion**: Instead of just logging `debug` on exceptions, if a specific path or type of artifact repeatedly fails (e.g., due to permissions or disk full errors after retries), the agent should:
            1.  Transition the affected path to a "quarantined" state, ceasing further write attempts to it for a duration.
            2.  Trigger an alert or more prominent logging (e.g., `error` level) to signal a deeper problem.
            3.  Periodically re-evaluate quarantined paths to see if the underlying issue has resolved.
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, New functionality
        *   **Action**: Add an automated disk space management feature.
        *   **Suggestion**: Implement a background agent that periodically scans artifact directories and deletes older or lower-priority files when total artifact storage exceeds a configured threshold (e.g., 80% of allocated space, or reaching a maximum total size). This prevents disk exhaustion, crucial for long-running agents generating many artifacts.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**
    *   **TASK**: `src\store\background_writer.py`, Entire module
        *   **Observation**: The module is strictly concerned with file I/O and thread management. It does not interact with UI elements, the DOM, selectors, user input, or visual representations.
        *   **Conclusion**: No violations of Operon's invariants (`no DOM/selectors`, `atomic focus+type`, `visual servo`) are present in this module.
