## `src\store\cleanup.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Latency Reduction for Real-time Inference (P99)**
    *   **Task:** Refactor `src\store\cleanup.py::cleanup_old_runs` to process deletions in smaller, configurable batches. This reduces the maximum blocking time for disk I/O, preventing prolonged resource contention that could impact Operon's real-time inference P99 latency.
        *   **Details:** Introduce an optional `batch_size: int = 10` parameter. When `delete` is `True`, iterate through `to_delete` in chunks of `batch_size`, performing `shutil.rmtree` for each batch. Consider adding a small `time.sleep()` between batches if fine-grained throttling is desired.
    *   **Task:** Suggest a design pattern for pre-calculating or caching directory sizes within the `run_dir` metadata. This would significantly reduce the I/O cost of `sum(f.stat().st_size for f in path.rglob("*") if f.is_file())` during cleanup.
        *   **Details:** Propose that the `state.json` file (or a similar metadata file) within each `run_dir` could store the total byte size of that run directory upon completion. Modify `cleanup_old_runs` to attempt to read this cached size first; if unavailable, fall back to the current `rglob` calculation.
    *   **Task:** Add a docstring note or conceptual helper function demonstrating how `src\store\cleanup.py::cleanup_old_runs` should be integrated into Operon's larger system for asynchronous execution to offload I/O from the main inference loop.
        *   **Details:** Describe how Operon would ideally execute this cleanup function in a separate, low-priority thread, process, or via an asynchronous job queue, ensuring it does not block critical real-time operations.

2.  **Structural Idempotency**
    *   **Task:** Add a docstring note to `src\store\cleanup.py::cleanup_old_runs` explicitly stating its idempotency.
        *   **Details:** Clarify that running the function multiple times with the same `root_dir` and `keep_days` parameters will consistently identify the same set of directories for deletion and that subsequent deletion attempts on already removed directories will have no further effect, maintaining a stable system state.
    *   **Task:** Enhance the robustness of `src\store\cleanup.py::cleanup_old_runs`'s size calculation against external file system changes.
        *   **Details:** Modify the `sum(f.stat().st_size ...)` loop to wrap `f.stat().st_size` in a `try-except FileNotFoundError` block. This ensures that if a file or sub-directory is removed by an external process between the initial `iterdir()` scan and the size calculation, the cleanup process does not crash and instead gracefully skips the non-existent file, contributing 0 to its size.

3.  **Agentic Features**
    *   **Task:** Propose an adaptive `keep_days` mechanism for `src\store\cleanup.py` when integrated into Operon's core agent.
        *   **Details:** Add a comment or conceptual code snippet demonstrating how Operon, as an agent, could dynamically determine the `keep_days` parameter for `cleanup_old_runs` based on real-time system metrics (e.g., current disk free space percentage, predicted storage needs, or historical run access patterns). For instance, if disk space falls below a critical threshold (e.g., 10% free), `keep_days` could be automatically reduced from 7 to 3 to free up space proactively.
    *   **Task:** Suggest integration points for `src\store\cleanup.py` with Operon's self-healing and monitoring capabilities.
        *   **Details:** Modify `cleanup_old_runs` to accept an optional `reporter: Callable[[str, str], None]` callback. This callback could be invoked after cleanup actions (e.g., `reporter("Cleaned X GB", "INFO")`, `reporter("Disk space critical", "ALERT")`) to feed information directly into Operon's internal monitoring system, enabling automated alerts or triggering further self-healing actions (e.g., suspending new run creation, notifying an operator).
    *   **Task:** Advise on incorporating resource-awareness into the cleanup process to avoid contention with Operon's active inference.
        *   **Details:** Add a note or an optional parameter (e.g., `is_inference_active: Callable[[], bool]`) to `cleanup_old_runs`. The cleanup function could periodically invoke this callback. If `is_inference_active()` returns `True`, the cleanup process could throttle its disk I/O (e.g., by increasing `time.sleep()` between batches) or temporarily pause, deferring resource-intensive operations until Operon's primary inference load subsides.

4.  **Operon Invariants Compliance**
    *   **Task:** Add a formal statement to `src\store\cleanup.py` confirming its adherence to Operon's core invariants.
        *   **Details:** Place a comment at the top of the module, beneath the existing docstring, stating: "This backend utility script operates purely on the filesystem and does not interact with visual components (e.g., DOM/selectors), user input mechanisms (e.g., atomic focus+type), or visual servoing. As such, it fully complies with Operon's core invariants."

## `src\store\memory.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore.get_hints`
    *   **Action:** Implement an in-memory index for `_cached_records` based on `benchmark`, `page_hint`, `subgoal`, and `failure_category`.
    *   **Reasoning:** The current approach of iterating through all records for filtering and scoring can lead to high P99 latency as `memory.jsonl` grows. An indexed structure (e.g., a dictionary mapping tuples of query parameters to lists of relevant records) will significantly speed up retrieval for real-time inference.
    *   **Pattern:** Indexed Data Structures / Pre-computation.

2.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore._load_records`, `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore._load_episodes`
    *   **Action:** Introduce a background loading mechanism for `memory.jsonl` and `episodes.jsonl` to warm caches.
    *   **Reasoning:** Cache invalidation or initial loading of large JSONL files are blocking operations that can spike P99 latency. Asynchronous loading in a background thread or process can ensure the main inference path always has a fresh or nearly fresh cache available without blocking.
    *   **Pattern:** Asynchronous Loading / Cache Warming.

3.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore.get_episode`
    *   **Action:** After `_load_episodes` populates `_cached_episodes`, also store episodes in an in-memory dictionary keyed by `(episode.normalized_intent, episode.benchmark)` for O(1) exact lookups.
    *   **Reasoning:** Iterating through a list for episode retrieval becomes slow with many episodes. A dictionary allows direct access, reducing P99 latency for this frequently used inference path.
    *   **Pattern:** In-Memory Indexing.

4.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore._write_episodes`
    *   **Action:** Refactor `_write_episodes` to implement atomic file replacement. This involves writing to a temporary file and then atomically renaming/moving it to replace the original `episodes.jsonl`.
    *   **Reasoning:** Overwriting the entire file synchronously is not robust; a crash during the write operation can lead to a corrupted or incomplete `episodes.jsonl`, resulting in data loss. Atomic replacement ensures either the old, valid file or the new, complete file is present.
    *   **Idempotency:** Ensures that despite potential mid-write failures, the file system state remains consistent and eventually converges to the desired content.

5.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore._decay_active_hints`
    *   **Action:** Add a mechanism to uniquely identify a "failure event" (e.g., using a `step_id` or a short-lived cache of recent failure contexts) to prevent redundant decay records for the same logical failure.
    *   **Reasoning:** If a higher-level workflow retries a step that repeatedly fails (and thus triggers `record_step` multiple times for the "same" failure), `_decay_active_hints` would append multiple decay records, potentially over-punishing valid hints. Decay should be an idempotent operation per distinct failure observation.
    *   **Idempotency:** Ensures that a specific failure event causes a hint's weight to decay only once, regardless of how many times `_decay_active_hints` might be invoked for that same event.

6.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore` (new method needed)
    *   **Action:** Implement a `_compact_memory_records()` method that periodically rewrites `memory.jsonl`, removing records below `_WEIGHT_PRUNE_THRESHOLD` or those beyond a certain age.
    *   **Reasoning:** `memory.jsonl` is append-only, leading to unbounded growth. This accumulates outdated or low-value records, increasing disk I/O and memory usage for `_load_records`. Periodic compaction acts as a "forgetting" mechanism.
    *   **Agentic Feature:** Self-managing memory / Proactive resource management. This is beyond standard workflow engines that typically don't prune their own history.
    *   **Pattern:** Offline Processing / Data Lifecycle Management.

7.  **Task:** `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore.record_step`, `src/models/memory.py::MemoryRecord` (and associated data models)
    *   **Action:** Enhance `MemoryRecord` to capture whether a `RecoveryDecision` following a `VerificationStatus.FAILURE` was successful in resolving the issue. Implement logic in `record_step` to create specific `MemoryRecord`s (e.g., `RecoveryHint`s) that map observed `FailureCategory` to effective `RecoveryDecision`s.
    *   **Reasoning:** The agent currently records `RecoveryDecision` but doesn't explicitly learn which recoveries *work* for which failures. This allows the memory to proactively suggest tested recovery strategies.
    *   **Agentic Feature:** Proactive self-healing / Learning from recovery. The agent can dynamically generate and prioritize recovery hints based on its past successes, moving beyond pre-defined recovery paths.

8.  **Task:** `src/models/perception.py::UIElement`, `src/models/policy.py::PolicyAction` (and transitive impact on `src/store/memory.py`)
    *   **Action:** Explicitly document the origin and guarantees of `element_id`. Confirm that `element_id` is *strictly* derived from visual information (e.g., bounding box, OCR text hash, visual features) and is *never* influenced by DOM attributes, XPath, or CSS selectors. If it is DOM-derived, redesign element identification across the system.
    *   **Reasoning:** Operon's "no DOM/selectors" invariant is critical. The `memory.py` module heavily relies on `element_id` for contextualizing hints and actions. Any DOM-derived `element_id` would fundamentally violate this core invariant.
    *   **Flag:** **Violation of "no DOM/selectors" invariant IF `element_id` is derived from DOM attributes.** The current module relies on this ID without defining its origin. This must be confirmed and, if necessary, corrected upstream.

9.  **Task:** `src/models/policy.py::ActionType`, `src/store/memory.py::FileBackedMemoryStore._build_step_records` (and all places handling `CLICK` and `TYPE` actions)
    *   **Action:** Redesign `ActionType` to include an `ActionType.FOCUS_AND_TYPE` (or similar atomic equivalent). All agent policy and execution logic must be updated to use this single atomic action for input, replacing separate `CLICK` and `TYPE` actions when targeting an input field. Update memory records and hints (`click_before_type`, `avoid_identical_type_retry`) to reflect this atomic action.
    *   **Reasoning:** Operon's "atomic focus+type" invariant means that these operations must be an indivisible action from the agent's perspective. The current memory records and generated hints (`click_before_type`, `avoid_identical_type_retry`) explicitly describe `CLICK` and `TYPE` as sequential, separate actions, directly contradicting this invariant. This implies a fundamental mismatch in the agent's action model.
    *   **Flag:** **Violation of "atomic focus+type" invariant.** The module's recording of `ActionType.CLICK` and `ActionType.TYPE` as distinct events, and its hints suggesting a sequence of these actions, directly contradict the stated invariant. This requires a re-evaluation of the agent's core action primitives.

## `src\store\replay.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 latency for real-time inference (via optimized data access):**
    *   **Task 1.1: Optimize `load_run_replay` for large files.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py`
        *   **Function:** `load_run_replay`
        *   **Action:** Modify `load_run_replay` to read `run.jsonl` line-by-line using `with log_path.open(...) as f: for line in f:`, instead of `read_text().splitlines()`. This reduces memory pressure and improves startup latency for very large log files, which is critical if this data feed were ever adapted for near-real-time analytics or online learning.
        *   **Reasoning:** `read_text().splitlines()` loads the entire file into memory, which can cause significant latency and memory spikes for large log files, impacting P99 if this function were ever called in a latency-sensitive context.

2.  **Identify opportunities for structural idempotency (via caching for performance):**
    *   **Task 2.1: Implement caching for `load_run_replay`.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py`
        *   **Function:** `load_run_replay`
        *   **Action:** Decorate `load_run_replay` with `functools.lru_cache` to cache results based on `run_id` and `root_dir`. This makes repeated calls to load the same replay idempotent in terms of computational effort and I/O. Consider a reasonable `maxsize` (e.g., `maxsize=32` or `64`) and `ttl` (if cache invalidation is desired in a dynamic environment, otherwise `lru_cache` alone is sufficient for static file reads).
        *   **Reasoning:** Loading and parsing run logs can be resource-intensive. If the same `run_id` is queried multiple times (e.g., by different CLI invocations in a script, or if integrated into a dashboard service), caching the parsed `RunLogEntry` list will reduce P99 latency for subsequent requests by avoiding redundant file I/O and parsing.

3.  **Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines (leveraging replay data):**
    *   **Task 3.1: Enable automated failure analysis and adaptive recovery learning.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py` (and related `src/models/logs.py`)
        *   **Function:** N/A (conceptual feature, leveraging `load_run_replay` data)
        *   **Action:** Propose a new module/service that consumes `RunLogEntry` data via `load_run_replay`. This service would analyze `entry.failure` (category, stop_reason), `entry.recovery_decision` (strategy, message, stop_reason), and `entry.verification_result` (status, reason) across many runs. The goal is to:
            *   Identify common failure modes.
            *   Correlate specific failures with successful/unsuccessful recovery strategies.
            *   Use this historical data to train a meta-policy that can predict failures earlier or select optimal recovery strategies for the live agent, thereby enabling self-healing behaviors beyond simple retries.
        *   **Reasoning:** The rich failure, verification, and recovery logs are invaluable for improving agent robustness. Automated analysis allows Operon to learn from its past mistakes and adapt its operational policies.

    *   **Task 3.2: Implement proactive progress monitoring and loop detection for live agents.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py` (and related `src/models/logs.py`)
        *   **Function:** N/A (conceptual feature, leveraging `load_run_replay` data)
        *   **Action:** Propose extending the `RunLogEntry` stream (not just static `run.jsonl`) to feed into a live monitoring component. This component would track `entry.progress_state.no_progress_streak` and `entry.progress_state.loop_detected` in real-time, comparing against historical thresholds derived from successful runs (loaded via `load_run_replay`). If a live agent's progress state deviates significantly or approaches a known problematic pattern, the monitoring component could trigger early intervention (e.g., a pre-emptive recovery action, a human alert, or a policy adjustment), preventing prolonged unproductive loops.
        *   **Reasoning:** Leveraging historical `progress_state` data for real-time comparison allows the agent to be more anticipatory and proactive in managing its task execution, moving beyond reactive error handling.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants:**
    *   **Task 4.1: Eliminate `perception_selector_trace` fields.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py` (display logic) and implicitly `src\models\logs.py` (data model)
        *   **Function:** `render_run_replay`
        *   **Action:** Remove the display of `entry.perception_debug.selector_trace_artifact_path`. More critically, trace this field back to its origin in `src\models\logs.py` and remove it from the `PerceptionDebugLog` model (and any data generation/storage logic).
        *   **Violation:** **DIRECT VIOLATION** of the `no DOM/selectors` invariant. Operon is "vision-only, zero-abstraction." The very existence of a "selector trace" implies that a selector mechanism (e.g., XPath, CSS selectors) is being used or generated somewhere in the system, even if only for debugging or internal representation. This is fundamentally against Operon's core principle.

    *   **Task 4.2: Eliminate `policy_selector_trace` fields.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\replay.py` (display logic) and implicitly `src\models\logs.py` (data model)
        *   **Function:** `render_run_replay`
        *   **Action:** Remove the display of `entry.policy_debug.selector_trace_artifact_path`. More critically, trace this field back to its origin in `src\models\logs.py` and remove it from the `PolicyDebugLog` model (and any data generation/storage logic).
        *   **Violation:** **DIRECT VIOLATION** of the `no DOM/selectors` invariant. Similar to `perception_selector_trace`, its presence indicates a breach of Operon's architectural integrity. The policy module should operate solely on visual perceptions and internal state, not selector-based abstractions.

## `src\store\run_logger.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Suggest patterns that reduce P99 latency for real-time inference.**
    *   **Task:** Evaluate the `src/store/background_writer.py` module to ensure it implements highly efficient batching and asynchronous flushing strategies. Verify that `bg_writer` doesn't incur significant overhead per append call (e.g., by ensuring it uses a thread-safe queue for buffered writes that are only flushed to disk periodically or when a certain buffer size is reached).
    *   **Task:** Refactor `src/store/run_logger.py::append_step_log_critical` to replace its synchronous disk write and immediate `fh.flush()` with a dedicated, ultra-low-latency, non-blocking asynchronous mechanism. This could involve a separate, high-priority in-memory ring buffer with a single dedicated writer thread, or leveraging operating system features for low-latency writes (e.g., `io_uring` on Linux, if applicable), ensuring the critical path of the agent is never blocked.
    *   **Task:** Implement optional, configurable compression for `RunLogEntry` data within `src/store/run_logger.py` before passing it to `bg_writer.append`. This can significantly reduce disk I/O volume for verbose logs, leading to overall lower latency provided the compression/decompression overhead is minimal compared to I/O savings.

2.  **Identify opportunities for structural idempotency.**
    *   **Task:** Review the `RunLogEntry` schema (defined in `src/models/logs.py`) to ensure it includes a robust, globally unique identifier (e.g., a UUID or a composite ID of run_id + step_id + event_sequence_num) for each log entry. This allows external log consumers or analysis tools to robustly identify and de-duplicate log events even if multiple `append_step_log` calls occur for the same logical event due to retries or fault tolerance mechanisms.
    *   **Task:** Introduce a dedicated function, `src/store/run_logger.py::write_run_summary(run_id: str, summary_data: dict) -> None`, that writes or overwrites a final summary file for a given `run_id`. This function would be idempotent, allowing it to be called multiple times without side effects beyond updating the latest summary, providing an idempotent way to store the final state or outcome of an Operon run.

3.  **Suggest agentic features (e.g., self-healing workflows) not present in standard workflow engines.**
    *   **Task:** Implement an adaptive logging policy where the Operon agent can dynamically adjust the verbosity, detail, or target output of `src/store/run_logger.py` calls based on its internal state, observed performance, or detected anomalies. For example, increasing detail for `perception_low_quality` events, or decreasing verbosity during periods of stable, high-performance operation. This requires `append_step_log` to consult a runtime agent configuration.
    *   **Task:** Develop a direct, agentic self-healing trigger mechanism. Instead of merely logging `terminal_failure` or `perception_low_quality` using `src/store/run_logger.py::append_step_log_critical`, these events should immediately publish to an internal agent message bus. A dedicated agent component should subscribe to these critical signals and trigger predefined recovery workflows (e.g., re-attempting a perception step, resetting a sub-module, or executing a fallback strategy) in real-time.
    *   **Task:** Introduce a "logging quality feedback loop." The Operon agent should periodically (or on demand) analyze its own historical `RunLogEntry` data (from logs written by `src/store/run_logger.py`) to identify patterns where log information was insufficient for root cause analysis or where certain log types are too noisy. The agent could then autonomously suggest or even implement modifications to its logging points or `RunLogEntry` schema.

4.  **Flag any violations of Operon's invariants: no DOM/selectors, atomic focus+type, visual servo.**
    *   **Violation Flagged:** `src/store/run_logger.py::append_step_log_critical` violates the spirit of Operon's real-time, zero-abstraction invariants, particularly "atomic focus+type" and "visual servo." The use of synchronous disk I/O and immediate `fh.flush()` introduces unpredictable blocking latency into the agent's execution path. While intended for critical signals, blocking on disk I/O directly conflicts with the need for operations to be immediate and non-interfering, potentially compromising the atomic nature of core agent interactions and the responsiveness of visual servo loops. This function must be refactored as per Task 1.2 to be entirely non-blocking from the perspective of the calling agent thread.

## `src\store\run_store.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference:**
    *   **Task 1.1: Optimize `create_run` for initial state persistence.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.create_run`
        *   **Action:** Evaluate the absolute necessity of `_write_state_sync` for the "observable immediately" requirement.
            *   **Option A (Recommended for lowest latency):** Replace `_write_state_sync` with an immediate enqueue to a dedicated, high-priority queue within `bg_writer` that guarantees flush within a very tight SLA, or introduce a fast, in-memory ephemeral store for new runs that the `/observer/api/run/{run_id}` can query before background persistence. This would make `create_run` non-blocking and significantly reduce its P99 latency.
            *   **Option B (If strict sync is critical):** Explore a more performant synchronous persistence mechanism if disk write is truly unavoidable (e.g., memory-mapped files or a lightweight key-value store optimized for synchronous writes).
    *   **Task 1.2: Enhance caching strategy for `get_run` to minimize disk I/O.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.get_run`
        *   **Action:** Implement a more robust and possibly persistent in-memory cache (e.g., using an LRU cache with a maximum size, or consider integrating with an external, fast K/V store like Redis if `_runs` grows too large for process memory) to serve `AgentState` objects, reducing reliance on disk reads for frequently accessed runs.
    *   **Task 1.3: Evaluate serialization format for performance.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore._write_state`, `FileBackedRunStore._write_state_sync`, `FileBackedRunStore.get_run`
        *   **Action:** Investigate alternative serialization formats (e.g., MsgPack, Protocol Buffers, or even a custom binary format) for `AgentState` instead of JSON, particularly for the `_write_state` path, to reduce CPU overhead during serialization/deserialization, especially for large `AgentState` objects. Profile `model_dump_json()` and `model_validate_json()` to quantify CPU cost.

2.  **Identify Opportunities for Structural Idempotency:**
    *   **Task 2.1: Make `update_state` idempotent for history appending.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.update_state`
        *   **Action:** Modify `update_state` to ensure that appending `perception` to `observation_history` (and similarly for `action_history` and `verification_history` in `AgentState`) is idempotent. This could involve:
            *   Adding a unique identifier to `ScreenPerception` (and related history models) and checking if an entry with that ID already exists before appending.
            *   Alternatively, use the `step_count` as a key: if the incoming `perception` corresponds to an already recorded `step_count`, overwrite or ensure consistency, rather than blindly appending.
    *   **Task 2.2: Define idempotency guarantees for `set_status` transitions.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.set_status`
        *   **Action:** Clarify expected behavior for `set_status` if called multiple times or out of order. While setting the same status is idempotent, ensure the workflow can handle retries or out-of-order calls where a non-terminal status might be set after a terminal one (e.g., `SUCCEEDED` then `RUNNING`). If this is an issue, add logic to prevent backward transitions or only allow specific forward transitions.

3.  **Suggest Agentic Features Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines:**
    *   **Task 3.1: Implement robust state recovery from full history.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.get_run`
        *   **Action:** Enhance `get_run` to check for `run.jsonl` (full history log) if `state.json` is missing or corrupted. In such cases, the agent should be able to reconstruct `AgentState` by replaying the `run.jsonl` entries up to the last known valid state, ensuring resilience against partial state file corruption.
    *   **Task 3.2: Introduce pluggable anomaly detection hooks.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.update_state`
        *   **Action:** Add a mechanism (e.g., a list of registered callback functions or a dedicated agentic service interface) that can be invoked after `AgentState` is updated in `update_state`. These hooks could analyze the `observation_history`, `action_history`, or other state changes for patterns indicative of anomalies (e.g., loops, stalled progress, unexpected visual changes) and trigger agent-level responses.
    *   **Task 3.3: Provide an agent-controlled synchronous flush mechanism.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Action:** Add a new public method `FileBackedRunStore.flush_state_sync(run_id: str)` that allows the Operon agent to explicitly request an immediate, synchronous write of the current `AgentState` to disk for a given `run_id`. This enables the agent to establish critical checkpoints before complex operations or potential failure points, overriding the default background writing behavior when necessary for stronger consistency guarantees.
    *   **Task 3.4: Automate contextual environment logging.**
        *   **File:** `src\store\run_store.py`
        *   **Function:** `FileBackedRunStore.create_run`
        *   **Action:** Expand `AgentState` to include fields for environmental context (e.g., OS version, Python version, relevant system configurations, network conditions, perceived application version if extractable) and automatically populate these fields during `create_run`. This metadata is crucial for debugging, reproducibility, and understanding run failures in a zero-abstraction environment.

4.  **Flag Violations of Operon's Invariants:**
    *   **No Violations Identified within this Module:** The `run_store.py` module itself deals with the persistence of data models (`AgentState`, `ScreenPerception`, etc.) and does not directly interact with web pages, perform actions, or interpret visual information. Therefore, it does not directly violate "no DOM/selectors," "atomic focus+type," or "visual servo."
    *   **Dependency on Model Adherence:** The adherence to Operon's invariants depends critically on the *definitions* of `src.models.perception.ScreenPerception` and the models used within `AgentState` (e.g., for `action_history`, `verification_history`). As long as these models encapsulate raw visual data and low-level, atomic interactions rather than DOM structures or high-level UI abstractions, this persistence layer remains compliant.

## `src\store\summary.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1. Patterns to Reduce P99 Latency for Real-time Inference (Summary Generation)**

The module is primarily for post-run summarization, not real-time agent inference. However, if summaries are needed quickly (e.g., for rapid feedback loops, CI/CD benchmarks), reducing latency in generating them is important. The main bottlenecks are extensive file I/O and subsequent data processing.

*   **Task 1.1: Implement Asynchronous File I/O for Batch Loading.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py`
    *   **Functions**: `_load_states`, `_load_steps_for_state`, `_retry_log_attempts`, `_load_selector_traces`
    *   **Action**: Refactor these functions to use `asyncio` and `aiofiles` (or similar async I/O library) for concurrent reading of multiple run states, step logs, retry logs, and selector traces, especially when `summarize_runs` is called with a directory target. This will significantly reduce the wall-clock time for I/O-bound operations across many runs.
    *   **Note**: This would require changing `summarize_runs` and potentially `generate_run_metrics` to be `async` as well.

*   **Task 1.2: Consider Parallel Processing for `generate_run_metrics`.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py`
    *   **Function**: `summarize_runs` (specifically the line `run_metrics = [generate_run_metrics(state.run_id, root_dir=root_dir) for state in states]`)
    *   **Action**: For large numbers of `states` (i.e., when summarizing many runs in a directory), evaluate using `multiprocessing.Pool` or `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` to parallelize calls to `generate_run_metrics`. This computation is CPU-bound after data loading, and parallelization can leverage multiple cores. Profile to determine if `ThreadPoolExecutor` (better for I/O-bound tasks that release GIL) or `ProcessPoolExecutor` (better for CPU-bound tasks) is more suitable given the async I/O changes.

*   **Task 1.3: Optimize Data Loading and Deserialization within `_load_states` and related functions.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py`
    *   **Functions**: `_load_state_from_path`, `_load_steps_for_state`, `_load_selector_traces`
    *   **Action**: For very high-frequency summary generation (e.g., on-demand analysis of recently completed runs), explore using a faster JSON deserializer if `json.loads` becomes a bottleneck. Also, if the same artifact files (e.g., `state.json`, `replay.json`) are accessed multiple times by different processes or threads within a short window, consider a shared in-memory cache (e.g., `functools.lru_cache` or a more sophisticated distributed cache if applicable).

**2. Opportunities for Structural Idempotency**

The module already exhibits good structural idempotency:

*   **Task 2.1: Confirm and Document Existing Idempotency.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py`
    *   **Functions**: `write_run_metrics`, `write_suite_summary`
    *   **Action**: Add docstrings or comments explicitly stating that these functions are idempotent. The use of `path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)` and `path.write_text` (which overwrites existing files) ensures that calling these functions multiple times with the same inputs will produce the same outcome on disk without errors or side effects beyond the initial write.
    *   **Reasoning**: All `generate_*` and `_load_*` functions are pure computations or read-only operations, inherently idempotent.

**3. Agentic Features (e.g., self-healing workflows) Not Present in Standard Workflow Engines**

This module provides critical metrics that can inform advanced agentic behaviors, extending beyond typical workflow orchestration.

*   **Task 3.1: Implement Adaptive Policy Adjustment based on `RunMetrics`.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py` (provides data), `src/agent/policy.py` (would consume data)
    *   **Action**: Develop a meta-agent or a policy evaluation component that consumes `RunMetrics` (especially `failure_category`, `loop_detected`, `no_progress_events`, `stale_target_events`, `average_selector_margin`).
        *   **Example 1: Self-Correction**: If `FailureCategory.STALE_TARGET_BEFORE_ACTION` is frequently observed for a specific `page_url` or `task_type`, the agent's policy could dynamically adjust its visual perception frequency, increase target re-verification steps, or apply a different "visual servo" strategy for that context in subsequent runs.
        *   **Example 2: Dynamic Resource Allocation**: If `perception_retry_count` is consistently high for certain tasks, suggesting visual ambiguity, the agent could dynamically request more computational resources for visual processing (e.g., higher resolution input, more robust perception models) on future attempts for similar tasks.
        *   **Example 3: Behavioral Adaptation**: If `loop_detected` or `no_progress_events` are high, the agent could trigger a more aggressive exploration strategy, reset its internal state, or seek human intervention/feedback.

*   **Task 3.2: Develop Proactive Anomaly Detection and Automated Experimentation.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py` (generates `BenchmarkSuiteSummary`)
    *   **Action**: Create a monitoring service that regularly runs `generate_suite_summary` for recent runs.
        *   **Anomaly Detection**: Set thresholds for metrics like `overall_success_rate`, `average_step_count`, `loop_detected_frequency`, or specific `failure_breakdown_by_failure_category`. If these metrics deviate significantly from baselines (e.g., using statistical process control), trigger automated alerts, rollback mechanisms, or initiate a diagnostic run.
        *   **Automated A/B Testing**: Integrate `generate_suite_summary` into an automated experimentation platform. When deploying new agent policy versions or perception models, automatically run benchmark suites, compare `BenchmarkSuiteSummary` outputs, and promote versions with superior `overall_success_rate` or lower average `retry_counts` without manual intervention.

*   **Task 3.3: Implement Context-Aware Self-Healing via Task Re-routing.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py` (provides summary metrics)
    *   **Action**: Based on `BenchmarkSuiteSummary` or `RunMetrics`, if a specific Operon instance or model struggles consistently with certain `task_type`s or `tag`s (e.g., high `failure_breakdown_by_failure_category` for "complex forms"), the system could automatically re-route such tasks to specialized Operon configurations/models known to perform better in those contexts. This creates a self-healing system at a higher orchestration level.

**4. Violations of Operon's Invariants**

*   **Task 4.1: Clarify Interpretation of "no DOM/selectors" invariant concerning `SelectorTrace`.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py` (uses `src.models.selector.SelectorTrace`)
    *   **Functions**: `generate_run_metrics`, `_load_selector_traces`
    *   **Flag**: **Potential Violation / Requires Clarification.**
    *   **Reasoning**: Operon's invariant is "no DOM/selectors" for its operation. This module *processes* `SelectorTrace` objects, which contain `total_score`, `score_margin`, `final_decision`, and `rejection_reason` related to selection. The critical question is whether `src.models.selector.SelectorTrace` (and its source in the agent's policy) is *derived from* or *implicitly relies on* DOM structure, or if it purely represents scores from a visual perception/selection system that has no knowledge of DOM.
        *   If `SelectorTrace` refers to the output of a *vision-only* selection mechanism (e.g., scoring bounding boxes based on visual features), then this module's use of it for summarization is *not* a violation. It measures the performance of the visual selector.
        *   If `SelectorTrace` contains or is generated by any process that directly accesses, parses, or is even aware of the underlying DOM structure (e.g., using XPath, CSS selectors, or a representation derived from the DOM), then its very existence as an artifact of the agent's operation would indicate a violation of the "zero-abstraction" and "no DOM/selectors" invariant.
    *   **Action**: Review `src/models/selector.py` and the code generating `SelectorTrace` to confirm it strictly adheres to vision-only principles without any DOM-based interaction or information. If it relies on DOM in any way, the *source* of these traces (not this summary module) needs re-architecting. Assuming the `SelectorTrace` model itself is vision-based, this module correctly summarizes its performance without violating the invariant.

*   **Task 4.2: Confirm `atomic focus+type` and `visual servo` are measured, not violated.**
    *   **File**: `src/store/summary.py`
    *   **Functions**: `generate_run_metrics`
    *   **Flag**: **No Violation.**
    *   **Reasoning**: The module reports `focus_failures`, `perception_retry_count`, and `stale_target_events`. These are *metrics* that measure the agent's performance and adherence to the `atomic focus+type` and `visual servo` principles. They indicate when the agent *failed* to uphold these behaviors or required retries, rather than violating the invariants themselves by using forbidden mechanisms. The module serves to audit the agent's behavior against these invariants.

## `src\tools\file_porter.py`

_Generated by Gemini architectural review pipeline._

---

1.  **Task:** Implement streaming download and upload to reduce P99 latency.
    *   **Description:** The current implementation downloads the entire file into memory (`resp.content`) before initiating the upload. For large files, this sequential blocking I/O significantly increases P99 latency. Switch to streaming the download directly to the Google Drive upload, leveraging `requests.Response.iter_content()` and `googleapiclient.http.MediaIoBaseUpload`. This reduces memory pressure and allows download and upload to overlap, improving real-time responsiveness.
    *   **File:** `src\tools\file_porter.py`
    *   **Function:** `run_porter`

2.  **Task:** Introduce structural idempotency for Drive uploads by checking for existing files.
    *   **Description:** Before uploading a new file, query the Drive API (`files.list`) to check if a file with the same `filename` already exists in the target `folder_id`. If it exists, return the ID of the existing file instead of creating a duplicate. This prevents multiple identical files from being created upon retry and ensures a consistent state, crucial for agent reliability.
    *   **File:** `src\tools\file_porter.py`
    *   **Function:** `run_porter`

3.  **Task:** Implement robust, agentic retry mechanisms for network operations.
    *   **Description:** Add a retry decorator (e.g., `tenacity` or a custom implementation with exponential backoff) to both the `requests.get` download and the `service.files().create` upload operations. This introduces self-healing capabilities, allowing the agent to gracefully recover from transient network issues without immediate failure, significantly reducing P99 latency caused by re-executing from scratch after a transient fault.
    *   **File:** `src\tools\file_porter.py`
    *   **Function:** `run_porter`

4.  **Task:** Implement an agentic mechanism for dynamic filename conflict resolution.
    *   **Description:** Building on the file existence check (Task 2), introduce a configurable policy for handling filename conflicts (e.g., `overwrite`, `rename_unique`, `return_existing_id`, `fail`). The agent could default to `return_existing_id` for idempotency, but allow override for specific use cases. This provides a higher degree of self-healing and adaptability compared to fixed behavior.
    *   **File:** `src\tools\file_porter.py`
    *   **Function:** `run_porter`

5.  **Task:** Refactor `_build_drive_service` for potential shared/cached instance.
    *   **Description:** While `google.auth` might internally cache credentials, the `build` call could still incur overhead if called frequently. For Operon's real-time needs, explore if the `drive` service object can be lazily initialized once per process or worker and reused, rather than rebuilding it on every `run_porter` call. This reduces startup latency for subsequent uses.
    *   **File:** `src\tools\file_porter.py`
    *   **Function:** `_build_drive_service` and `run_porter`

6.  **Task:** Review and confirm Operon invariant adherence.
    *   **Description:** Confirm that `src\tools\file_porter.py` does not interact with the DOM, use selectors, perform atomic focus+type operations, or utilize visual servoing techniques.
